For this re-published version, the prior versions of the IPR Policy will apply, except that the
previous requirement for Adopters (as defined in the earlier IPR Policy) to agree to an O-RAN
Adopter License Agreement to access and use Final Specifications shall no longer apply or be
required for these Final Specifications after 1st July 2022.
The copying or incorporation into any other work of part or all of the material available in this
specification in any form without the prior written permission of O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.  is
prohibited, save that you may print or download extracts of the material on this site for your
personal use, or copy the material on this site for the purpose of sending to individual third
parties for their information provided that you acknowledge O-RAN ALLIANCE as the source of
the material and that you inform the third party that these conditions apply to them and that they
must comply with them.

1 Introductory Material 1
1.1 Foreword 2
This Technical Specification has been produced by the O-RAN Alliance. 3
The contents of the present document are subject to continuing work within O-RAN and may change following formal 4
O-RAN approval. Should the O-RAN Alliance modify the contents of the present document, it will be re-released by O-5
RAN with an identifying change of release date and an increase in version number as follows: 6
Release x.y.z 7
where: 8
x the first digit is incremented for all changes of substance, i.e. technical enhancements, corrections, updates, 9
etc. (the initial approved document will have x=01). 10
y the second digit is incremented when editorial only changes have been incorporated in the document. 11
z the third digit included only in working versions of the document indicating incremental changes during the 12
editing process. 13
1.2 Scope 14
1.2.1 General 15
The present document defines tests that validate the conformance to the protocols defined in [2] for the Lower Layer 16
Split Option 7.2x interface between the O-RU and the O-DU.  A guiding principle for these conformance tests is to use 17
only standard interfaces that are defined by the specification [2] or relevant 3GPP specifications.  The construction of 18
these tests avoids the requirement for a device to include any special interfaces used solely for the purpose of these 19
tests. 20
While these tests are not written to evaluate the performance of an O-DU or O-RU device, some tests require obtaining 21
measurements and evaluating the success or failure of the device to process sample data correctly based on portion of 22
the protocol being tested at the time.     23
In general, unless otherwise stated, the tests cover LTE (Stand-Alone), NR Non-Stand-Alone (NSA) and NR Stand-24
Alone (SA).  25
1.2.2 U-Plane and C-Plane Scope 26
This version of the Conformance Test specification defines tests which validate the conformance of an O-RU.  The tests 27
are designed to cover a large number of optional functionalities defined in [2].  Therefore, for any given O-RU 28
implementation, a subset of these tests may not be applicable.  It is the responsibility of the tester to understand the 29
applicability of each test to the feature provided by a particular O-RU.    30
Future versions of this specification may add tests which validate the conformance of the O-DU to the U-Plane and C-31
Plane and may expand on other areas not currently addressed in this version. 32
1.2.3 S-Plane  33
This version of the Conformance Test specification defines tests for time synchronization of the O-RU and O-DU.  The 34
tests defined in this version include both functional and performance tests.  Functional tests validate the ability of the O-35
RU and O-DU to achieve the proper synchronization management state based on a variety of PTP, and optionally 36
SyncE input conditions.  Performance tests validate the conformance of the recovered clock for the O-DU or O-RU.   37
Concerning the scope of the S-Plane, various synchronization options have been defined in the ORAN CUS 38
Specification [2] for distributing synchronization to the O-RU (LLS-C1, LLS-C2, LLS-C3 and LLS-C4). Depending on 39
the specific ORAN deployment being considered not all of them may be relevant. When testing the S-Plane, the tester 40
shall identify which of the test cases are relevant depending on the specific deployment scenarios addressed. As a 41
general guideline the following applies: 42

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       9
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
1) Direct connection between O-DU and O-RU:  1
 LLS-C1 is generally the main sync option to be validated.  2
 LLS-C4 may be considered as alternative or as a complement to C1 3
2) Synchronization network between O-DU and O-RU 4
 LLS-C2 for cases where the synchronization is delivered to the O-RU via the O-DU and over the bridged 5
network. In this topology the PRTC synchronizing the O-DU may be local or remote.  6
 LLS-C3 for cases when the synchronization is distributed to the O-RU without involving the O-DU. In 7
this case one or more PRTC may be remote and may also be local. 8
 LLS-C4 may be considered as alternative or as a complement to LLS-C2/C3 9
For LLS-C1 and LLS-C2, a local PRTC is either embedded in or co-located with the O-DU. A remote PRTC is 10
located anywhere in the network (backhaul or fronthaul).    11
 12
 13

CONDITIONAL MANDATORY.  Note that tests that are REQUIRED are for those functions of the DUT that by 16
specification are required to be supported.  Optional functionality in a DUT implies that the corresponding conformance 17
test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY and is mandatory only if the DUT supports the optional functionality.  18

1.3.1 Definitions 27
For the purposes of the present document, the terms and definitions given in 3GPP TR 21.905, “Vocabulary for 3GPP 28
Specifications”[1]and the following apply. A term defined in the present document takes precedence over the definition 29
of the same term, if any, in [1] 30
C-Plane Control Plane: refers specifically to real-time control between O-DU and O-RU, and should not be 31
confused with the UE’s control plane 32
DL DownLink: data flow towards the radiating antenna 33
eNB eNodeB (applies to LTE) <E-UTRAN NodeB / Evolved NodeB> 34
EVM Error Vector Magnitude – see section 6.5.2 Modulation quality in 3GPP TS 38.104 35
fm-pm Fault Management, Performance Management role 36
gNB gNodeB (applies to NR) <Next Generation NodeB> 37
M-Plane Management Plane: refers to non-real-time management operations between the O-DU and the O-38
RU 39
NETCONF Network Configuration Protocol. For details see: RFC 6241, “Network Configuration Protocol 40
(NETCONF)”, IETF, June 2011 41
NSA Non-Stand-Alone network mode that supports operation of SgNB attached to MeNB 42
O-CU O-RAN Central Unit – a logical node hosting PDCP, RRC, SDAP and other control functions 43

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       19
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
O-DU O-RAN Distributed Unit: a logical node hosting RLC/MAC/High-PHY layers based on a lower 1
layer functional split. O-DU in addition hosts an M-Plane instance. 2
O-RU O-RAN Radio Unit <O-RAN Radio Unit: a logical node hosting Low-PHY layer and RF 3
processing based on a lower layer functional split. This is similar to 3GPP’s “TRP” or “RRH” but 4
more specific in including the Low-PHY layer (FFT/iFFT, PRACH extraction).>. O-RU in 5
addition hosts M-Plane instance. 6
PTP Precision Time Protocol (PTP) is a protocol for distributing precise time and frequency over 7
packet networks. PTP is defined in the IEEE Standard 1588. 8
PDCCH Physical Downlink Control Channel applies for LTE and NR air interface 9
PBCH Physical Broadcast Channel applies for LTE and NR air interface 10
SA Stand-Alone network mode that supports operation of gNB attached to a 5G Core Network 11
SCS OFDM Sub Carrier Spacing 12
SSB Synchronization Signal Block, in 5G PBCH and synchronization signal are packaged as a single 13
block 14
subordinate The term “subordinate” is used as a replacement for “slave” and is consistent with its use in CUS 15
specification. When consensus emerges on how to eliminate the use of the term “slave” in the 16
referenced standards organization, that approach will be applied to this specification 17
sudo Super-User Do role 18
S-Plane Synchronization Plane: Data flow for synchronization and timing information between nodes 19
SyncE Synchronous Ethernet, is an ITU-T standard for computer networking that facilitates distribution 20
of clock signals over the Ethernet physical layer 21
T-BC Telecom Boundary Clock 22
TWAMP Two-Way Active Measurement Protocol 23
UDP User Datagram Protocol 24
UE User Equipment terminology for a mobile device in LTE and NR 25
UL UpLink: data flow from the UE towards the core network, that is from the O-RU towards in the O-26
DU in a Fronthaul context. 27

2 Test Configuration 1
The conformance tests described in this document require test equipment with specific capabilities to support the testing 2
of each protocol including the M-Plane, U-Plane, C-Plane and S-Plane. In addition, the tests define a specific 3
connectivity between the test equipment and the device under test.  This section describes the test equipment 4
requirements at a high level.  Details are included in each test.   5
As noted in the introduction in the Scope paragraphs, the initial focus of the M-Plane, C-Plane and U-Plane 6
conformance tests is the O-RU.  Version 2.00 and later include S-Plane tests for the O-DU in addition to the S-Plane 7
tests for the O-RU.  The initial test configuration description below is focused on the test equipment and configuration 8
required to test the O-RU. O-DU test configuration descriptions for the S-Plane are covered in the S-Plane section of 9
this document. 10
2.1 Test Configuration for O-RU as the Device Under Test 11
When testing the O-RU, it is connected to test equipment called Test Equipment O-RU (TER).  The TER is shown in  12
Figure 2.1-3.1.1.1-1 below.   TER surrounds the DUT and connects to both the fronthaul interface itself and the radio 13
interface. At the radio interface, the TER collects RF signals from the DUT (downlink) and sends RF signals to the 14
DUT receiver (uplink).  Thus, the TER is made up of three main components, a CUSM-Plane Emulator (CUSM-E), a 15
signal analyser and a signal generator as shown in Figure 2.1-3.1.1.1-1. The RF test interface is described in TS 36.141 16
for LTE, TS 38.141-1 for NR conducted, and TS 38.141-2 for non-conducted tests.  The fronthaul interface is standard 17
Ethernet as described above.  In this case, the DL data flow is evaluated based on what is received by the signal 18
analyser in the RF domain as radiated by the O-RU, and the UL data flow is evaluated based on what is emitted by the 19
signal generator in the RF domain and received by the CUSM-E.   20
When the O-RU is the Device Under Test (DUT), there is Test Equipment, RU (“TER”) that is used to connect to the DUT, run the test and evaluate the test result.fronthaul connectionDUT = O-RURF connection orantenna array(s)Test Equipment, RU(TER)CUSM-Plane EmulatorSignal GeneratorThe Test Equipment, RU (“TER”) provides everything needed to operate the test, including:M-Plane commands to collect O-RU capabilities and configure the O-RUSynchronization via G.8275.1 (Mandatory for O-RU)C-Plane and U-Plane data flow to the O-RUCollection of RF energy to determine if the O-RU reacted correctly to the DL C-Plane and U-Plane dataRadiation of RF energy to be received by the O-RU (note: this could be actually radiated, or conveyed through multiple RF cabled connections)Collection of O-RU UL fronthaul data flows and evaluating it for correctness based on the supplied RF energy to the O-RU antennas or RF connectorsSignal Analyser
 21
Figure 2.1-3.1.1.1-1 Test Setup, DUT = O-RU 22
While M-Plane conformance tests do not generally require all the functions shown for a TER in Figure 2.1-3.1.1.1-1, 23
the intent of this description is to show the general capabilities required for all tests on the O-RU as the DUT including 24
U-Plane, C-Plane and S-Plane tests.  If tests are restricted to only the M-Plane, the required test equipment 25
configuration may be simplified.   26

3 Conformance Measurements 1
3.1 M-Plane Measurements 2
3.1.1 Transport and Handshake Test Scenarios 3
3.1.1.1 Transport and Handshake in IPv4 Environment (positive case) 4
 5
A. Test Description and Applicability 6
This scenario is MANDATORY. 7
This scenario validates that the O-RU properly executes the session establishment procedure with VLANs and a 8
DHCPv4 server.  This test is applicable to IPv4 environments. 9
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 10
 3.1 Management Plane Transport aspects  11
 3.2 NETCONF Call Home to O-RU Controller(s) 12
 13
B. Test Entrance Criteria 14
The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are operational, 15
configured and connected to the O-RU 16
 17
C. Test Methodology 18
a. Initial Conditions 19
1. The O-RU is powered on and has an ethernet connection to the DHCP-server 20
2. The configured DHCPv4 server is reachable by the O-RU NETCONF Server through the VLAN 21
configured for M-Plane. 22
3. Default SSH credentials (sudo) are used by both the O-RU NETCONF Server and the TER NETCONF 23
Client 24
4. IP details for test purposes are pre-defined and fixed (applies to the DHCP server). 25
 26
b. Procedure 27
1. The O-RU NETCONF Server can be preconfigured with no VLAN (known in 802.1Q as native ethernet 28
or an untagged VLAN), a VLAN ID or may optionally perform a VLAN scan by issuing DHCP Discover 29
trying to reach the DHCP Server 30
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server continues the DHCPv4 procedure on the preconfigured VLAN or first 31
VLAN where the Offer from DHCP Server / Relay is received if the scan method is used 32
3. O-RU NETCONF Server retrieves IP details and the IP address of the controlling TER NETCONF Client 33
from the DHCP Server.  Note: RFC 2131 is followed for DHCPv4 34
4. The O-RU NETCONF Server establishes TCP connection and performs a Call Home procedure towards 35
the NETCONF Client using the IP details obtained in step 3 36
5. The TER NETCONF Client establishes a SSH session with the O-RU NETCONF Server.  Proper 37
credentials are used. 38
6. The O-RU NETCONF Server accepts the SSH connection establishment from the TER NETCONF Client 39
7. The TER NETCONF Client and O-RU NETCONF Server exchange capabilities through NETCONF 40
<hello> messages. 41
Note: RFC 6241 is followed for NETCONF communication. 42
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  43
Test scenario step 7 is performed successfully. 44

3.1.1.2 Transport and Handshake in IPv4 Environment (negative case) 1
A. Test Description and Applicability 2
This scenario is MANDATORY 3
This scenario validates that the O-RU properly executes the session establishment procedure with VLANs and a 4
DHCPv4 server.  This test is applicable to IPv4 environments.  Two negative flows are included in this test: 5
 The TER NETCONF Client does not trigger a SSH session establishment in reaction to Call Home 6
initiated by THE O-RU NETCONF Server. 7
 The TER NETCONF Client uses improper credentials when trying to establish a SSH session with the O-8
RU NETCONF Server. 9
 10
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 11
 3.1 Management Plane Transport aspects 12
 3.2 NETCONF Call Home to O-RU Controller(s) 13
 14
B. Test Entrance Criteria 15
The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are operational, 16
configured and connected to the O-RU. 17
 18
C. Test Methodology 19
a. Initial Conditions 20
a. O-RU is powered on and has an ethernet connection to the DHCP-server 21
b. Configured DHCPv4 server is reachable for O-RU NETCONF Server through the VLAN configured for 22
M-Plane. 23
c. Default SSH credentials (sudo) are used by both O-RU NETCONF Server and NETCONF Client 24
d. IP details for test purposes are pre-defined and fixed (applies to DHCP server). 25
e. Procedure 26
i. Flow 1 27
1. The O-RU NETCONF Server can be preconfigured with no VLAN (known in 802.1Q as native 28
ethernet or an untagged VLAN), a VLAN ID or may optionally perform a VLAN scan by issuing a 29
DHCP Discover trying to reach DHCP Server 30
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server continues the DHCPv4 procedure on the preconfigured VLAN or first 31
VLAN where the Offer from the DHCP Server / Relay is received if the scan method is used 32
3. The O-RU NETCONF Server retrieves IP details and the IP address of controlling TER NETCONF 33
Client from the DHCP Server.  Note: RFC 2131 is followed for DHCPv4 34
4. The O-RU NETCONF Server establishes TCP connection and performs Call Home procedure with 35
the TER NETCONF Client using IP details obtained in step 3 36
5. The TER NETCONF Client does not initiate the SSH session establishment procedure. 37
6. The O-RU NETCONF Server periodically repeats the Call Home towards TER NETCONF Client.  38
 39
ii. Flow 2 40
1. The O-RU NETCONF Server can be preconfigured with a VLAN ID or may optionally perform a 41
VLAN scan by issuing a DHCP Discover trying to reach the DHCP Server 42
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server continues the DHCPv4 procedure on the preconfigured VLAN or first 43
VLAN where the Offer from the DHCP Server / Relay is received if the scan method is used 44
3. The O-RU NETCONF Server retrieves IP details and the IP address of the controlling TER 45
NETCONF Client from DHCP Server.  Note: RFC 2131 is followed for DHCPv4 46
4. The O-RU NETCONF Server establishes a TCP connection and performs the Call Home procedure 47
with the TER NETCONF Client using IP details obtained in step 3 48
5. The TER NETCONF Client initiates the SSH session establishment procedure with improper 49
credentials. 50
6. Due to the incorrect SSH credentials, the O-RU NETCONF Server rejects the SSH connection 51
establishment from the TER NETCONF Client. 52
7. The O-RU NETCONF Server starts periodic Call Home procedure towards the TER NETCONF 53
Client. 54
 55

2. Flow 2: Scenario reaches step 7.  The O-RU NETCONF Server falls into Call Home procedure loop. 3

b. Procedure 10
1. The O-RU NETCONF Server supervision timer expires 11

 <rpc supervision-watchdog-reset></rpc> 14
to the O-RU NETCONF Server. 15

watchdog reset message. The O-RU NETCONF server must adjust the timer accordingly if this optional 19
test is performed. 20
6. The O-RU NETCONF Server sends a supervision notification towards the TER NETCONF Client with 21
respect to time-date sent in rpc-reply in step 3. 22
7. Steps 1 to 4 are looped for 30 iterations. 23
8. Note: RFC 6241 is followed for NETCONF communication. 24

                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
C. Test Methodology 1
a. Initial Conditions 2
1. The test procedure described in section 3.1.1.1 or 3.1.1.3for IPv4 and IPv6 respectively is successfully 3
completed. 4
 5
b. Procedure 6
1. The TER NETCONF Client triggers <rpc><get><filter> towards NETCONF Server.  The <filter> 7
argument contains a regular expression that the O-RU NETCONF Server shall apply as a filter. For 8
example, a filter that filters all low-level-rx-endpoints:  9
  <rpc message-id="101" xmlns="urn:o-ran:uplane-conf:1.0" > 10
      <get> 11
          <source>running</source> 12
          <filter type = ”subtree”> 13
              <top xmlns="urn:o-ran:uplane-conf:1.0/”> 14
                  <user-plane-configuration> 15
                      <low-level-rx-endpoints> 16
                      </low-level-rx-endpoints> 17
                  </user-plane-configuration> 18
              </top> 19
          </filter> 20
      </get> 21
   </rpc> 22
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server responds with <rpc-reply><data> where <data> contains details for objects 23
as conforming to the <filter> (as per the above example filter: all low-level-rx-endpoints) 24
 25
D. Test Requirement (expected result) 26
Test step 2 is performed successfully. 27

  <rpc message-id="101" xmlns=" urn:ietf:params:xml:ns:netconf:base:1.0" > 6

alarm 17: No external sync source”.  The format of alarm notification follows RFC5277. 18

3.1.6 O-RU Software Update 14
3.1.6.1 O-RU Software Update and Install (positive case) 15
A. Test Description and Applicability 16
This scenario is MANDATORY 17
This test validates that the O-RU can successfully perform a software download and software install procedure. 18
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 19
 5. Software Management 20
 21
B. Test Entrance Criteria 22
The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are operational, 23
configured and connected to the O-RU. 24
C. Test Methodology 25
a. Initial Conditions 26
1. The test procedure described in section 3.1.4.1 is successfully completed. 27
2. A correct and internally consistent SW package is available for test purposes. 28
3. The O-RU provides at least one slot available for SW update procedure.  The status of this slot is assumed 29
to be {active = False, running = False, access = READ-WRITE} 30
4. A sFTP server is available with an account for the SW update procedure on the TER 31
 32
b. Procedure 33
1. The TER NETCONF Client triggers <rpc><software-download>.  The O-RU NETCONF Server responds 34
with <rpc-reply><software-download> 35
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server performs a software download procedure.  When the download is 36
completed, the O-RU NETCONF Server sends <notification><download-event> with status 37
COMPLETED to TER NETCONF Client 38
3. The TER NETCONF Client triggers <rpc><software-install> informing the O-RU NETCONF Client 39
about the desired slot for installation.  This slot must have the attributes active = FALSE, running = 40
FALSE, access = READ-WRITE.  The O-RU NETCONF Server responds with <rpc-reply><software-41
install> with status STARTED. 42
4. The O-RU NETCONF Server examines the downloaded software.  The files are error free by design in 43
this test.  The O-RU NETCONF Server installs the new software files to the desired slot.  44
5. The O-RU NETCONF Server sends <notification><install-event><status> to the TER NETCONF Client. 45
Field <status> contains the value COMPLETED to indicate the successful installation of software to the 46
desired slot. 47
 48

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       32
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
D. Test Requirement (expected result) 1
1. Test step 5 completed with notification that indicates successful installation of the downloaded software. 2
2. Status of SW slot used for SW installation is set to VALID.  Other parameters of software slot shall not be 3
changed. 4
 5
3.1.6.2 O-RU Software Update (negative case) 6
A. Test Description and Applicability 7
This scenario is MANDATORY. 8
This scenario corresponds the following chapters in [3]: 9
 5. Software Management 10
 11
B. Test Purpose 12
This test validates that the O-RU can successfully perform a software download procedure.  One or more files are 13
intentionally corrupted to make sure that the O-RU is able to recognize an invalid software update file and protect 14
itself from installing this file.  15
C. Test Methodology 16
a. Initial Conditions 17
The test procedure described in section 3.1.4.1 is successfully completed. 18
A modified software package is available for test purposes (proper content of manifest.xml, but fake/invalid 19
content of software files) 20
The O-RU provides at least one slot available for the software update procedure (status != INVALID, active = 21
False, running = False, access = READ-WRITE) 22
A sFTP server is available with an account dedicated for the software update procedure 23
b. Procedure 24
1. The TER NETCONF Client triggers <rpc><software-download>.  The O-RU NETCONF Server responds 25
with <rpc-reply><software-download> 26
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server performs the software download procedure.  When the download is 27
complete, the O-RU NETCONF Server sends <notification><download-event> with status COMPLETED 28
to the TER NETCONF Client 29
3. The TER NETCONF Client triggers <rpc><software-install> informing the O-RU NETCONF Server 30
about desired slot the software shall be installed to.  The O-RU NETCONF Server responds with <rpc-31
reply><software-install> with status STARTED. 32
4. The O-RU NETCONF Server determines that the software file is invalid and sends <notification><install-33
event><status> to the TER NETCONF Client.  The Field <status> is correctly updated with one of the 34
following status: FILE_ERROR or INTEGRITY_ERROR. 35
 36
D. Test Requirement (expected result) 37
1. Test step 4 completed a described. 38
2. Status of SW slot used for SW installation is set to INVALID.  Other parameters of software slot shall not be 39
changed. 40

3.1.9  External Input / Output Ports 25
3.1.9.1 External Input Port State Detection 26
A. Test Description and Applicability 27
This scenario is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. The test is applicable only for O-RUs supporting logical input 28
ports. 29
This test validates proper handling of logical input ports. 30
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 31
 11.4.1 External Input 32
 33
B. Test Entrance Criteria 34
 The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are 35
operational, configured and connected to the O-RU. 36
 Supplementary circuitry is required to force a change of logical state of input lines belonging to an input port. 37
It is assumed that logical input ports are internally pulled to logical high state by O-RU, therefore 38
supplementary circuitry shall only allow to change the input port to a logical low. To determine a physical 39
input line for this test, one shall read the customer documentation applicable for the O-RU being tested. 40
 41
C. Test Methodology 42
a. Initial Conditions 43
1. The test procedure described in section 3.1.4.1 is successfully completed. 44
 45
b. Procedure 46
1. The External Input Ports are left in their normal, default stated.  For the purposes of this test, these input 47
ports are assumed to be a logical high.  48
2. The TER NETCONF Client retrieves state of chosen input port by issuing <rpc><get><filter 49
type="subtree"><external-io xml...><input><port-in></port-in></input></external-50
io></filter></get></rpc> 51
3. The O-RU NETCONF Server provides the state of every line-in belonging to the input port under test to 52
the TER NETCONF Client. For all input lines, the state is TRUE, indicating open circuit (no shortage to 53
ground is detected by input lines) 54

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       38
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
4. The TER supplementary circuitry randomly shorts one or more input lines to the ground. Changes shall 1
occur with a periodicity greater than 30 seconds. 2
5. For every change the O-RU NETCONF Server sends notification <external-input-change> to the TER 3
NETCONF Client.   The notification contains updated states of input lines belonging to the port under test. 4
A state FALSE indicates shortage to ground detected by particular input line. 5
6. This test scenario is looped to step 4 for a total of 10 iterations 6
 7
D. Test Requirement (expected result) 8
Step 5 is correctly validated for each iteration of the test.  9
 10
3.1.9.2 External Output Port State Control 11
A. Test Description and Applicability 12
This scenario is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. The test is applicable only for O-RUs supporting logical output 13
ports. 14
This test validates proper handling of logical output ports. 15
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 16
 11.4.2 External Output 17
 18
B. Test Entrance Criteria 19
 The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are 20
operational, configured and connected to the O-RU. 21
 Supplementary circuitry is required to measure voltage of an output port signal.  To determine the mapping of 22
physical output lines to ports, one shall read customer documentation for the O-RU being tested.  The 23
definition of voltage levels served by output lines of output ports and the maximum allowed current sourced by 24
single an output line shall be validated against the TER capabilities. 25
 26
C. Test Methodology 27
a. Initial Conditions 28
1. The test procedure described in section 3.1.4.1 is successfully completed. 29
 30
b. Procedure 31
1. The TER NETCONF Client issues :<rpc><edit-config> to the O-RU NETCONF Server requesting all 32
output lines belonging to output port to be set to FALSE. 33
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server sets logical LOW state to output lines corresponding to step 1 and responds 34
to TER NETCONF Client with <rpc-reply> 35
3. The TER supplementary circuitry shows that all output lines of the target output port are set to logical 36
LOW state. 37
4. The TER NETCONF Client issues :<rpc><edit-config> towards NETCONF Server requesting a random 38
change of states of output lines belonging to target output port.  Changes shall occur with a periodicity 39
greater than 30 seconds. 40
5. The O-RU NETCONF Server sets the requested states of output lines for the states defined by step 4 and 41
responds to NETCONF Client with <rpc-reply>.  The TER supplementary circuitry validates the change. 42
6. This test scenario is looped to step 4 for a total of 10 iterations 43
 44
D. Test Requirement (expected result) 45
Step 5 is correctly validated for each iteration of the test.  46

3.1.11 ALD Communications 4
3.1.11.1 ALD Communications Test 5
A. Test Description and Applicability 6
This scenario is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY for a O-RU equipped with a RET port (regardless of whether 7
this is a raw RS-485 port or OOK modem coupled internally to antenna connector(s)).  This scenario shall be 8
performed against each ALD port exposed by the O-RU. 9
The purpose of the test is to validate the ALD communications protocol and operation of the O-RU. The following 10
functions are validated in this test. 11
 Proper transmission of the content if RPC <ald-communication> towards desired ALD port 12
 Proper calculation of FCS 13
 Proper application of basic transparency to content to be transmitted 14
 Proper addition of start / stop flags 15
 Proper reception of payload injected to ALD port 16
 Proper removal of start / stop flags 17
 Proper application of basic transparency to content received from ALD port 18
 Proper validation of FCS in data received from ALD port. 19
 20
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 21
 11.3 Operational aspects of Antenna Line Devices 22
 23
B. Test Entrance Criteria 24
 The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are 25
operational, configured and connected to the O-RU. 26
 It is assumed, that O-RU being a subject of this conformance test scenario is proven to be compliant to the 27
following specifications: 28
1. ISO/IEC 13239:2002 “High-level data link control (HDLC) procedures” 29
2. 3GPP TS 25.460 “UTRAN Iuant Interface: General aspects and principles” 30
3. 3GPP TS 25.461 ”UTRAN Iuant Interface: Layer 1” 31
4. 3GPP TS 25.462 ”UTRAN Iuant Interface: Signalling Transport” 32
5. 3GPP TS 25.466 “UTRAN Iuant Interface: Application Part” 33
 The O-RU uses a 9.6 kbps data rate on its ALD port(s) for transmission and reception, regardless of connector 34
supported by particular ALD port. 35
 36
 37
C. Test Methodology 38
As O-RU does not verify correctness of the payload that is exchanged between NETCONF Client and ALD (except 39
FCS for traffic coming from ALD) - any payload can be used in test vector, under condition, that test vectors are 40
compliant to referenced above set of specification documents (e.g. length is not smaller than minimum size of real 41
message). 42
RS-485 sniffer / injector is needed for this test. Such a device shall be connected either to O-RU’s RS-485 port or 43
to RS-485 port of Smart BiasT connected to O-RU with coaxial cable (depending on O-RU construction) 44
Unless not specified otherwise – RS-485 sniffer / injector shall be connected to ALD port corresponding to record 45
“port-id” used in RPC <ald-communication>. 46
In case O-RU exposes ALD port as antenna port, test environment should utilize Smart BiasT for conversion 47
between OOK modulation at antenna port and RS-485 signaling that RS-485 sniffer / injector can handle. DC 48
voltage for Smart BiasT device shall be provided by O-RU through antenna feeder. 49

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       41
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
If not specified otherwise, for test purposes RS-485 sniffer / injector is connected to ALD port which will be 1
addressed in RPC <ald-communication> within the scenario. 2
As this test is intended to verify O-RU functions and there will be no real ALD connected – compliance to the 3
required HDLC message structure is required, whilst the AISG payload can be artificial (unless otherwise specified 4
in test case). The O-RU does not verify if messaging is correct, hence, for test simplicity and ease of test result 5
verification, artificial test vectors can be used. 6
a. Initial Conditions 7
2. The test procedure described in section 3.1.4.1 is successfully completed. 8
 9
a. Procedure 10
i. Test Case 1: Transmission towards ALD (positive scenario) 11
Scope: CRC calculation, transparency algorithm application, start / stop flag addition, datagram 12
transmission using desired ALD port  13
1) NETCONF Client sends regular RPC <ald-communication> message containing bytes 0x7D and 14
0x7E in “ald-req-msg” record. 15
2) O-RU calculates FCS, adds it to datagram provided in record “ald-req-msg”, applies basic 16
transparency (replaces every occurrence of byte “0x7E” with two bytes “0x7D 0x5E”, respectively, 17
replace byte “0x7D” with two bytes “0x7D 0x5D”) and add start/stop flags 0x7E. 18
3) O-RU sends payload calculated in step 2 through ALD port mentioned in record “port-id” of RPC. 19
4) RS-485 sniffer / injector receives payload sent by O-RU. Received payload is subject of analysis for 20
scenario success / failure classification 21
 22
ii. Test Case 1 Test Requirement (expected result) 23
Content received by RS-485 listener / injector is compared with content of RPC <ald-communication>. 24
a) payload shall be sent by desired ALD port of O-RU 25
b) FCS shall be properly calculated 26
c) basic transparency shall be properly applied 27
d) start / stop flags shall be added to payload that has been received by RS-485 sniffer / injector 28
Test scenario is considered as completed with success in case all mentioned above conditions are satisfied. 29
Any deviation means test scenario is failed. 30
 31
iii. Test Case 2: Reception from ALD (positive case) 32
Scope: datagram reception, start / stop flag detection and removal, transparency algorithm applications, 33
CRC verification  34
Note: Test case 2 shall be performed just after Test case 1 so that content injected by RS-485 sniffer / 35
injector is considered by O-RU as ALD’s response to message sent towards ALD in Test case 1. Timing 36
between Test case 1 and Test case 2 shall follow 3GPP specifications mentioned above. 37
1) RS485 sniffer / injector sends properly formatted (start / stop flags, FCS and min / max payload size) 38
message containing strings “0x7D 0x5E” and “0x7D 0x5D” towards O-RU’s ALD port used in Test 39
case 1. 40
2) O-RU receives the content. 41
3) O-RU removes start / stop flags, performs basic transparency (replaces “0x7D 0x5E” with “0x7E” 42
and “0x7D 0x5D” with “0x7D”), makes sure if FCS is correct according content of datagram.  43
4) O-RU sends “ald-resp-msg” towards NETCONF Client. 44
 45
iv. Test Case 2 Requirement (expected result) 46
Content received by NETCONF Client is compared with content injected by RS-485 sniffer / injector. 47
a) record “ald-port” shall indicate proper O-RU’s ALD port as source of the payload 48
b) basic transparency is properly applied 49
b) counter of received octets is properly incremented 50
d) counters of frames with wrong FCS (CRC) and frames without stop flags are not incremented 51

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       42
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
Test scenario is considered as completed with success in case all mentioned above conditions are satisfied. 1
Any deviation means test scenario is failed. 2
v. Test Case 3: Reception from ALD (negative case – wrong FCS) 3
Scope: datagram reception, start / stop flag detection and removal, transparency algorithm application, 4
CRC verification  5
Note: Test case 3 shall be performed just after Test case 1 so that content injected by RS-485 sniffer / 6
injector is considered by O-RU as ALD’s response to message sent towards ALD in Test case 1. Timing 7
between Test case 1 and Test case 3 shall follow 3GPP specifications mentioned above. 8
1) RS-485 sniffer / injector sends message containing wrong FCS towards O-RU’s ALD port used in Test 9
case 1. 10
2) O-RU receives the content. 11
3) O-RU removes start / stop flags, performs basic transparency (replaces “0x7D 0x5E” with “0x7E” and 12
“0x7D 0x5D” with “0x7D”) and detects, that FCS is incorrect according content of received datagram. 13
4) O-RU sends “ald-resp-msg” towards NETCONF Client. 14
 15
vi. Test Case 3 Requirement (expected result) 16
Content received by NETCONF Client is compared with content injected by RS-485 sniffer / injector. 17
a) record “ald-port” shall indicate proper O-RU’s ALD port as source of the payload 18
b) record “ald-resp-msg” is empty 19
b) counter of received octets and counter of frames without stop flags are not incremented 20
d) counters of frames with wrong FCS (CRC) is incremented 21
Test scenario is considered as completed with success in case all mentioned above conditions are satisfied. 22
Any deviation means test scenario is failed. 23
 24
vii. Test Case 4: Reception from ALD (negative case – no stop flag) 25
Scope: datagram reception, start / stop flag detection 26
Note: Test case 4 shall be performed just after Test case 1 so that content injected by RS-485 sniffer / 27
injector is considered by O-RU as ALD’s response to message sent towards ALD in Test case 1. Timing 28
between Test case 1 and Test case 4 shall follow 3GPP specifications mentioned above. 29
1) RS-485 sniffer / injector sends message not terminated by stop flag “0x7E” towards O-RU’s ALD port 30
used in Test case 1. 31
2) O-RU receives the content. 32
3) O-RU reaches the end of reception window without receiving stop flag that would terminate the 33
datagram. 34
4) O-RU sends “ald-resp-msg” towards NETCONF Client. 35
 36
viii. Test Case 4 Requirement (expected result) 37
Content received by NETCONF Client is compared with content injected by RS-485 sniffer / injector. 38
a) record “ald-port” shall indicate proper O-RU’s ALD port as source of the payload 39
b) record “ald-resp-msg” is empty 40
b) counter of received octets and counter of frames of frames with wrong FCS (CRC) are not incremented 41

________________________________________________________________________________________________

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       43
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
d) counter of frames without stop flags is incremented 1
Test scenario is considered as completed with success in case all mentioned above conditions are satisfied. 2
Any deviation means test scenario is failed. 3
 4
ix. Test case 5: Transmission towards ALD (negative scenario – wrong ALD port) 5
Scope: CRC calculation, transparency algorithm application, start / stop flag addition, datagram 6
transmission using desired ALD port (ports are not used by the same HDLC Primary Device) 7
Scenario is applicable only in case O-RU supports more than one ALD port and under condition that ALD 8
ports do not share single modem. 9
IMPORTANT: In this scenario RS-485 sniffer / injector shall be connected to ALD port different from 10
than the one indicated in record “port-id” of RPC <ald-communication>. 11
1) NETCONF Client sends regular RPC <ald-communication> message. 12
2) O-RU performs the content processing and sends the content towards ALD port that corresponds to 13
content of record “port-id” of RPC 14
3) RS-485 sniffer / injector does not receive payload sent by O-RU.  15
 16
x. Test Requirement (expected result) 17
Test scenario is considered as completed with success in case RS-485 sniffer / injector does not receive 18
payload in step 3. Any deviation is considered as failed test case. 19
 20
xi. Test case 6: Transmission towards ALD (negative scenario – non-existing ALD port) 21
Scope: datagram reception 22
1) NETCONF Client sends regular RPC <ald-communication> message. Parameter <port-id> used in 23
RPC does not point to existing ALD port. 24
2) O-RU sends <rpc-response> to NETCONF Client. In the response parameter “status” contains value 25
“REJECTED” and parameter “error-message” informs about wrong ALD port has been used in RPC 26
<ald-communication> 27
3) NETCONF Client receives described above <rpc-response> message. 28
 29
xii. Test Requirement (expected result) 30
Test scenario is considered as completed with success in case step 3) is reached. 31

3.1.12 Log Management 33
3.1.12.1 Log Management Test 34
A. Test Description and Applicability 35
This scenario is MANDATORY. 36
This test validates the capability of the O-RU to upload troubleshooting logs including alarm information. 37
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 38
 11.2.1 Troubleshooting 39
 40
B. Test Entrance Criteria 41
 The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are 42
operational, configured and connected to the O-RU. 43
 Supplementary circuitry is required to measure voltage of an output port signal.  To determine the mapping of 44
physical output lines to ports, one shall read customer documentation for the O-RU being tested.  The 45

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       44
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
definition of voltage levels served by output lines of output ports and the maximum allowed current sourced by 1
single an output line shall be validated against the TER capabilities. 2
 3
C. Test Methodology 4
a. Initial Conditions 5
1. The test procedure described in section 3.1.4.1 is successfully completed. 6
 7
b. Procedure 8
1. The TER NETCONF Client sends <rpc><start-troubleshooting-logs> to the O-RU NETCONF Server.  9
The O-RU NETCONF Server responds with <rpc-reply>< troubleshooting-status-grouping >. 10
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server starts generating one or more file(s) containing troubleshooting logs.  When 11
the generation of the log file(s) are completed, the O-RU NETCONF Server sends 12
<notification><troubleshooting-log-generated> with a list of one or more log file names to the TER 13
NETCONF Server.  14
NOTE: It is assumed that the generated log file(s) contains troubleshooting logs related to alarm 17 15
measured in 3.1.5.2 but the content and format are not specified. 16
3. The TER NETCONF Client sends  <rpc><file-upload>log-file-name</file-upload></rpc> to the O-RU 17
NETCONF Server to start uploading the log file(s).  The O-RU NETCONF Server responds with <rpc-18
reply><file-upload> with status SUCCESS.  19
4. The O-RU NETCONF Server uploads the log file(s) to NETCONF Client by sFTP. When file upload is 20
completed, the O-RU NETCONF Server sends <notification><upload-notification> with status 21
SUCCESS. 22
 23
D. Test Requirement (expected result) 24
Test step 4 is performed successfully. 25
NOTE: The O-RU vendor may check the contents of the uploaded log file in detail for the reported alarm 17, 26
but as noted, the content and format of troubleshooting logs are not defined. 27

operational, configured and connected to the O-RU. 42
2. Result validation of this test requires TER capabilities such as a network sniffer that allows for traffic analysis 43
over ETH frames between O-RU and O-DU. 44
 45

Plane interfaces. 52

 1
3.2 UC-Plane Measurements 2
3.2.1 UC-Plane Standard Test Definitions 3
The following sections describe test scenarios for equipment implementing the U-Plane and C-Plane O-RAN option 4
7.2x protocols.    5
The initial focus of this conformance test document is validation of the O-RU as the device under test (DUT).  Future 6
versions of this specification may address conformance tests with other devices as the DUT. 7
3.2.1.1 UC-Plane Measurements, O-RU TEST SCENARIO 8
In these sets of tests, the Device Under Test (DUT) is the O-RU.   9
This document describes conformance tests for 4 scenarios: 10
1. Conducted FDD tests for FR1 radios 11
2. Non-conducted (OTA) FDD tests for FR1 radios 12
3. Conducted TDD tests for FR1 radios 13
4. Non-conducted tests for TDD FR1 and FR2 radios 14
 15
The O-RU must only be tested for the scenarios that apply to the O-RU capabilities. The fact that there are 4 scenarios 16
defined does not imply that every O-RU must be tested for all scenarios in order to be O-RAN compliant and 17
consequently the O-RU does not have to support all the capabilities required to test all 4 scenarios (i.e. support of FR1, 18
FR2, TDD, FDD, conducted and non-conducted). In other words, depending on whether the O-RU supports capabilities 19
such as FDD, TDD, FR1 and or FR2, the corresponding scenarios that match the O-RU capabilities will apply only. For 20
example, an O-RU that does not have or cannot provide access to antenna ports (or TAB connectors), supports TDD 21
and operates at FR2 bands, the corresponding scenario that the O-RU will need to be tested to be O-RAN conformant is 22
scenario #4 only. Another example, for an O-RU that supports FDD, operates at FR1 bands and has or can provide 23
access to antenna ports (or TAB connectors), scenario #1 or #2 can apply but only one of the two possible scenarios will 24
be selected to test the O-RU for O-RAN conformance.   25
 26
For scenario #1 and #3 above the RF test setup is as described in 3GPP TS 38.141-1[NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE].  For 27
scenarios #2 and #4 the RF test setup is as described in TS 38.141-2. Note that O-RAN conformance testing is expected 28
to be “off-line” and not to be run while an O-DU and/or O-RU is operating and serving actual users.  The O-RU 29
manufacturer must also make available the same declarations described in 3GPP TS 38.141-1, TS 38.141-2 [NR] and 30
TS 36.141 [LTE] Section 4.6.  This will determine the radio’s support for multi-carrier operation (e.g., if multi-carrier 31
operation is supported on different connectors) 32
Since the purpose of this document is to test O-RAN Fronthaul conformance and not to duplicate 3GPP RF tests, only 33
selected parts of TS 38.141-1, TS 38.141-2 [NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE] will be used for RF testing.  These selected test 34
features are only necessary to test whether the O-RU correctly interpreted and generated the O-RAN C-Plane and U-35
Plane messages correctly. There will also be some additions to the test waveforms used in TS 38.141-1, TS 38.141-2 36
[NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE] to fully exercise the features of the O-RAN Fronthaul protocol.  These selected parts and 37
additions are summarized below: 38
3.2.1.1.1 For scenario #1 (Conducted FDD tests for FR1 radios) 39
 For downlink tests for type 1-C radios (radios with antenna port connectors and passive antennas) the test 40
configuration described in TS 38.141-1 D.1.1 will be used.  Only a single antenna port will be used unless the 41
test explicitly requires more than one port and the radio supports more than one port.  RF test equipment will 42
be connected at the point described in TS 38.141-1 section 4.2.1. Note that an antenna port is an electrical 43
conducting port that is connected to an array element. 44
 For uplink tests for type 1-C radios (radios with antenna port connectors and passive antennas) the test 45
configuration described in TS 38.141-1 D.2.1 will be used.  Only a single antenna port will be used unless the 46

Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.

test explicitly requires more than one port and the radio supports more than one port.  RF test equipment will 1
be connected at the point described in TS 38.141-1 section 4.2.1. Note that an antenna port is an electrical 2
conducting port that is connected to an array element. 3
 For downlink tests for type 1-H radios (radios with TAB connectors and active antenna systems) the test 4
configuration described in TS 38.14138.141-1 D.3.1 will be used for conducted tests.  Only a single TAB 5
connector will be used unless the test explicitly requires more than one connector.  RF test equipment will be 6
connected at the point described in TS 38.141-1 section 4.2.2. Note that a transceiver array boundary (TAB) 7
connector is an electrical conducting port that is connected to an array element via a radio distribution network 8
(RDN). 9
 For uplink tests for type 1-H radios (radios with TAB connectors and active antenna systems) the test 10
configuration described in TS 38.14138.141-1 D.4.1 will be used for conducted tests.  Only a single TAB 11
connector will be used unless the test explicitly requires more than one connector.  RF test equipment will be 12
connected at the point described in TS 38.141-1 section 4.2.2. Note that a transceiver array boundary (TAB) 13
connector is an electrical conducting port that is connected to an array element via a radio distribution network 14
(RDN). 15
 The basic downlink test will start with the Test model described in NR-FR1-TM1.1 and E-TM1.1.  Subsequent 16
tests will adapt this model to test additional features of the O-RAN interface (e.g., Modifying the payload data, 17
blanking some symbols, etc.).  Note this test model describes the IQ data contained in the O-RAN packets not 18
the O-RAN specific parameters.  This test model will also be augmented with the following O-RAN specific 19
parameters: 20
Includes “stock” eAxC values as configured via M-Plane: 21
 DU_Port_ID: two bits, nominal value 00b 22
 BandSector: nominal 6 bits, nominal value 000000b 23
 CC_ID: nominal 4 bits, nominal value 0000b (most tests invoke only one component carrier) 24
 RU_port_ID: 4 bits, nominal values 0000b through 0011b or to whatever max value needed for a 25
specific test 26
 If the radio manufacturer declares support for multi-carrier a different eAxC will be assigned for each carrier. 27
Note that most tests described in 3GPP TS 38.141-1[NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE]  require testing at the bottom, 28
middle and top of the supported bands of the radio.  This specification relaxes that requirement because the 29
purpose is to test the fronthaul compliance and not the radio performance. 30
 Compression: Static 16-bit fixed point IQ bitwidth in both DL and UL 31
 Beamforming: no beamforming (beamId = 0x0000), assumed to mean boresight radiation (normal to the 32
antenna surface) at some undetermined beamwidth (recall that beam weight magnitudes must be equal to 33
unity) 34
 Transport: L2 Ethernet, eCPRI with no fragmentation and no QOS 35
 Delay Parameters: The test will be executed with a direct fiber connection to the O-RU and the network delay 36
is considered negligible for the purpose of delay management.  Therefore, T12_min = T12_max = 0 and 37
T34_min = T34_max = 0. 38
The radio will report its supported values for: 39
o T2a_min/max_up 40
o Ta3_min/max_up 41
o T2a_min/max_cp_ul 42
o Tcp_adv_dl 43
These parameters will be used to calculate the delay windows needed for the delay management tests below.  44
Note that T1a_min_up = T2a_min_up and T1a_max_up = T2a_max_up due to the fixed, zero network delay.  45
Similarly, Ta4_min_up = Ta3_min_up and Ta4_max_up = Ta3_max_up.  Similarly, T1a_min_cp_ul = 46
T2a_min_cp_ul and T1a_max_cp_ul = T2a_max_cp_ul.   47
 48
 Uplink tests will start with the basic 3GPP test signal for Fixed Reference Channels for receiver sensitivity and 49
in-channel selectivity as described in 3GPP TS 38.141-1[NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE].  All O-RAN specific 50
parameters will be the same as described above for downlink testing.  As with downlink testing subsequent 51
tests will build on this basic waveform modifying parameters as needed to exercise O-RAN specific features. 52
 Uplink tests will be conducted using power levels at least 30dB higher than the power levels used to test 3GPP 53
Receiver sensitivity described in 3GPP TS 38.141-1 Table 7.2.5-1[NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE]. This is to ensure 54

defined in TS 38.141-2 4.2-1. The RF analyser test equipment is connected to the Test Antenna and is located 31
out of the OTA chamber. 32

TS 38.141-2 E.2.1 where the Test Antenna will be placed inside an OTA chamber and measurements are 34
referenced to the radiated characteristics defined over the air (OTA) at the Radiated Interface Boundary (RIB) 35
defined in TS 38.141-2 4.2-1. The RF generator test equipment is connected to the Test Antenna and is located 36
out of the OTA chamber. 37

3.2.1.1.5 Test Configuration for the UC-Plane 35
The TER shown in Figure 2.1-3.1.1.1-1 provides M-Plane and S-Plane commands and sequences to correctly set up the 36
O-RU for testing using the fronthaul connection – meaning a criterion and prerequisite for executing all UC-Plane tests 37
is proper operation of the O-RU’s synchronization and M-Plane capabilities.  The TER provides the specific C-Plane 38
and U-Plane data flows and collects data from the radiated energy from the O-RU and evaluates based on the collected 39
RF energy whether the O-RU correctly received and interpreted the fronthaul DL data flow.  For many tests a single RF 40
detector is satisfactory to detect the radiated signal but for beamforming tests an RF pattern must be measured to 41
validate the correct beam is being generated according to the C-Plane commands and U-Plane data flowing across the 42
fronthaul interface. 43
In addition, the TER generates RF energy using the signal generator and feeds it to the O-RU’s antennas (or antenna 44
connectors) which is expected to be used by the O-RU, in conjunction with the C-Plane UL commands sent by the TER 45
over the fronthaul connection, to generate UL data flows on the fronthaul connection which are received and evaluated 46
by the TER.  For almost all tests a single RF emitter is satisfactory to generate the radiated signal, even beamforming 47
tests wherein the received power level will validate that the beam main lobe was correctly specified across the fronthaul 48
interface, except for the case of uplink channel-information-based beamforming tests where multiple RF emitters are 49
needed to emulate multiple uplink spatial streams. 50

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       54
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
3GPP-specified tests will be used here to simplify the testing, because such tests will need to be supported by the O-RU 1
anyway for 3GPP conformance testing.  The specific test cases identify where this is possible and where changes must 2
be made to adequately test O-RAN features. 3
Note that when testing the O-RU for fronthaul interface conformance, much more than the fronthaul interface is being 4
tested, indeed the entire O-RU is under test, including digital and analog processing having nothing to do with the 5
fronthaul interface.  Therefore a “passed” test can be interpreted with some confidence as indicating a properly 6
operating fronthaul interface, but a “failed” test may indicate a problem with the fronthaul interface or with some other 7
operation within the O-RU therefore failed tests may require some troubleshooting.  While 3GPP TS 38.141-1, TS 8
38.141-2 [NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE] describes the basic waveform used in these tests it does not describe how the 9
various channels should be put into O-RAN sections.  The 3GPP TS 38.141-1 NR-FR1-TM1.1 [NR FR1], TS 38.141-2 10
NR-FR2-TM1.1 [NR FR2], and TSTS 36.141 E-TM1.1 [LTE] signals are tightly packed with data.  All tests will divide 11
that data into “stock” data sections using the sections described below.  To expedite the definition and creation of the 12
tests, a set of standard test environments and patterns is defined in this section.  This includes a “stock” arrangement of 13
data sections in DL (same is used for UL) which can be used regardless of the specific bandwidth and SCS used in the 14
test.  Specifically, there are “stock” 1-symbol, 2-symbol, and 3-symbol data section sets that shall be cited in test 15
definitions (numbered “A” through “F”) that will support various test cases.  The test cases are expected to specify the 16
data section definition of a test slot and all slots are expected to follow the same data section definition unless a test 17
specifically states otherwise.  In many cases only some symbols within a slot will be subject to testing; the remaining 18
symbols are expected to remain undefined for the test and may have data sections defined according to the normal 19
operation of the O-DU (e.g. set to carry synch or reference signals consistent with LTE or NR).  In cases where a 20
specific type of data section cannot be supported by the DUT, then that data section is omitted in the symbol(s) and the 21
corresponding U-Plane data shall be set to zero in DL (and arranged to have no RF power in UL).  Figure 3.2.1.1-2 22
shows the “stock” data section definition. 23

 26
There is also “stock” U-Plane data that is PN23 data, representing user data prior to modulation, as specified within 27
3GPP 38.14138.141-1[CCITT Recommendation O.151 (10/92): https://www.itu.int/rec/T-REC-O.151-199210-I/en] 28
which is assumed to start at a frame boundary and be identical in all frames in both DL and UL, unless a specific test 29
states differently.  The PN sequence is expected to be running for the duration of the frame for whatever is the 30
bandwidth and SCS (this is different from how the data sections are handled, wherein the data sections are truncated 31
based on the number of PRBs per symbol).  However, in many cases only some symbols within a frame will be actually 32
subject to testing (as defined by the specific tests) so will contain the test PN sequence data; the remaining symbols are 33
expected to remain undefined for the test and may contain data according to the normal operation of the O-DU (e.g. set 34
to carry synch or reference signals consistent with LTE or NR).  Note that the PN sequence initial value is provided by a 35
seed which may be included as a Test Command parameter. If the parameter is omitted the PN sequence generator will 36
use a “seed” value of all ones. 37

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       55
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
For all tests, the test definition shall define the specific slots and symbols subject to test (carrying the “stock” C-Plane 1
data section definition and the “stock” U-Plane data) with the remaining slots and symbols undefined but carrying 2
normal 3GPP synch and control data and empty user data.  All slots and symbols subject to test are identical in each 3
frame, so tests do not have to wait for a specific frame number and are not expected to reset or otherwise perturb the 4
normal frame number sequence.  This is intended to allow the test to disrupt normal O-DU and O-RU operation as little 5
as possible. If there is a specific need to validate the construction of a specific frame or slot of data, a test may elect to 6
zero the test data and leave undefined the data sections for all except one slot or frame of data; where this is necessary it 7
will be described in the specific test definition, but this is expected to be an exceptional case. 8
3.2.1.1.6 Generic Steps for Test Execution, O-RU TEST SCENARIO 9
The following are the generic test steps used when testing the O-RU, although specific tests may deviate from this 10
general procedure: 11
1) Configure the Test Equipment, O-RU (TER) for test execution, which may include defining the specific test to 12
execute. This may also include using a scripting language for describing the test. 13
2) Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 14
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1. 15
3) Send appropriate C-Plane and U-Plane DL data flows and collect the O-RU radiated energy (or collect from 16
antenna connectors) using RF detection equipment. 17
4) Evaluate the RF energy pattern from the O-RU to determine if the O-RU correctly received and interpreted the 18
fronthaul C-Plane and U-Plane data flows.  In some cases it also includes decoding and demodulating the RF 19
signal to ensure all UC-Plane messages were interpreted correctly. 20
5) Send appropriate C-Plane messages to define the desired UL U-Plane flow, at the same time cause the RF 21
signal generator to radiate (or feed into antenna connectors) the appropriate RF energy pattern for the test.  22
This also means meeting the appropriate timing windows to allow the O-RU to decode and process the C-Plane 23
messages before the signal generator starts sending RF. 24
6) Collect the O-RU UL data flows on the fronthaul interface and evaluate for correctness; this will generally be 25
U-Plane data only but in limited cases (LAA) may include UL C-Plane messages too. 26
7) Since FDD uplink and TDD tests require tight timing constraints between the components of the TER it is 27
recommended that CUSM emulator signal the RF test equipment when C-Plane signalling has started for a 28
frame.  How this signal is used by the RF test equipment to synchronize transmission and reception is 29
implementation dependant. 30
 31
 32
3.2.1.2 UC-Plane Measurements, O-DU Test Scenario 33
For future study. 34
3.2.2 Minimum Capabilities of the TER for U-Plane and C-Plane Tests 35
Since many features of the O-RAN protocol rely on the O-DU instructing the O-RU to put data in specific resource 36
blocks using a specific compression method it is imperative that the test equipment support features that allow 37
comparing data on the fronthaul side with data on the RF side of the radio. 38
3.2.2.1 Signal Analyzer 39
 Must have the capability of decoding and demodulating an RF signal either received over the air or on a 40
conducted interface.  This data must be made available for comparison with data sent on the fronthaul 41
interface. 42
 Must be able to determine the Phase and amplitude of any signal for beamforming tests. 43
 Obviously must support the frequency range of the radio being tested. 44
3.2.2.2 Signal Generator 45
 Must provide software capable of building a correct 5G or LTE waveform. 46
 Should have the ability to automatically build 3GPP compliant test waveforms and should provide a 47
mechanism for editing the parameters of that waveform. 48

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       56
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
 Must be able to be synchronized with the O-DU emulator to ensure proper timing of uplink C-Plane and U-1
Plane messages 2
3.2.2.3 CUSM-ECUSM-Plane Emulator (CUSM-E) 3
 Must be able to extract IQ data from uplink U-Plane messages and demodulate and decode the data to ensure it 4
is the same as what was commanded in the uplink C-Plane messages. 5
 Must have the ability to synchronize with the RF signal source. 6
 Should have the ability to perform as a PTP Master or subordinate depending on the synchronization 7
configuration the radio supports. 8
 Must have the ability to accept frequency domain IQ and encapsulate it according to user input on the correct 9
sections. 10

3.2.3 FR1 FDD Conducted-Signal Tests  12
3.2.3.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class NR testing Generic (NRG)  13
Note that all downlink tests in this section use a 3GPP test wave form with 30 KHz subcarrier spacing and 100 MHz 14
Bandwidth as described in section 3GPP 38.141 -1 NR-FR1-TM1.1 and section 3.2.1.1.5 of this document.  There are 15
several variations on this test signal depending on the capabilities of the radio.  If the radio does not support the 16
numerology used in the example tests as reported in the M-plane it will be up to the test developer to modify their tests 17
to adapt to the radio.  This can usually be accomplished by using stock test patters described above.  The test is 18
expected to follow the same spirit as the tests in this document but things like symbol numbers, number of PRBs, etc. 19
may have to be changed. 20
All uplink tests in this section use a 3GPP test waveform described in 38.141-1 section A1, in particular G-FR1-A5-1 21
(30 kHz subcarrier spacing, QPSK, 100 MHz BW). As with downlink tests if the radio does not support this signal it is 22
up to the test developer to modify the parameters of the test without changing the spirit of the test. 23
3.2.3.1.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Base 3GPP DL 24
A. Test Description and Applicability 25
This test is MANDATORY. 26
 27

3.2.3.1.3 UC Plane O-RU Base Class FDD Test UL 26
A. Test Description and Applicability 27
This test is MANDATORY. 28
 29
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can meet the most basic uplink requirements for O-RAN fronthaul 30
correctly interpreting C-Plane messages and correctly constructing uplink U-Plane messages from an RF signal. 31
Subsequent tests will build on this to exercise additional capabilities of the Fronthaul. 32
 33
The test validates that correct uplink operation of the O-RU using 3GPP Reference Sensitivity level definition 34
(Section 7.2 TS 138.141-1) of the Conducted Receiver Characteristic Test section (Section 7 TS 138.141) and power 35
Levels at least 30 dB above Reference Sensitivity power Level described in TS 138.141-1 Table 7.2.5-1.  This is to 36
improve the likelihood that all data will be received by the radio correctly since we are not interested in testing 37
receiver sensitivity but only the O-RAN protocol compliance.  38
 39

5.  It will be for 5G New Radio only. The radio must have conducted antenna ports (FR1) or TAB connectors. Note 23

C. Test Methodology 27
Leverage from the well-known payload (PN23 sequence) of the uplink signal to compare it with the payload of the 28
signal communicated on the O-RAN interface. The IQ information is extracted from the U-Plane message and 29
demodulated to retrieve payload.  30
  31
a: Initial Conditions 32

Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  Connect the signal source to the O-RU antenna 34
port and configure the source to transmit the required 3GPP test signal upon receiving a trigger signal from the 35

CUSM-E.  The signal source power level should be adjusted to at least 30 dB above the setting used in the 3GPP 1
receiver sensitivity test. 2
b: Procedure 3
 Load uplink test waveform (G-FR1-A1-5 : SCS30k_51RB) on the RF Signal Source  4

trigger signal from the O-DU emulator that C-Plane messages have been sent. 6

windows  10

 Extract IQ information  12
 Extract Payload 13
 Compare payload binary sequences  14
  15

the test frame. 32

The O-RU must support the default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.1 of this document.  The test numerology will be 11
30 kHz subcarrier spacing and 100 MHz Bandwidth as described in section 3GPP TS 138.141-1 section G-FR1-12
A1-5.  It will be for 5G New Radio only. The radio must have conducted antenna ports (FR1) or TAB 13
connectors. The radio must report that it supports the SymInc parameter.   Note this signal may be changed to any 14
of the 3GPP sensitivity test signals in table A.1-1 in 3GPP TS 138.141-1 if the ratio does not support the 15
numerology and bandwidth used in this test.  The test signal described in this section will be used if the radio 16
supports that numerology and bandwidth. 17
 18
C. Test Methodology 19
Leverage from the well-known payload (Pseudo Random sequence) of the uplink signal to compare it with the 20
payload of the signal communicated on the O-RAN interface. The IQ information is extracted from the U-Plane 21
message and demodulated to retrieve payload.  22
  23
a. Initial Conditions 24
Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 25
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  Connect the signal source to the O-RU 26
antenna port and configure the source to transmit the required 3GPP test signal upon receiving a trigger signal 27
from the CUSM-E.  The signal source power level should be adjusted to at least 30 dB above the setting used 28
in the 3GPP receiver sensitivity test. 29
b. Procedure 30
 Load uplink test waveform (G-FR1-A1-5 : SCS30k_51RB, 100 MHz) on the RF Signal Source.  Note this 31
signal has a PN23 sequence as user data.  Configure the source to generate a new PN23 sequence in 32
symbols #5 and #6. 33
 Configure Signal Source to play test waveforms on 10ms frame boundaries starting when it receives a 34
trigger signal from the O-DU emulator that C-Plane messages have been sent. 35
 Load C-Plane message sequence on Test Equipment O-RU (TER) – Only symbols #5 and #6 in each slot 36
will be used in this test. All other symbols will contain either reference signals or data but will not be 37
considered part of the test.  These two symbols will be used to determine whether the radio properly 38
increments the current symbol ID when the symInc bit is set. The C-Plane message for symbol #5 should 39
have the symInc bit set.  This message should have a second section describing symbol #6 (using the 40
symInc mechanism).  All PRBs in each symbol will be requested (In the example waveform 51 PRBs). 41
 Arm Test Equipment O-RU (TER) to capture DUT fronthaul Messages  42
 Launch test to play the C-Plane messages and trigger the source to play the RF signal on a frame 43
boundary.  44
 Record U-Plane messages from DUT for a complete frame and the eAxC corresponding to the Antenna 45
port  46
 Extract IQ information  47
 Extract Payload 48
 Compare payload binary sequences  49
  50
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  51
1. The verdict is “Test pass” if payload binary sequences match between the uplink test frame sent to the DUT 52
and the received U-Plane data from the DUT.  In particular symbols number 5 and 6 should properly contain 53
the correct PN23 sequences that were built by the signal source. 54
2. If any of the test conditions is not true, the verdict for the whole test is "Fail" 55

3.2.3.1.8 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Extended using reMask Parameter 3GPP DL – 1
Resource Allocation 2
A. Test Description and Applicability 3
This test is MANDATORY. 4
 5
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can correctly decode and interpret C-Plane and U-Plane 6
messages putting resource block in the correct place in the transmitted signal using the reMask parameter. In 7
this test stock data section #6”D” will be used to exercise the reMask, only PRBs 1 through 5 will be used in 8
this test. 9
 10
Using a standard 3GPP NR-FR1-TM1.1 test frame for FDD the O-DU emulator (i.e., O-RAN interface of 11
the TER described in section 2.1) will generate C-Plane and U-Plane messages that require the O-RU to 12
transmit on the downlink the standard NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal as modified below.  This signal is shown 13
below in Figure 3.2.3.1-8: 14
 15
 16  17
Figure 3.2.3.1-8 NR-FR1-TM1.1 Modification 1 18
 19
This generic 3GPP NR-FR1-TM1.1 test frame consists of a PDCCH in the first two symbols of every slot 20
consisting of 3 PRBs.  All the remaining PRBs in the frame consist of Physical Downlink Shared Channel 21
data. 22
 23
This test requires non-zero data to populate all allocated resource blocks (as described below).  This data 24
will be a PN23 sequence with a seed value of all ones. 25
 26
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can accurately interpret C-Plane resource allocation messages 27
with the reMask parameter set, transfer U-Plane data into the correct resource elements and transmit this 28
data accurately in the downlink.  This test is applicable for Type A and Type B radios (No precoding is 29
required).  The test will be conducted therefore there will be no channel distortion or interference.  It is 30
mandatory the radio pass this test to be considered O-RAN conformant. 31
 32
This test will utilize stock data section #6 described above. 33
 34
B. Test Entrance Criteria 35
The O-RU must support the default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.1 of this document.  The test numerology 36
will be 30 KHz subcarrier spacing and 100 MHz Bandwidth as described in section NR-FR1-TM1.1.  It will 37
be for 5G New Radio only. The radio must have conducted antenna ports (FR1) or TAB connectors. 38

 1
The Radio must support the reMask parameter as notified by the M-Plane.  The signal analyzer must have 2
the ability to decode the downlink shared channel. 3
 4
C. Test Methodology 5
 6
a. Initial Conditions 7
Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using M-Plane 8
commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  Connect the signal analyser to the O-RU antenna port and 9

b. Procedure 11
Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal described above in the O-DU 12
emulator.  Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that 13
describe the signal as described below. Every symbol allocated should be described by a single type 1 14
section (DL-SCH and DCI).   Only symbol #6 will be used for the reMask test. The data in this section 15
must be a PN23 sequence using an initial seed of all ones. The first bits of the PN23 will be in PRB1 16
and continue in consecutive resource elements to the end of PRB5. No section type zero messages will 17
be used for this test. 18
 19
Symbol number 6 should be stock data section type “D” as shown above.  This test will only be using 20
PRBs 1 through 5.  The corresponding C-Plane message will contain a section IDs in a single C-Plane 21
message describing symbol #6.  The startSymbolId in the application header will be symbol #6. The C-22
Plane message will have one section with the reMask set to only the odd number resource elements.  23
The number of PRBs will be 4. The start PRB will be 1. 24
 25
The corresponding U-Plane message will be a new PN23 Sequence (initial seed is all ones) in PRBs 1 26
through 5 of symbol #6. 27
 28
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  29
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance requirement 30
for this radio category (i.e., EVM). 31
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should only contain the same PN23 signals that were sent 32
in the U-Plane but only every other odd resource element. 33

this data accurately in the downlink.  This test is applicable for Category A and Category B radios (No precoding is 1

purpose of this test is not to test the use of section extension 10 with either section extension 1 or 2 (Real time 3

TM1.1.  It will be for 5G New Radio only.  26
 27
There will be numPortc “layers” or eAxCs referred to in the test.  That is there will be one C-Plane message 28
referencing the port group eAxC ID obtained from the M-Plane but numPortc U-Plane messages. 29
