                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
C. Test Methodology 1
 2
a. Initial Conditions 3
Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using M-4
Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  Connect the signal analyser to the O-RU 5
antenna ports being tested and configure the analyser with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and 6
demodulate the transmitted signal.  Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase 7
coherence between the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.  Let the DUT and TER to 8
warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range. 9
b. Procedure 10
Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal described above in the O-DU emulator.  11
Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane message that describes the signal.  12
This message should include section extension 10. Note the test will be performed three times exercising all 13
three beam group types. Every symbol should be described by a single section (DL-SCH and DCI) using 14
section type 1 messages. The data in the sections must be a PN23 sequence using an initial seed of all ones. No 15
section type zero messages will be used for this test.  Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages for each 16
layer (i.e., numPortc repetitions).  17
 18
Test case #1 (beamGroupType = 00b, Common Beam): 19
For this test the beamGroupType parameter should be set to 00b. It is expected that all layers will be played on 20
the same beam ID and this is the beam ID used in the corresponding C-Plane message. Play those messages to 21
the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.1.  Repeat the entire frame the number of 22
times required to synch the signal analyser and allow it to demodulate and decode the test frame.  Use the 23
signal analyser to decode at least two beams and ensure they are the same. 24
 25
Test case #2 (beamGroupType = 01b, beam matrix indication): 26
For this test the beamGroupType parameter should be set to 01b. It is expected that all layers will be played on 27
consecutive beam IDs starting with the beam ID in the C-Plane message. Play those messages to the O-RU 28
respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.1.  Repeat the entire frame the number of times 29
required to synch the signal analyser and allow it to demodulate and decode the test frame.  Use the signal 30
analyser to decode at least two beams and ensure they meet the consecutive beam criteria. 31
 32
Test case #3 (beamGroupType = 10b, beam vector listing): 33
For this test the beamGroupType parameter should be set to 10b. In this case the section extension should list 34
“numPortc” beam IDs in section extension 10.  It is expected that all layers will be played on the beam IDs 35
indicated in the section extension. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in 36
section 3.2.1.1.1.  Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyser and allow 37
it to demodulate and decode the test frame.  Use the signal analyser to decode at least two beams and ensure 38
they agree with the beam vector listing. 39
 40
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  41
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance requirement for this 42
radio category (i.e., EVM). 43
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should be the same as the signal described above.   44
3. If it contains all the same PRB assignments and data, and the beams are measured as described in test cases #1 45
through #3 above the test passes. 46

d. Procedure 20

of the test waveform is as described in 3GPP. 23

signal from the O-DU emulator that C-Plane messages have been sent. 25
 Inject the test signal into the O-RU with the application of an initial set of beamweights, or equivalently 26
magnitude and phase relation, between all the TER ports connected to the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) 27
to emulate the phase and magnitude difference “seen” by the antenna elements under test. For example, 28
initial beamweights could be set to be “all equal” (i.e. no beamforming).   29
 Load C-Plane message sequence on Test Equipment O-RU (TER) – Use the O-DU emulator control 30
interface to build the appropriate C-Plane message (Single C-Plane message) that describes the signal. For 31
this test symbols number 6 and 7 will be used in each slot.   32
Every symbol should be described by a single type 1 section (DL-SCH and DCI) except symbols #6 and #7 33
which will be used as the payload data. The data in symbol #6 is expected to be a new PN23 sequence 34
starting in the first PRB and continuing to PRB 51.  Symbol #7 should be identical to symbol #6. No section 35
type zero messages will be used for this test.  The C-Plane message should include section extension 10 with 36
numPortc equal to what was received on the M-Plane at start up.  The eAxC ID should be the group eAxC ID 37
also received from the M-Plane.  Run the test three times using: 38
Test Case #1 (beamGroupType = 00b, Common Beam): All layers should have the same beam ID.  The 39
signal sent by the source should correspond to the same beam ID.  It is expected that the source is connected 40
to at least two port groups to ensure the same beam is being used. 41
Test Case #2 (beamGroupType = 01b, beam matrix indication): All layers should have consecutive beam IDs 42
starting with the beam ID in the C-Plane message.  The signal sent by the source should correspond to the 43
consecutive beam IDs.  It is expected that the source is connected to at least two port groups to ensure the 44
consecutive beams are being used 45
Test Case #3 (beamGroupType = 10b, beam vector listing): All layers will be assigned beam IDs based on 46
the list of beam IDs contained in the section extension.  The number of beam IDs must be equal to numPortc.  47
The signal sent by the source should correspond to the signalled beam IDs.  It is expected that the source is 48
connected to at least two port groups to ensure that the correct beams are being used 49

3.2.3.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming (BFM)  1
This section describes the beamforming conformance testing for ORAN fronthaul interface. The tests do not aim to test 2
the O-RU beamforming performance or capabilities but to test that the O-RU under test focuses the RF energy or 3
sensitivity into a specific direction and with a specific granularity following the O-DU emulator (i.e., O-RAN interface 4
of the TER described in section 2.1) C-Plane messages.  5
Unless stated otherwise in a test case, the following statements apply to all the test cases defined in this section: 6
 It is based on conducted testing with a setup such as described in Section 2.1 and it only applies to O-RU DUTs 7
that have conducted antenna ports or TAB connectors. 8
 9
 It applies to Type A and Type B O-RU DUTs. 10
 11
 It applies to LTE and/or 5G New Radio O-RU DUTs.  In both cases, precoding is not required in any test case.   12
 13
 If O-RU DUT supports Analog Beamforming (i.e. time domain beamforming), all the U-Plane test frames are 14
defined by segmenting the Stock Test A: 1 section per symbol.  The definition of this Stock Test A can be 15
found in Figure 3.2.1.1-2 and the description accompanying this Figure.  Each slot shall include multiple 16
sections (one per symbol within the slot) and only one beam at a time (i.e. one beamId at a time) and therefore 17
only one beam can be tested per slot. 18
 19
 If O-RU DUT supports Digital Beamforming (i.e. frequency domain beamforming), all the U-Plane test frames 20
are defined by segmenting the Stock Test B: 2 sections per symbol definition as shown in Figure 3.2.1.1-2.  21
Each slot shall include multiple sections (two per symbol within the slot) and only one beam per section at a 22
time (i.e. one beamId at a time) and therefore up to two different beams can be tested per slot. 23
 24
 If O-RU DUT supports multiple polarizations, it is up to the TER to determine if the testing is carried out for 25
each polarization separately or multiple polarizations at the same time. In any case, it is important to guarantee 26
that the correct eAxC_ID for the correct polarization (or polarizations) is exercised.  27
 28
 For O-RU DUT that support LTE:  29
o Downlink tests will use a standard 3GPP E-TM1.1 test frame for FDD (Section 6.1.1.1 TS136.141-1) with 30
20MHz bandwidth (100 RB) as shown in Figure 3.2.3.2-1. 31

Figure 3.2.3.2-1 E-TM1.1 FDD 20 MHz 100RB 33
If 20MHz is not supported by the O-RU DUT, then it will use the highest bandwidth supported by the O-34
RU DUT. 35
o Uplink test will use a standard 3GPP UL RMC Configuration definition for FDD (TS36.521-1) and 36
power levels 30dB above Reference Sensitivity power level with 10MHz bandwidth (100 RB) as shown 37
in Figure 3.2.3.2-2. 38

RU DUT. 42

 19

ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.  24

test and configure the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the 26
transmitted signal.  27

3.2.3.2.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP UL – No Beamforming 53
A. Test Description and Applicability 54
This test is MANDATORY. 55
 56
 57

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       84
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can receive a basic 3GPP test frame with no beamforming 1
(beamId=0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 2
 3
 4
B. Test Entrance Criteria 5
 Manufacturers’ declaration that defines list of magnitude and phase relation (or beamweights) between antenna 6
ports or TAB connectors and/or beam directions with antenna array characteristics when O-RU DUT is 7
operating with no beamforming.  8
 9
C. Test Methodology 10
 11
a. Initial Conditions 12
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 13
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1. 14
 Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase coherence between the antenna 15
ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.  16
 Connect the signal source to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the beam under test 17
and configure the source with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and generate the test 18
signal.  19
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.   20
 21
b. Procedure 22
a. Build an appropriate test signal described above in the signal source of the TER.  23
b. Inject the test signal into the O-RU with the application of an initial set of beamweights, or equivalently 24
magnitude and phase relation, between all the TER ports connected to the antenna ports (or TAB 25
connectors) to emulate the phase and magnitude difference “seen” by the antenna elements under test. For 26
example, initial beamweights could be set to be “all equal” (i.e. no beamforming). 27
c. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the 28
signal and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (UL-29
SCH) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 30
d. Play the C plane messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.1. while 31
also triggering the signal source.   32
e. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the DUT, allow it to create and send the U 33
plane messages to the O-DU and for the O-DU to demodulate, decode and extract the payload. 34
f. Repeat the previous steps but now in step b apply a different set of beamweights or phase relation between 35
all the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) when injecting the test signal into the O-RU. For example, 36
repeating the process for a number of different beamweights will simulate the reception of the test signal 37
from different beam directions. This allows to determine if the O-RU is really focusing the sensitivity to 38
the correct beam direction. 39
 40
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  41
1. The test frame received by the TER/O-DU should be the same as the signal described above and should contain 42
all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data. 43
2. The beamweights or magnitude and phase relation at the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) of the test signal 44
that achieves the highest performance (i.e. best EVM, power, SNR, etc.) should match with the manufacturer’s 45
declaration of the phase relation expected for no beamforming. 46

3.2.3.2.3 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Predefined-beam 48
Beamforming 49
A. Test Description and Applicability 50
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 51
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with predefined-beams 52
beamforming (beamId≠0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 53
The transmitted beam direction is measured for each indexed beam required in this measurement, see below. The 54
measured transmitted direction is compared to manufacturer-designated direction. Transmitted direction could be 55
defined by the phase relation between the antenna ports or TAB connectors under test, or directly by extracting the 56
beam direction. 57

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       85
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
Depending on the O-RU beamforming capabilities regarding the ability to generate “coarse”, “fine” and/or “beam 1
groups”, as defined in [2] Section 10.4.1.1. 2
 3
The elevation θ and azimuth Φ angles are defined as in [2] Section 10.4.1.1: 4
 5
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Predefined-beam Beamforming conformance test 6
might include multiple test that the O-RU must comply: 7
a. “Coarse” beamIds test:  8
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that are defined as coarse granularity (coarse beamIds) to the O-DU 9
emulator, the test should include the following beams: 10
1. A coarse beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles. 11
2. A coarse beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 12
3. A coarse beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 13
4. A coarse beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 14
5. A coarse beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 15
 16
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth (Φ) or elevation angle (θ), fewer than 5 beam angles will be measured. 17
 18
b.  “Fine” beamIds test:  19
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that are defined as fine granularity (fine beamIds) to the O-DU 20
emulator, the test should include the following beams: 21
1. A fine beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles. 22
2. A fine beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 23
3. A fine beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 24
4. A fine beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 25
5. A fine beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 26
 27
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth or elevation angle, fewer than 5 beam angles will be measured. 28
 29
c.  “beam-group” beamIds test:  30
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that belong to same and different beam-groups to the O-DU emulator, 31
the test should include the following beams: 32
1. All beams that belong to a beam-group with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) or elevation (θ) angles. 33
2. All beams that belong to a beam-group with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ). 34
3. All beams that belong to a beam-group with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ). 35
4. All beams that belong to a beam-group with maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 36
5. All beams that belong to a beam-group with minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 37
 38
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth or elevation angle, fewer than 5 beam-groups will be measured. 39
 40
 41
B. Test Entrance Criteria 42
 Manufacturers’ defined list of beam indices and their associated magnitude and phase relation between antenna 43
ports or TAB connectors and/or beam directions with antenna array characteristics. 44
 45
C. Test Methodology 46
 47
a. Initial Conditions 48
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 49
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  50
 Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase coherence between the antenna 51
ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.   52
 Connect the signal analyzer to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the beam under 53
test and configure the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the 54
transmitted signal.  55
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range. 56

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       86
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
   1
b. Procedure 2
a. Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal described above in the O-DU emulator.   3
b. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal 4
and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (DL-SCH and 5
DCI) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 6
c. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows 7
described in section 3.2.1.1.1.   8
d. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to demodulate 9
and decode the test frame. 10
e. Extract either the beamweights, or magnitude and phase relation, or beam direction from the measured 11
signal. 12
 13
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  14
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance requirement for this 15
radio category (i.e., EVM). 16
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should be the same as the signal described above and should 17
contain all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data. 18
3. The signal relation (i.e. beamweights, or magnitude and phase relation) between antenna ports or TAB 19
connectors, or the extracted beam direction, should match the expected relation, or beam direction, 20
corresponding to the beam under test within a tolerance defined by the manufacturer.  21
 22
3.2.3.2.4 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP UL – Predefined-beam 23
Beamforming 24
A. Test Description and Applicability 25
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 26
 27
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can receive a basic 3GPP test frame with predefined-beams 28
beamforming (beamId≠0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC).  29
 30
The same description and criteria for selecting the beams to be tested applies as in section 3.2.3.2.3 applies, but 31
instead it is related to the uplink direction.  32
 33
B. Test Entrance Criteria 34
 35
 Manufacturers’ defined list of beam indices and their associated magnitude and phase relation between antenna 36
ports or TAB connectors and/or beam directions with antenna array characteristics. 37
  38
C. Test Methodology 39
 40
a. Initial Conditions 41
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 42
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1. 43
 Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase coherence between the antenna 44
ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.    45
 Connect the signal source to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the beam under test 46
and configure the source with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and generate the test 47
signal.  48
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.   49
 50
b. Procedure 51
a. Build an appropriate test signal described above in the signal source of the TER. 52
b. Inject the test signal into the O-RU with the application of an initial set of beamweights, or equivalently 53
magnitude and phase relation, between all the TER ports connected to the antenna ports (or TAB 54
connectors) to emulate the phase and magnitude difference “seen” by the antenna elements under test. For 55
example, initial beamweights could be set to be “all equal” (i.e. no beamforming).   56

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       87
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
c. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the 1
signal and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (UL-2
SCH) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 3
d. Play the C plane messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.1. while 4
also triggering the signal source.   5
e. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the DUT, allow it to create and send the U 6
plane messages to the O-DU and for the O-DU to demodulate, decode and extract the payload. 7
f. Repeat the previous steps but now in step b apply a different set of beamweights or phase relation between 8
all the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) when injecting the test signal into the O-RU. For example, 9
repeating the process for a number of different beamweights will simulate the reception of the test signal 10
from different beam directions. This allows to determine if the O-RU is really focusing the sensitivity to 11
the correct beam direction. 12
 13
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  14
1. The test frame received by the TER/O-DU should be the same as the signal described above and should contain 15
all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data. 16
2. The beamweights or magnitude and phase relation at the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) of the test signal 17
that achieves the highest performance (i.e. best EVM, power, SNR, etc.) should match with the manufacturer’s 18
declaration of the beam under test. 19
 20

b. A weight-based beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle 39
(θ). 40
c. A weight-based beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle 41
(θ). 42
d. A weight-based beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle 43
(θ). 44

(θ). 46
 47

 49
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Weight—based Dynamic Beamforming 50
conformance test should also evaluate the following compression methods for each of the supported beams 51
described above (a. to e.) for the O-RU to comply: 52
a. No compression method applied to the beamforming weights.  53
b. Block floating point compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit mantissa. 54
c. Block scaling compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit scaler. 55
d. μ-law compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit fixed width. 56
e. Beamspace compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit scaler.  57

 13
a. Initial Conditions 14

using section type 1 messages, the sections in the first symbol of the slot will contain section extension 28
extType=0x01 to convey the beam weights, it is not required that the next sections contain extension type 1 29
since the same beam IDs will not change along the slot. If O-RU does not support a field, then its value 30
should be 0x0. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 31
c. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows 32
described in section 3.2.1.1.1.   33
d. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to demodulate 34
and decode the test frame. 35
e. Extract either the beamweights, or magnitude and phase relation, or beam direction from the measured 36
signal. 37

The beamweights or magnitude and phase relation at the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) of the test signal 7 that achieves the highest performance (i.e. best EVM, power, SNR, etc.) should match with the 8 manufacturer’s declaration of the beam under test. 9  10 3.2.3.2.9 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Channel-Information-based 11 Beamforming 12 A. Test Description and Applicability 13 This Test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 14  15 The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with channel-information-based 16 beamforming with multiple spatial streams from multiple users (i.e. MU-MIMO). 17  18 For Category A radios, the test is for each polarization separately and consequently either different or same channel 19 models can be defined for each of the polarization. For Category B, same channel might be used for both 20 polarizations and the test might measure each polarization separately. 21 The transmitted beam direction is measured for each scenario required in this measurement.  The measured 22 transmitted direction is extracted from the decoded received signal in the TER. Transmitted direction is defined by 23 properly receiving a data transmission between the O-RU and the target User Equipment while destroying or 24 heavily attenuating the data transmission between the O-RU and the other User Equipment. 25 The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Channel-Information-based Beamforming 26 conformance test should evaluate the following scenarios for the O-RU to comply and will rely on TER Channel 27 Emulation capabilities as shown in Figure 3.2.3.2-3.  28  29  30 Figure 3.2.3.2-3 TER with Channel Emulation Capability 31  32 a. A scenario where two spatial streams, or eAxC flows, are generated for two users (one layer each) with M 33 antenna ports or TAB connectors. The O-DU will report to the O-RU via C plane messages an emulated 34

channel estimate 𝐻 ≜  [ℎଵଵ, . . . , ℎଵெ, ℎଶଵ, . . . , ℎଶெ] ∈ ℂଶ௫ெ. The emulated channel  𝐻  shall model a static channel, 1
with rank not lower than the number of spatial streams, and it shall not be a block-diagonal channel. As an 2
example, a Butler channel model could be implemented as emulated channel. The O-RU will calculate and 3
apply the beamweight matrix 𝐺 ≜  [𝑔ଵଵ, . . . ,𝑔ଵெ,𝑔ଶଵ, . . . ,𝑔ଶெ] ∈ ℂெ௫ଶ in such that the received signal at the 4
users is the same as the generated in the O-DU. It is up to the O-RU on how to calculate the beamforming 5
weights, for example Zero-forcing, regularized zero-forcing / MMSE, etc.   6
 7
If O-RU supports Analog Beamforming (Time Domain Beamforming), the test should not apply any analog 8
beamforming or time domain beamforming. In this case, M is not the number of antenna ports or TAB connectors 9
but the number of TRX channels supported by the O-RU. 10
 11
B. Test Entrance Criteria 12
 13
 The O-RU must have at least two TRX chains with conducted antenna ports (or TAB connectors) to be 14
connected to a signal analyzer. 15
 The TER equipment must either include a channel emulator between the O-RU antenna ports and the signal 16
analyzer or the signal analyzer be capable of applying the required channel matrix being emulated between the 17
O-RU and the users.  18
 Manufacturers’ defined list of number of TRX chains and what antenna ports or TAB connectors are connected 19
to each TRX chain.  20
 21
C. Test Methodology 22
 23
a. Initial Conditions 24
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 25
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  26
 Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase coherence between the antenna 27
ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.   28
 Connect the signal analyzer to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the scenario under 29
test and configure the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the 30
transmitted signal.  31
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.   32
 33
b. Procedure 34
a. Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal described above in the O-DU 35
emulator.   36
b. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal 37
and the scenario under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (DL-SCH and 38
DCI) using section type 5 and 6 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 39
c. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows 40
described in section 3.2.1.1.1. 41
d. Capture the test signals and pass them through a channel emulator or apply the signal processing required to 42
emulate the channel under test.   43
e. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to 44
demodulate and decode the test frame. 45
 46
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  47
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance requirement for this 48
radio category (i.e., EVM). 49
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should be the same as the signal described above and should 50
contain all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data. 51

3.2.3.3 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Compression (CMP) 1
Validate the correct implementation and interpretation of mandatory and optional IQ data compression formats 2
described in [2]. Also, evaluate the consistency in U-Plane signaling. 3
It applies to the following CUS fronthaul specification sections in [2]: 4
 Section 5.4.2 for layout of C-Plane message, in particular Section Type 1 5
 Section 5.4.4.10 for applicability of "udCompHdr" and "reserved" fields 6
 Section 6.3.3.15/16/17 for applicability of udCompParam 7
 Section 6.3.2 for U-Plane message layout 8
 Section 6.3.3 for coding of applicable Information Elements 9
 Table 8-2 for mandatory/optional capabilities. 10
 Annex A  11
 12
The objective is primarily to test the protocol, prior to the compression algorithms performance. 13
Signalling: IQ Compression related fields in UC-Plane messages include:  14
 U-Plane IQ data field  15
 C-Plane udCompHdr (per section 5.4.4.10 of [2]) 16
 U-Plane udComphdr (per section 6.3.3.13 of [2]) 17
 U-Plane udCompParam (per section 6.3.3.15 of [2]) 18
 19
Compression: Current specification includes 5 compression modes, including uncompressed mode (fixed point).  Tests 20
should cover each one of these modes   21
 fixed-point 22
 block floating-point 23
 block scaling 24
 mu-law 25
 modulation compression (modulation compression not included in this document)  26
 27
IQ Bit Width: IQ information can be represented using different bit width (1-16 bits). To optimize test time, tests 28
should be performed on a subset of bit widths  29
 9 bits 30
 14 bits  31
3.2.3.3.1 Overview of Compression Test Methodology 32
A common test methodology and structure will be used across all compression test cases. Each one of the test cases will 33
be defined with specific input parameters and expected output values.  34
To minimize influence of the Radio’s RF performance to the test results, the test methodology will be based on a 35
relative comparison between modulated signal measurements performed on a test frame with uncompressed IQ (fixed 36
16 bits) and measurements on the same test frame using compressed IQ. The test will verify that the difference between 37
measurements fits within an acceptable range for the test to pass. 38
For downlink test, the modulated signal measurement is performed by a signal analyser on the antenna port of the O-39
RU.  40
For uplink measurement, the modulated signal measurement is performed with the IQ extracted from the Uplink U-41
Plane data sent by the O-RU on the O-RAN interface.  42
The following paragraphs in this overview section outline the details of these common test methodologies.  43
3.2.3.3.1.1 Test Frame 44
The test frames used for compression conformance test will be referred in this document as “NR-FR1-CMP-TST-45
FRAME-DL” Downlink Standard Compression Test frame and “NR-FR1-CMP-TST-FRAME-UL” Uplink Standard 46
Compression Test frame. They are 5G NR frames based on the description in section 3.2.1.1.5 with specific attributes 47
described below. 48

3.2.3.3.1.2 Test Frame Power  3
To ensure that the compressed IQ exponent value is properly tested, each symbol of the test frame will include 3 4
sections with different power levels.  The Power levels are relative powers to the first group of PRBs transmitted.  Any 5
valid 3GPP power level may be used for the first set of PRBs as long as the power levels of the remaining PRBs are 6
also valid.  Figure 3.2.3.3-1 below shows PRB power relative to the first set of PRBs. 7
    0 dB for the bottom third of total PRBs in the symbol (referred as PDSCH0) 8
 -10 dB for the middle third of total PRBs in the symbol (referred as PDSCH1) 9
 -20 dB for the upper third of total PRBs in the symbol (referred as PDSCH2) 10
 11
The spectrum representation of the frame shown in Figure 3.2.3.3-1 below highlights the various power levels for each 12
group of PRBS within a symbol.  13

3.2.3.3.1.7 Results Analysis 3
In general, for each specific Compression Test in this conformance test document, the test will pass if the following 4
conditions are met: 5
 Power measurement differences between Uncompressed and Compressed are within acceptable range  6
 EVM measurement difference between Uncompressed and Compressed are within acceptable range  7
 Data integrity measurements show no data corruption 8
 Uplink U-Plane Header measurements exclude fields for static compression 9

3.2.3.3.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Compression Static Format (SFM) Fixed-Point (FP)  3
A. Test Description and Applicability 4
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY and should be performed if the O-RU supports this compression 5
format. 6
 7
The purpose of this test is to: 8
 Validate correct encoding of IQ data under the following conditions.  9
o RU Static compression configurations 10
o Fixed point IQ data format 11
o Selection of 2 supported bit width: 9 bits, 14 bits  12
o Uplink / downlink 13

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       103
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
 Validate that in the U-Plane PRB header, the udCompHeader, “reserved” and udCompParam fields are 1
not present  2
 3
B. Test Entrance Criteria 4
 The test uses the setup and methodology described in section 3.2.1.1. 5
 6
 7
C. Test Methodology 8
a.  Initial Conditions 9
 The O-RU is started 10
 Fronthaul Ethernet interface configured for communication between TER and the DUT. 11
 O-RU synchronized with TER using S-Plane 12
 Communication established between TER and the DUT such that it is possible to exchange U-Plane and 13
C-Plane messages  14
 Signal Analyzer connected to DUT’s antenna port and setup according to DUT RF output configuration 15
 Signal Source connected to DUT’s antenna port and setup according to DUT RF input configuration 16
 17
b.  Procedure 18
For each supported bit width (9 bits, 14 bits), the following tests need to be performed: 19
  20
1. Downlink test 21
 Via the M-Plane or another suitable mechanism, put the O-RU into a static configuration with the 22
downlink configured as follows: no compression, (16 bits) 23
 Arm Signal Analyzer to capture the next Frame  24
 Send the “uncompressed” NR-FR1-CMP-TST-FRAME-ST-DL-UNC-16B test stimulus file to the 25
DUT 26
 With the Signal Analyzer, perform the 3 power measurements  27
 CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH0 in dBm 28
 CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH1 in dBm 29
 CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH2 in dBm 30
 With the Signal Analyzer, perform the 3 EVM measurements  31
 CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH0 in % 32
 CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH1 in % 33
 CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH2 in % 34
 With the Signal Analyzer, check Data integrity measurements  35
 CMP-Uncompressed-BER-PDSCH0  36
 CMP-Uncompressed-BER-PDSCH1  37
 CMP-Uncompressed-BER-PDSCH2  38
 Via the M-Plane or another suitable mechanism, put the O-RU into a static configuration with the 39
downlink configured as follows: Fixed point, 9-bit (then 14 bits)  40
 Send the “Compressed” NR-FR1-CMP-TST-FRAME-ST-DL-FPF-9B (then 14B) test stimulus 41
file to the DUT 42
 With the Signal Analyzer, perform the 3 power measurements  43
 CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH0 in dBm 44
 CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH1 in dBm 45
 CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH2 in dBm 46
 With the Signal Analyzer, perform the 3 EVM measurements  47
 CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH0 in % 48
 CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH1 in % 49
 CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH2 in % 50
 With the Signal Analyzer, check Data integrity measurements  51
 CMP-Compressed-BER-PDSCH0  52
 CMP-Compressed-BER-PDSCH1  53
 CMP-Compressed-BER-PDSCH2  54
 Verify the following conditions  55
 Power measurements within acceptable range  56
 Difference between CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH0 and CMP-57
Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH0 is within ACC_PWR_PDSCH0 range 58

Compressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH1 is less than ACC_EVM_PDSCH1 value. 45
 Difference between CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH2 and CMP-46
Compressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH2 is less than ACC_EVM_PDSCH2 value. 47
 Validate that the BER Measurements show no errors  48
 CMP-Uncompressed-BER-PDSCH0 = 0 49
 CMP-Uncompressed-BER-PDSCH1 = 0 50
 CMP-Uncompressed-BER-PDSCH2 = 0 51
 CMP-Compressed-BER-PDSCH0 = 0 52
 CMP-Compressed-BER-PDSCH1 = 0 53
 CMP-Compressed-BER-PDSCH2 = 0 54
 55
G. Test Requirement (expected result)  56
1. All validation steps above are within expected ranges or correctly match the expected outcome. 57

3.2.3.4 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Delay Management (DLM) 11
This section describes conformance test cases for O-RU Delay Management. 12
The test setup for these test cases is shown in 2.1.  13
When performing the conformance test cases for scenario class Delay Management it does not matter which timing 14
method is used. The different timing methods are described in section 2.3.2, 2.3.3, 2.3.4 and 2.3.5 in the CUS 15
Specification [2] 16
Delay Management downlink tests will test whether the O-RU can accurately transmit data when C and U plane 17
messages are received at the extreme ends of their respective reception windows. Uplink tests will test whether the O-18
RU can accurately transmit received data to the CUSM-E when the CUSM-E transmits uplink C-Plane messages within 19
the correct uplink reception window.  It also tests whether the O-RU sends its U-Plane messages within the correct 20
reception window. 21
Figure 3.2.3.4-1 shows a simplified timing relation for the C- and U-Plane messages for downlink. 22
The size of the control plane reception window on the O-RU will be: (T2a_max_up +Tcp_adv_dl) – (T2a_min_up 23
+Tcp_adv_dl) = C-Plane reception window.   The start-point (before t=0) will be: T2a_max_up + Tcp_adv_dl = start of 24
C-Plane transmission window. 25
The size of the reception window for the user plane will be: T2a_max_up - T2a_min_up. The start-point (before t=0) 26
will be T2a_max_up. 27
As an example, if the values are set such as T2a_max_up = 264 µs, Tcp_adv_dl = 63 µs and T2a_min_up = 53 µs, then 28
the C-Plane reception window would be 211 µs, the start of C-plane transmission window would be 327 us, the U-plane 29
reception window would 211 µs and the start of U-plane transmission window would be 264 µs. 30
 31
 32

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       113
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00

Figure 3.2.3.4-1 Simplified Timing for Downlink 2

The Delay Management uplink test cases for the O-RU will test that if the C-Plane fronthaul messages is received with 4
respective reception window then the corresponding U-Plane messages will be sent in the O-RU’s transmission 5
window. 6
Figure 3.2.3.4-2 shows a simplified timing relation for the C-Plane and U-Plane messages for uplink. 7
Similar to the downlink case, the size of the control plane reception window is T2a_max_cp_ul - T2a_min_cp_ul . The 8
start-point of (before t=0) of the C-plane reception window is T2a_max_cp_ul. 9
The size of the transmission window for the user plane will be: Ta3_max_up  - Ta3_min_up. The start-point (after t=0) 10
will be Ta3_min_up. 11
If we follow the same example values as the ones set in the downlink case, the C-plane reception window would be 211 12
µs, the start-point of the C-plane reception window would be 274 µs, the U-plane transmission window would be 70 µs 13
and the start-point of the U-plane transmission window would be 20 µs.  14

3.2.3.4.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class DLM Test #1: Downlink – Positive testing 9
A. Test Description and Applicability 10
This test is MANDATORY. 11
 12
This test case will validate that the timing on the air interface is according to requirements specified in the 13
CUS Specification when the C-Plane and the U-Plane messages are received within the O-RU’s reception 14
windows. 15
 16
Four different test cases for downlink can be performed when the expected outcome is positive, i.e. the O-RU 17
shall be able to transmit the received U-Plane-data on the air interface.  These are shown in Figure 3.2.3.4-5.  18
Note that in these tests the C-Plane reception window may be applicable to the slot or symbol boundaries 19
depending on the Radio’s capabilities.  That is, in some radios, the C-Plane reception window is at the 20
beginning of each slot and all C-Plane messages will be sent at once within this window.  Other radios will 21
require C-Plane messages to be sent in a reception window for each symbol, In all cases U-Plane messages will 22
be sent during reception windows corresponding to each symbol regardless of whether the radio has large 23
enough buffers to store U-Plane data for multiple symbols. 24
 25

1st case “C-Plane Early – U-Plane Early”; the C-Plane message is received by the O-RU at the beginning of 4
the reception window for the C-Plane messages (indicated with small green box in figure 2.5). The 5
corresponding U-Plane data is received in the beginning of the reception window for the U-Plane messages 6
(indicated with small blue box in figure), i.e. Tcp_adv_dl later. 7
2nd case “C-Plane Early – U-Plane Late”; the C-Plane message is received by the O-RU at the beginning of 8
the reception window for the C-Plane messages. The corresponding U-Plane data is received earliest Tcp_adv_dl 9
after the C-Plane message i.e. in the end of the U-Plane reception window. 10
3rd case “C-Plane Late – U-Plane Early”; the C-Plane message is received by the O-RU at the end of the 11
reception window for the C-Plane messages.  The corresponding U-Plane data is received earliest Tcp_adv_dl 12
after the C-Plane message i.e. in the end of the reception window. 13
4th case “C-Plane Late – U-Plane Late”; this case is greyed out in the figure since it will in practice be the 14
same case as number 3, the U-Plane message cannot be received later than it is in case 3. 15
 16

The O-RU must have a conducted antenna port (or TAB connector) to be connected to a signal analyzer.  The 19
reception windows will be calculated and used by the CUSM-E based on the delay parameters reported by the 20
radio on the M-Plane. 21
 22
C. Test Methodology 23
 24
a. Initial Conditions 25
Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 26
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1. Connect the RF Signal 27

Analyzer to the O-RU antenna port. Determine the correct reception windows the radio claims to 1
support using delay management parameters repowered by the radio, 2
b. Procedure 3
Configure the CUSM-ECUSM-E to send C-Plane and U-Plane messages so these messages are received 4
within the reception windows for respective plane according to the three cases (1..3) described in figure 5
above. NOTE: Make sure that the C-Plane message is received at least Tcp_adv_dl earlier then the 6
corresponding U-Plane message(s) by the O-RU. 7
 8
On the RF-signal-analyzer observe the received signal and compare the decoded data on the selected test 9
symbol to the send PN23 sequence for that symbol. 10

3.2.3.4.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class DLM Test #2: Uplink – Positive testing 15
A. Purpose and Description  16
This test is MANDATORY. 17
 18
This test case will validate that the transmission of the U-Plane data in uplink direction are transmitted correctly by 19
the O-RU within its transmission window.  The CUSM-E will send C-Plane messages at both ends of the C-Plane 20
reception window specified by the radio using the M-Plane (Two tests).  The C-Plane messages will describe a test 21
frame as shown above.  The frame will have one designated symbol in each slot (not containing DMRS 22
information).  The C-Plane message will ask the radio to send that symbol’s data from each slot. 23
 24
After the correct C-Plane messages are sent the CUSM-E will trigger the signal generator to send a valid test signal 25
to the radio’s RF port.  This signal will contain a new, known PN23 sequence in the same symbol (per slot) 26
designated by the C-Plane messages. 27
 28
The positive test outcome for these uplink test cases is that the corresponding U-Plane data for a specific C-Plane 29
message is transmitted within the O-RU’s transmission window IF the C-Plane message was received within the O-30
RU’s reception window as shown in Figure 3.2.3.4-6 31
.  The data will be transmitted to the radio by an external signal generator and the uplink signal will be as described 32
above.  The test data sent by the signal generator will contain a known, new PN23 sequence in one symbol of each 33
slot.  The CUSM-E will expect to receive the same data for the correct symbol in each slot. 34

cases shown in figure above. 31

respectively. 36

3.2.3.5 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Transport (TRN) 1

3.2.3.6 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class LAA (LAA) 3
The purpose of this section is to specify LAA test cases to test the compliance of the O-RU to the O-RAN 4
specifications. Although in LAA operation, regular C-Plane and U-Plane messages (used for operation over licensed 5
spectrum as well) are transmitted over the fronthaul interface between the O-DU and O-RU, there exist additional C-6
Plane messages that are required specifically for LAA operation over unlicensed spectrum. These additional C-Plane 7
messages are based on Section type 7 and are communicated in both UL and DL directions between the O-DU and O-8
RU.  9
 10
The LAA test cases only focus on LAA-related messages and operations. Other testing aspects that are applicable to 11
LAA and non-LAA technologies (e.g., delay management, beamforming, compression, etc.) are not considered in this 12
section; Please refer to other sections in the conformance test specification document. 13
 14
LAA considered in this section is based on 3GPP Rel. 13, which only considers downlink transmission on the 15
unlicensed spectrum (i.e., uplink transmission goes on the licensed component carrier). Hence, all the test cases in this 16
section will consider downlink operation only. This includes DL U-Plane messages and DL/UL C-Plane messages. Note 17
also that UL C-Plane messages only exist in LAA technology. 18
 19
The LAA test cases for the O-RU test if the O-RU is capable of conforming with the CUSM-E instructions in terms of: 20
1) Correctly performing the listen-before-talk (LBT) procedure (i.e., managing the congestion window). 21
2) Timely data transmission based on the spectrum sensing outcome. 22
3) Timely deferring from occupying the spectrum based on the messages received from the O-DU. 23
 24
On the other hand, testing O-RU capabilities (e.g., spectrum sensing) is out of scope of this specifications since it’s not 25
directly related to the O-RAN fronthaul interface.  26
 27
3.2.3.6.1 CU-DU-LAA-CWM Test #1: LBT PDSCH Configuration and Response  28
A. Test Description and Applicability 29
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY.  The test must be executed if the O-RU supports LAA. 30
This test validates that the O-RU is capable of the following functions 31
 Correctly receiving and interpreting C-Plane messages (Section Type 7 and specifically laaMsgType 0) 32
from the TER to correctly perform LBT.  33
 Correctly receiving U-Plane data from the TER and correctly processes the data (i.e., drop it or transmit 34
it) based on the LBT outcome.  35
 Correctly performing LBT and correctly generating C-Plane messages to inform the TER about the LBT 36
outcomes using Section Type 7 and specifically laaMsgType 2. 37
 38
This test assumes that the O-RU is capable of processing Section Type 1 C-plane messages and its corresponding 39
U-plane messages. 40
It applies to the following CUS fronthaul specification sections: 41
 Section 5.4.2 for layout of C-Plane messages, in particular Section Type 1 and Section Type 7. 42
 Section 5.4.5.14 for applicability of “laaMsgType” (LAA message type) 43
 Section 5.4.5.15 for applicability of “laaMsgLen” (LAA message length) 44
 Section 5.4.5.16 for applicability of “lbtHandle” (LBT Handle) 45
 Section 5.4.5.17 for applicability of “lbtDeferFactor” (listen-before-talk defer factor) 46
 Section 5.4.5.18 for applicability of “lbtBackoffCounter” (listen-before-talk backoff counter) 47
 Section 5.4.5.19 for applicability of “lbtOffset” (listen-before-talk offset) 48
 Section 5.4.5.20 for applicability of “MCOT” (maximum channel occupancy time) 49
 Section 5.4.5.21 for applicability of “lbtMode” (LBT Mode) 50
 Section 5.4.5.22 for applicability of “lbtPdschRes” (LBT PDSCH Result) 51
 Section 5.4.5.23 for applicability of “sfStatus” (subframe status) 52

 Section 5.4.5.25 for applicability of “initialPartialSF” (Initial partial SF) 1

 Table 8-2 for mandatory capabilities 3
 4
The purpose of this test is to: 5
 Validate that the O-RU can correctly interpret C-Plane messages by correctly performing LBT.  6

outcome to the TER based on the description in Section 5.3.4 in [2] 29

to enable O-RU Conformance Testing. 37

LBT.  39

                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00  LTE UC-Plane O-DU Scenario Class LAA (LAA) described in clause 3.2.3.6 1  LTE UC-Plane O-DU Scenario Class Section Type 3 described in clause 3.2.3.8 2  3 Subsequently, LTE-only specific generic test cases are explicitly covered in the subsections below.  One of the key 4 differences applicable for LTE specific test cases as compared to NR is due to the explicit precoding behavior supported 5 by some of the transmission modes for LTE.  6 In particular, for a Category B O-RU to implement precoding for LTE TM2-TM4, specific C-Plane instructions need to 7 be provided to the O-RU from the O-DU.  This specific aspect of the O-RAN fronthaul interface is enabled by the 8 section extension = 0x3 described in the CUS Plane specification [2]. 9 For all the test cases described in this section: 10  Downlink tests will use a standard 3GPP E-TM1.1 test frame for FDD (Section 6.1.1.1 TS136.141-1) as shown in 11 Figure 3.2.3.7-1. 12  13 Figure 3.2.3.7-1 3GPP E-TM1.1 Test Frame for FDD 14  15  Uplink tests will use a standard 3GPP UL RMC Configuration definition for FDD (TS36.521-1) and power levels 16 30dB above Reference Sensitivity power level as shown in Figure 3.2.3.7-2 UL RMC Configuration for FDD: 17  18  19 Figure 3.2.3.7-2 UL RMC Configuration for FDD 20 All the downlink tests in this section use a 3GPP test wave form LTE Test Model 1.1 (E-TM1.1) with 20 MHz 21 Bandwidth as described in TS 36.141 section 6.1.1.1.   22 There are several variations on this test signal depending on the capabilities of the radio.  If for example the radio does 23 not support the bandwidth used in the example tests as reported in the M-plane it will be up to the test developer to 24 modify their tests to adapt to the radio.  The test is expected to follow the same spirit as the tests in this document may 25 have to be changed. 26 Likewise, all uplink tests in this section use a 3GPP test waveform described in 36.141 section A1.  As with downlink 27 tests if the radio does not support this signal it is up to the test developer to modify the parameters of the test without 28 changing the spirit of the test. 29 3.2.3.7.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Base 3GPP DL 30 A. 3.2.3.7.3 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Extended 3GPP UL – Resource Allocation 18
A. Test Description and Applicability 19
This test is MANDATORY. 20
 21
The purpose of this test is to validate correct uplink operation of the O-RU using 3GPP Reference Sensitivity 22
level definition (Section 7.2 TS 136.141) of the Conducted Receiver Characteristic Test section (Section 7 TS 23
36.104) and power Levels at least 30 dB above Reference Sensitivity power Level described in E-TM1.1.  This 24
is to improve the likelihood that all data will be received by the radio correctly since we are not interested in 25
testing receiver sensitivity but only the O-RAN protocol compliance.  26
 27
Under those conditions, 3GPP compliant O-RU should deliver uplink U-Plane information that matches with 28
the uplink signal.  29
 30
The TER (Test Equipment, O-RU) generates an uplink signal on the antenna connector or TAB connector, 31
together with the corresponding C-Plane messages on the Fronthaul interface. The TER will capture the U-32
Plane messages generated by the DUT and validate if the payload matches with the uplink signal.  33
 34
This test is applicable for both Type A and Type B radios. 35
 36
It applies to the following CUS fronthaul specification sections 37
 Section 5.4.2 for layout of C-Plane message, in particular Section Type 1 38
 Section 6.3.2 for U-Plane message layout 39
 Section 6.3.3 for coding of applicable Information Elements 40

MHz Bandwidth as described by E-TM1.1. 45

 The signal analyzer must have the ability to decode the downlink shared channel. 47

3.2.3.7.5 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class With Precoding (WPR) TxD 23
A. Test Description and Applicability 24
This test is MANDATORY. 25
 26
The purpose of this test is to validate the correct implementation of transmit diversity of a Category B O-RU with 27
two antenna ports.  TxD uses TM2 (transmission Mode 2).  For TxD, information for 2 layers are packed into a 28
PRB for transmission from O-DU and are unpacked at the O-RU.  TxD precoding is applied based on the C Plane 29
configuration before RF transmission.  30
 31
Using a standard E-TM1.1 test frame for FDD the CUSM-E (i.e., O-RAN interface of the TER described in section 32
3.2.2) will generate C-Plane and U-Plane messages that require the O-RU to transmit on the downlink the standard 33
E-TM1.1 signal.   34
 35
This test is applicable for Type B radios only. 36
 37
B. Test Entrance Criteria 38
 39
 The O-RU must support the default parameters in section 3.2.1 of this document.  The test bandwidth is 20 40
MHz Bandwidth as described by E-TM1.1. 41

3.2.3.7.6 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class With Precoding (WPR) SM 31
A. Test Description and Applicability 32
This test is MANDATORY. 33
 34
The purpose of this test is to validate the correct implementation of TM3/4 Spatial Multiplexing transmission mode 35
for a Category B O-RU with two antenna ports.  For TM3/4 Spatial Multiplexing, information for 2 layers are 36
packed into a PRB for transmission from O-DU and are unpacked at the O-RU, subsequently TM3/4 based 37
precoding is applied based on the C Plane configuration before over the air transmission.  38
 39
Using a standard E-TM1.1 test frame for FDD the CUSM-E (i.e., O-RAN interface of the TER described in section 40
3.2.2) will generate C-Plane and U-Plane messages that require the O-RU to transmit on the downlink the standard 41
E-TM1.1 signal.   42
 43
This test is applicable for Type B radios only. 44
 45

3.2.3.8 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Section Type 3 (ST3) 40
This section will specify the test scenarios to validate the correct decoding of C-Plane messages with section type 3. 41

3.2.3.8.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class ST3 Test #1: NR PRACH 43
A. Test Description and Applicability {MANDATORY} 44
This test is MANDATORY. 45
This test will validate the correct decoding of C-Plane messages containing section type 3 in 5G NR scenario by 46
testing the correct detection of a PRACH signal.  47
TER will setup the signal generator with a PRACH test waveform according to TS 38.141-1 section 8.4.1 and A.6. 48
The test waveform will contain the same preamble ID repeated by following the timing offset scheme specified in 49
the figures 8.4.1.4.2-2 or 8.4.1.4.2-3 TS 38.141-1 depending on the selected PRACH format. 50

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       131
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
This is an example for FR1 – SCS=30 KHz – BW=100MHz – Format A3, at each occasion the time offset of the 1
same preamble index (selected according to table A.6-1 TS 38.141.1) is incremented by 100nsec starting from 0 up 2
to 800nsec (9 occasions per frame). Each PRACH occasion is at the beginning of the first nine used sub-frames. 3
The scheme is repeated every frame. 4
 5
 6
Figure 3.2.3.8-1 FR1 SCS 30Kz 100MHz Format A3 7
 8
According to the PRACH waveform setting, the TER will generate a corresponding sequence of C-Plane messages 9
with section type 3. By the corresponding U-Plane messages in the uplink direction, the TER will try to detect the 10
presence of the corresponding preamble at the expected timing offset and calculate the probability of detection Pd 11
according to the definition in TS38.141-1 section 8.4.1.1.  12
The signal will be exercised at only one O-RU port without adding any external AWGN power level or multipath 13
fading profile and at a power level avoiding detection errors due to poor SNR (rule described in the sub-section C 14
of this scenario class). 15
B. Test Entrance Criteria 16
O-RU must have a conducted antenna port (FR1) or TAB connector. 17
By the M-plane, TER will detect all the supported SCSs, FFT sizes and carrier bandwidths by the O-RU. To test 18
the correct interpretation of section type 3, it is assumed that only one combination of the three above parameters 19
supported by the O-RU is enough to validate the test. TER shall generate C-Plane messages according to one of the 20
PRACH formats in table A.6-1 TS 38.141. TER will choose the format either according to the manufacturer 21
declaration item D.103 “PRACH format and SCS” in TS 38.141-1 or according to the format information obtained 22
by the M-plane in case O-RU implements this feature. If more formats are claimed, only one shall be selected to 23
reduce the test time, preference will be given to a format specified in Table A.6.1 TS 38.141. It is assumed that the 24
O-RU manufacturer will support at least one in that table. For the case of long preambles, it is assumed format 0 is 25
always supported since the only one shown in the table A.6-1 TS 38.141.  26
C. Test Methodology 27
a. Initial Conditions 28
The O-RU is synchronized using G.8275.1. The signal generator is connected to the antenna port under test and 29
synchronized to the same frequency reference of the O-RU. CUSM-E has completed the activation of one carrier on 30
the O-RU port and enabled one endpoint supporting section type 3. The endpoint is configured with no data 31
compression.  32
b. Procedure 33
1. Set signal generator power by the following method: 34

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       132
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
a. Select SNR from the scenario with two RX antennas and AWGN propagation condition in table 8.4.1.5-1
1, 8.4.1.5-2 or 8.4.1.5-3 TS 38.141-1 depending on the selected SCS and PRACH format. 2
b. Select the AWGN power level according to the configured SCS and channel bandwidth in table 3
8.4.1.4.2-1 TS 38.141-1and38.141-1and multiply by the PRACH signal bandwidth.  4
c. The output power will be given by the formula (SNR+Noise power – 3dB) rounded to the first decimal 5
digit. Extra 3dB are to compensate that SNR and noise power are selected from the two RX ports test 6
case and this test procedure requires only one O-RU port. 7
 8
For example, for the FR1 – SCS=30 KHz – BW=100MHz – Format A3 SNR is -13.5dB and noise level 9
is -70.1dBm/98.28MHz. signal generator power = -13.5dB -70.1dBm/98.28MHz*(139*30 KHz)-3dB 10
=-19.5dBm.  11
2. Set signal generator frequency offset to the central carrier frequency. PRACH will be mapped over frequency 12
according to msg1-FrequencyStart ( ) parameter equal to 0. PRACH format is set according to what TER 13
has selected from the manufacturer declarations. 14
3. Start PRACH waveform generation on the signal generator. 15
4. Configure CUSM-E to generate C-Plane section type 3 messages according to the PRACH occasions 16
described in subsection A and by the following approach: 17
a. In case of a PRACH format not including preamble repetitions, only one C-Plane message with one 18
section ID is generated per PRACH occasion. O-DU emulator will set “cpLength” field according to 19
table 6.3.3.1-2 or table 6.3.3.1-1 TS 38.211 and to the format specified in section 5.4.4.14 in [2] 20
“timeOffset” field will be set according to the PRACH occasion position inside the slot and by 21
following the format value specified section 5.4.4.12 CUS plane specification.  22
b. In case of a PRACH format with preamble repetitions, the implementation can be achieved by one C-23
Plane message with one section ID or by N number of C-Plane messages with one section ID 24
corresponding to the single PRACH repetition as described in section 5.3.2 CUS plane specification. 25
TER shall exercise both approaches and perform them in two separate test sessions by repeating steps 4 26
and 5. 27
c. In both scenarios “filterIndex” field is setup based on the PRACH format and according to table 5.9 28
of [2]and “beamId” field will set to 0 (no beamforming). 29
5. TER will perform PRACH detection per each PRACH occasion and compare the result with the expected 30
preamble ID and the expected timing offset. Since the external AWGN and fading generator are not present the 31
time error tolerance should be low, TER will use the time error tolerance in table 8.4.1.1-1 for AWGN case 32
according to the corresponding PRACH format and PRACH SCS. A counter of successful detections is 33
incremented at every matching. The probability of detection is given by the ratio between that counter and the 34
number of the expected received PRACH occasions within the test time. 35
6. Repeat the test procedure by setting msg1-FrequencyStart ( ) parameter to the right edge of the 36
configured carrier bandwidth in order to exercise a different frequency offset number in section type 3. 37
D. Pass/Fail Criteria (expected result) 38
1. Test is pass if the probability of detection is 100%. 39
 40

3.2.4 FR1 FDD Non-conducted OTA Signal Tests 16

Conducted-Signal Tests.  Only the setup for the tests are different reflecting the difference between non-conductive and 19
conductive mode testing.  20
3.2.4.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming (BFM)  21
This section describes the beamforming conformance testing for ORAN fronthaul interface. The tests do not aim to test 22
the O-RU beamforming performance or capabilities but to test that the O-RU under test focuses the RF energy or 23
sensitivity into a specific direction and with a specific granularity following the O-DU emulator (i.e., O-RAN interface 24
of the TER described in section 2.1) C-Plane messages.  25
Unless stated otherwise in a test case, the following statements apply to all the test cases defined in this section: 26
 It is based on Over-the-Air (OTA) testing with a setup such as described in Section 2.1 and it may be applied to 27
any O-RU DUTs, whether the O-RU DUTs have conducted antenna ports or TAB connectors or not. 28
 29
 It applies to Type A and Type B O-RU DUTs. 30
 31
 It applies to LTE and/or 5G New Radio O-RU DUTs.  In both cases, precoding is not required in any test case.   32
 33
 If O-RU DUT supports Analog Beamforming (i.e. time domain beamforming), all the U-Plane test frames are 34
defined by segmenting the Stock Test A: 1 section per symbol.  The definition of this Stock Test A can be 35
found in Figure 3.2.1.1-2 and the description accompanying this Figure.  Each slot shall include multiple 36
sections (one per symbol within the slot) and only one beam at a time (i.e. one beamId at a time) and therefore 37
only one beam can be tested per slot. 38
 39
 If O-RU DUT supports Digital Beamforming (i.e. frequency domain beamforming), all the U-Plane test frames 40
are defined by segmenting the Stock Test B: 2 sections per symbol definition as shown in Figure 3.2.1.1-2.  41
Each slot shall include multiple sections (two per symbol within the slot) and only one beam per section at a 42
time (i.e. one beamId at a time) and therefore up to two different beams can be tested per slot. 43
 44
 If O-RU DUT supports multiple polarizations, it is up to the TER to determine if the testing is carried out for 45
each polarization separately or multiple polarizations at the same time. In any case, it is important to guarantee 46
that the correct eAxC_ID for the correct polarization (or polarizations) is exercised.  47
 48

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       135
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
 For O-RU DUT that support LTE:  1

20MHz bandwidth (100 RB) as shown in Figure 3.2.3.2-1. 3

B. Test Description and Applicability 32
This test is MANDATORY. 33
 34
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with no beamforming 35
(beamId=0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 36
 37
B. Test Entrance Criteria 38
 Manufacturers’ declaration that defines list of beam directions when O-RU DUT is operating with no 39
beamforming.  40
 41
C. Test Methodology 42
 43
a. Initial Conditions 44
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 45
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  46
 Ensure that the test antenna/s and TER equipment is calibrated within acceptable tolerance.  47
 Place the test antenna/s to a defined position within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.2 and configure 48
the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the transmitted 49
signal. 50
 Place the O-RU into a test calibrated point within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.2. 51
 Align the O-RU to a default initial position, i.e. align the O-RU to the origin of coordinates of the declared 52
coordinate reference point and orientation in the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.2.  53
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.  54
 55
b. Procedure 56
f. Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal described above in the O-DU 57
emulator.   58

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       137
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
g. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the 1
signal and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (DL-SCH 2
and DCI) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 3
h. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing 4
windows described in section 3.2.1.1.2.   5
i. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to 6
demodulate and decode the test frame. 7
j. Measure any metric/s that allows for extracting the transmitted beam direction from a single measurement, 8
i.e. transform-based techniques, or take as many measurements of any metric/s from multiple angles, by 9
for example rotating the O-RU, that allows for extracting beam direction from multiple measurement, i.e. 10
beam scanning. 11

 13
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  14
4. The signal measured by the signal analyzer at the expected transmitted beam direction should satisfy a basic 15
3GPP signal performance requirement for this radio category (i.e., EVM). 16
5. The test frame received at the expected transmitted beam direction by the signal analyzer should be the same as 17
the signal described above and should contain all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data. 18
6. The extracted beam direction is defined as the direction where the best metric/s were measured (i.e. best EVM, 19
power, SNR, etc.) and should match the expected beam direction for the expected no beamforming within a 20
tolerance defined by the manufacturer.  21

3.2.4.2.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP UL – No Beamforming 23
A. Test Description and Applicability 24
This test is MANDATORY. 25
 26
 27
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can receive a basic 3GPP test frame with no beamforming 28
(beamId=0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 29
 30
 31
B. Test Entrance Criteria 32
 Manufacturers’ declaration that defines list of beam directions when O-RU DUT is operating with no 33
beamforming.  34
 35
C. Test Methodology 36
 37
a. Initial Conditions 38
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 39
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  40
 Ensure that the test antenna/s and TER equipment is calibrated within acceptable tolerance.  41
 Place the test antenna/s to a defined position within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.2 and configure 42
the signal source with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and generate the test signal. 43
 Place the O-RU into a test calibrated point within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.2. 44
 Align the O-RU to a default initial position, i.e. align the O-RU to the origin of coordinates of the declared 45
coordinate reference point and orientation in the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.2.  46
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.  47
 48
b. Procedure 49
g. Build an appropriate test signal described above in the signal source of the TER.  50
h. Inject the test signal into the O-RU with the application of an initial beam direction. This initial beam 51
direction could be the boresight direction of the receiver antenna array. 52
i. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the 53
signal and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (UL-54
SCH) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 55
j. Play the C plane messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.2 while 56
also triggering the signal source.   57
k. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the DUT, allow it to create and send the U 58
plane messages to the O-DU. 59

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       138
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
l. Allow the O-DU to demodulate, decode and extract the payload and to measure and extract any required 1
metric/s from the received signal that will be used later to determine what is the best received direction. 2
m. Repeat the previous steps but now in step b apply a different beam direction when injecting the test signal 3
into the O-RU. Repeating the process for a number of different beam directions will exercise the reception 4
of the test signal from different beam directions. This allows to determine if the O-RU is really focusing 5
the sensitivity to the correct beam direction. 6
 7
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  8
1. The test frame received at the expected beam direction by the TER/O-DU should be the same as the signal 9
described above and should contain all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data. 10
2. The extracted beam direction is defined as the direction where the best metric/s were measured (i.e. best EVM, 11
power, SNR, etc.) and should match the expected beam direction for the expected no beamforming within a 12
tolerance defined by the manufacturer.  13

3.2.4.2.3 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Predefined-beam 15
Beamforming 16
A. Test Description and Applicability 17
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 18
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with predefined-beams 19
beamforming (beamId≠0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 20
The transmitted beam direction is measured for each indexed beam required in this measurement, see below. The 21
measured transmitted direction is compared to manufacturer-designated direction. Transmitted direction is defined 22
by extracting the beam direction. 23
Depending on the O-RU beamforming capabilities regarding the ability to generate “coarse”, “fine” and/or “beam 24
groups”, as defined in [2] Section 10.4.1.1. 25
 26
The elevation θ and azimuth Φ angles are defined as in [2] Section 10.4.1.1: 27
 28
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Predefined-beam Beamforming conformance test 29
might include multiple test that the O-RU must comply: 30
a. “Coarse” beamIds test:  31
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that are defined as coarse granularity (coarse beamIds) to the O-DU 32
emulator, the test should include the following beams: 33
1. A coarse beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles. 34
2. A coarse beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 35
3. A coarse beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 36
4. A coarse beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 37
5. A coarse beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 38
 39
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth (Φ) or elevation angle (θ), fewer than 5 beam angles will be measured. 40
 41
b.  “Fine” beamIds test:  42
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that are defined as fine granularity (fine beamIds) to the O-DU 43
emulator, the test should include the following beams: 44
1. A fine beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles. 45
2. A fine beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 46
3. A fine beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 47
4. A fine beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 48
5. A fine beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 49
 50
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth or elevation angle, fewer than 5 beam angles will be measured. 51
 52
c.  “beam-group” beamIds test:  53

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       139
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that belong to same and different beam-groups to the O-DU emulator, 1
the test should include the following beams: 2
1. All beams that belong to a beam-group with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) or elevation (θ) angles. 3
2. All beams that belong to a beam-group with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ). 4
3. All beams that belong to a beam-group with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ). 5
4. All beams that belong to a beam-group with maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 6
5. All beams that belong to a beam-group with minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 7
 8
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth or elevation angle, fewer than 5 beam-groups will be measured. 9
 10
