3.2.4.2.7 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Attribute-based Dynamic 26
Beamforming 27
A. Test Description and Applicability 28
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 29
 30
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with attributed-based dynamic 31
beamforming with one spatial stream (single eAxC).  32
 33
If the O-RU DUT supports Attribute based Dynamic Beamforming, this test is mandatory for the O-RU DUT to be 34
O-RAN conformant.   35
The transmitted beam direction and attributes are measured for each attributed beam required in this measurement, 36
see below. The measured transmitted direction and attributes, i.e. pointing azimuth and elevation angles, 37
beamwidths and sidelobe suppression, is compared to manufacturer-designated direction and attributes. 38
Transmitted direction and beam attributes are defined extracting the beam properties. 39
The elevation θ and azimuth Φ angles are defined as in Section 10.4.1.1 of [2]. 40
 41
 42
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Attribute-based Dynamic Beamforming 43
conformance test should evaluate the following beams for the O-RU to comply: 44
f. An attribute-based beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles with any beamwidth and sidelobe 45
suppression supported by the O-RU under this beam direction. 46
g. An attribute-based beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle 47
(θ) with the widest beamwidth and lowest sidelobe suppression supported for this specific beam direction. 48
h. An attribute-based beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle 49
(θ) with the narrowest beamwidth and highest sidelobe suppression supported for this specific beam direction. 50
i. An attribute-based beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle 51
(θ) with the widest beamwidth and lowest sidelobe suppression supported for this specific beam direction. 52
j. An attribute-based beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle 53
(θ) with the narrowest beamwidth and highest sidelobe suppression supported for this specific beam direction. 54
 55
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth (Φ) or elevation angle (θ), fewer than 5 beam angles and attribute 56
configurations will be measured. 57
 58

 1
B. Test Entrance Criteria 2
 Manufacturers’ defined list of supported beam attributes that are supported by the O-RU and/or their 3
associated beam directions with antenna array characteristics. 4
 5
C. Test Methodology 6
 7
a. Initial Conditions 8
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 9
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  10
 Ensure that the test antenna/s and TER equipment is calibrated within acceptable tolerance.  11
 Place the test antenna/s to a defined position within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.2 and configure 12
the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the transmitted 13
signal. 14
 Place the O-RU into a test calibrated point within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.2. 15
 Align the O-RU to a default initial position, i.e. align the O-RU to the origin of coordinates of the declared 16
coordinate reference point and orientation in the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.2.  17
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.   18
 19
b. Procedure 20
a. Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal described above in the O-DU 21
emulator.   22
b. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal 23
and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by one or two sections (DL-SCH and DCI) 24
using section type 1 messages, the sections in the first symbol of the slot will contain section extension 25
extType=0x02 to convey the beam weights, it is not required that the next sections contain extension type 2 26
since the same beam IDs will not change along the slot.  If O-RU does not support a field, then its value 27
should be 0x0. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 28
c. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows 29
described in section 3.2.1.1.1.   30
d. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to 31
demodulate and decode the test frame. 32
e. Measure any metric/s that allows for extracting the transmitted beam attributes from a single measurement, 33
i.e. transform-based techniques, or take as many measurements of any metric/s from multiple angles, by for 34
example rotating the O-RU, that allows for extracting beam attributes from multiple measurement, i.e. 35
beam scanning. 36
 37
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  38
1. The signal measured at the expected beam direction by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal 39
performance requirement for this radio category (i.e., EVM). 40
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should be the same as the signal described above and should 41
contain all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data. 42
3. The extracted beam attributes are referenced from the measured beam direction where the best metric/s were 43
measured (i.e. best EVM, power, SNR, etc.) and should match the expected beam direction and attributes for the 44
beam under test within a tolerance defined by the manufacturer.  45

                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
B. Test Entrance Criteria 1
 Manufacturers’ defined list of supported beam attributes that are supported by the O-RU and/or their 2
associated beam directions with antenna array characteristics. 3
 4
C. Test Methodology 5
 6
a. Initial Conditions 7
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 8
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1. 9
 Ensure that the test antenna/s and TER equipment is calibrated within acceptable tolerance.  10
 Place the test antenna/s to a defined position within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.2 and configure 11
the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the transmitted 12
signal. 13
 Place the O-RU into a test calibrated point within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.2. 14
 Align the O-RU to a default initial position, i.e. align the O-RU to the origin of coordinates of the declared 15
coordinate reference point and orientation in the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.2.  16
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.   17
 18
b. Procedure 19
a. Build an appropriate test signal described above in the signal source of the TER.  20
b. Inject the test signal into the O-RU with the application of an initial beam direction. This initial beam 21
direction could be the boresight direction of the receiver antenna array. 22
c. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal 23
and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by one or two sections (UL-SCH) using section 24
type 1 messages, the sections in the first symbol of the slot will contain section extension extType=0x02 to 25
convey the beam weights, it is not required that the next sections contain extension type 2 since the same 26
beam IDs will not change along the slot. If O-RU does not support a field, then its value should be 0x0. No 27
section type zero messages will be used for this test. 28
d. Play the C plane messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.12. while 29
also triggering the signal source.   30
e. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the DUT, allow it to create and send the U 31
plane messages to the O-DU and for the O-DU to demodulate, decode and extract the payload. 32
f. Repeat the previous steps but now in step b apply a different beam direction when injecting the test signal 33
into the O-RU. Repeating the process for a number of different beam directions will exercise the reception of 34
the test signal from different beam directions. This allows to determine if the O-RU is really focusing the 35
sensitivity to the correct beam direction with the correct beam attributes. 36
 37
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  38
1. The test frame received at the expected beam direction by the TER/O-DU should be the same as the signal 39
described above and should contain all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data. 40
2. The extracted beam attributes are referenced from the measured beam direction where the best metric/s were 41
measured (i.e. best EVM, power, SNR, etc.) and should match the expected beam direction and attributes for 42
the beam under test within a tolerance defined by the manufacturer.  43

A. Test Description and Applicability 47
This Test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 48
 49
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with channel-information-based 50
beamforming with multiple spatial streams from multiple users (i.e. MU-MIMO). 51
 52
For Category A radios, the test is for each polarization separately and consequently either different or same channel 53
models can be defined for each of the polarization. For Category B, same channel might be used for both 54
polarizations and the test might measure each polarization separately. 55
The transmitted beam direction is measured for each scenario required in this measurement.  The measured 56
transmitted direction is extracted from the decoded received signal in the TER. Transmitted direction is defined by 57

A scenario where two spatial streams, or eAxC flows, are generated for two users (one layer each) with M 10 antennas ports or TAB connectors. The O-DU will report to the O-RU via C plane messages an channel 11 estimate 𝐻 ≜  [ℎଵଵ, . . . , ℎଵெ, ℎଶଵ, . . . , ℎଶெ]∈ ℂଶ௫, which is the effective channel as seen by the antennas 12 representing the multiple UEs, which are spaced sufficiently such that the O-RU can effectively equalize out 13 the interference between the users.. The O-RU will calculate and apply the beamweight matrix 𝐺 ≜14  [𝑔ଵଵ, . . . , 𝑔ଵெ, 𝑔ଶଵ, . . . , 𝑔ଶெ] ∈ ℂெ௫ଶ in such that the received signal at the users is the same as the generated in the 15 O-DU. It is up to the O-RU on how to calculate the beamforming weights, for example Zero-forcing, 16 regularized zero-forcing / MMSE, etc.   17  18 If O-RU supports Analog Beamforming (Time Domain Beamforming), the test should not apply any analog 19 beamforming or time domain beamforming. In this case, M is not the number of antennas ports or TAB connectors 20 but the number of TRX channels supported by the O-RU. 21  22 B. 3.2.5 FR1 TDD Conducted Signal Tests 1
3.2.5.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class NR testing Generic (NRG)  2
All TDD tests described in this section will be combined UL and DL tests (i.e., a single test frame describing both up 3
link and down link). The default test frame used in this section is described in section 3.2.1.1.3 of this document. There 4
are several variations on this test signal depending on the capabilities of the radio.  If the radio does not support the 5
numerology used in the example tests as reported in the M-plane it will be up to the test developer to modify their tests 6
to adapt to the radio.  This can usually be accomplished by using stock test patterns described above.  The test is 7
expected to follow the same spirit as the tests in this document but things like symbol numbers, number of PRBs, etc. 8
may have to be changed. 9
3.2.5.1.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Base 3GPP DL/UL 10
A. Test Description and Applicability 11
This test is MANDATORY. 12
 13
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can meet the most basic uplink and downlink requirements for O-14
RAN fronthaul using a TDD signal.  Subsequent tests will build on this to exercise additional capabilities of the 15
Fronthaul. 16
 17
Using the standard TDD test frame described in section 3.2.1.1.3 the O-DU emulator (i.e., O-RAN interface of the 18
TER described in section 2.1) will generate C-Plane and U-Plane messages that require the O-RU to transmit on the 19
down link and uplink the default signal.   20
 21
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit and receive  a basic 3GPP, TDD test frame using the 22
default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.5 of this document (or a similar 3GPP waveform) except only one spatial 23
stream on one antenna will be used.  This test is applicable for Category A and Category B radios (No precoding 24
is required).  As per section 3.2.1.1.3 this test requires non-zero data (PN23 Sequence) to populate all allocated 25
resource blocks.  This configuration corresponds to stock data section A in all symbols that do not contain 26
PDCCH channels. 27
 28
B. Test Entrance Criteria 29
The O-RU must support the default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.3 of this document.  The test numerology will be 30
30 KHz subcarrier spacing and 100 MHz Bandwidth as described by TM-FR1-TM1.1.  It will be for 5G New 31
Radio only. The radio must have conducted antenna ports (FR1) or TAB connectors. 32
 33
The O-RU must have a conducted antenna port (or TAB connector) to be connected to a signal analyzer and signal 34
source.  It must also support the default parameters defined in section 3.2.1.1.3 above. 35
 36
C. Test Methodology 37
a. Initial Conditions 38
Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 39
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  Connect the signal analyser and 40
signal source to the O-RU antenna ports and configure the analyser with any set-up information needed to 41
allow it to synch and demodulate the transmitted signal.   42
b. Procedure 43
Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the signal described above in section 3.2.1.1.3 in the CUSM 44
emulator.  Built the appropriate test frame (uplink slots) for the signal source. Use the CUSM emulator 45
control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal. Every symbol used in 46
the test should be described by a single section (DL-SCH that are used for the test, DMRS and DCI) using 47
section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test.  Encapsulate the IQ data 48
in U-Plane messages for downlink slots only. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows 49
described in section 3.2.1.1.3.  Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal 50
analyser and allow it to demodulate and decode the test frame.  It will be the responsibility of the TER’s 51
signal analyser and source to coordinate downlink and uplink TDD transmissions.  The CUSM Emulator of 52
the TER is responsible for receiving uplink U-Plane messages, extracting IQ and decoding it to bits which 53
can be compared to those sent by the signal source. 54
 55

 20

B. Test Entrance Criteria 25
The O-RU must support the default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.3 of this document.  The test numerology will be 26
30 KHz subcarrier spacing and 100 MHz Bandwidth as described in section 3.2.1.1.3.  It will be for 5G New 27
Radio only. The radio must have conducted antenna ports (FR1) or TAB connectors. 28
 29
The O-RU must have a conducted antenna port (or TAB connector) to be connected to a signal analyzer.  It must 30
also support the default parameters defined in section 3.2.1.1.1 above. 31
 32
C. Test Methodology 33
a. Initial Conditions 34
Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 35
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  Connect the signal analyser to the 36
O-RU antenna port and configure the analyser with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and 37
demodulate the transmitted signal.  Connect the signal source to the O-RU antenna port and configure it as 38
described below. 39
b. Procedure 40
Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the signal described above in section 3.2.1.1.3 in the CUSM 41
emulator. In this case use a PN23PN23 sequence for the downlink shared channel.  Build the appropriate 42
test frame (uplink slots) for the signal source. Use the CUSM emulator control interface to build the 43
appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the uplink and downlink signals. Every symbol used in the test 44
should be described by a single section (DL-SCH that are used for the test, DMRS and DCI) using section 45
type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test.  Encapsulate the IQ data in U-46
Plane messages for downlink slots only. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows 47
described in section 3.2.1.1.3.  Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal 48
analyser and allow it to demodulate and decode the test frame.  It will be the responsibility of the TER’s 49
signal analyser and source to coordinate downlink and uplink TDD transmissions.  The CUSM Emulator of 50
the TER is responsible for receiving uplink U-Plane messages, extracting IQ and decoding it to bits which 51
can be compared to those sent by the signal source. 52
 53
For the downlink slots and symbols: Every allocated (see below) symbol should be described by a single 54
section (DL-SCH and DCI) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for 55
this test.  Symbol #3 of each downlink slot should be Stock data section type  “D” as shown in section 56
3.2.1.1.5 above. The control plane message for symbol #3 will only include PRBs number 5 through 23.  57
This C-Plane message will have the rb bit set to one for this section. All other DL-SCH symbols will not 58

3.2.5.1.4 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Extended using SymInc parameter 3GPP DL/UL – 41
Resource Allocation 42
A. Test Description and Applicability 43
This test is MANDATORY. 44
 45
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can accurately interpret C-Plane resource allocation messages with 46
the SymInc parameter set, transfer U-Plane data into the correct resource blocks and transmit this data accurately in 47
the downlink and interpret and capture the correct resource blocks in the uplink with the SymInc parameter set.    48
This test uses a PN23 sequence in all test PDSCH sections. 49
 50
Using the standard TDD test frame described in section 3.2.1.1.3 the O-DU emulator (i.e., O-RAN interface of the 51
TER described in section 2.1) will generate C-Plane and U-Plane messages that require the O-RU to transmit on the 52
down link and uplink the specified signal using the SymInc bit in both uplink and downlink.   53
 54
Only one spatial stream on one antenna will be used.  This test is applicable for Category A and Category B radios 55
(No precoding is required).  All downlink user data in this test will be a PN23 sequence and all uplink user data 56
will also be a PN23 sequence. 57
 58
B. Test Entrance Criteria 59

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.

                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
The O-RU must support the default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.3 of this document.  The test numerology will be 1
30 KHz subcarrier spacing and 100 MHz Bandwidth as described in section 3.2.1.1.3.  It will be for 5G New Radio 2
only. The radio must have conducted antenna ports (FR1) or TAB connectors. 3
 4
The radio must support the SymInc Parameter as notified by the M-Plane.  The Signal Analyzer must have the 5
ability to decode the downlink shared channel. 6
 7
 8
C. Test Methodology 9
a. Initial Conditions 10
Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 11
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  Connect the signal analyser to the 12
O-RU antenna port and configure the analyser with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and 13
demodulate the transmitted signal.  Connect the signal source to the O-RU antenna port and configure it as 14
described below. 15
b. Procedure 16
Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the signal described above in section 3.2.1.1.3 in the CUSM 17
emulator. In this case use a PN23 sequence for the downlink shared channel.  Build the appropriate test 18
frame (uplink slots) for the signal source. Use the CUSM emulator control interface to build the appropriate 19
C-Plane messages that describe the uplink and downlink signals. Every symbol used in the test should be 20
described by a single section (DL-SCH that are used for the test, DMRS and DCI) using section type 1 21
messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test.  Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane 22
messages for downlink slots only. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described 23
in section 3.2.1.1.3.  Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyser and 24
allow it to demodulate and decode the test frame.  It will be the responsibility of the TER’s signal analyser 25
and source to coordinate downlink and uplink TDD transmissions.  The CUSM Emulator of the TER is 26
responsible for receiving uplink U-Plane messages, extracting IQ and decoding it to bits which can be 27
compared to those sent by the signal source. 28
 29
 30
For the downlink slots and symbols: Every symbol should be described by a single type 1 section (DL-31
SCH and DCI) except symbols #5 and #6 which will be used for the SymInc test. The data in these sections 32
must be a PN23 sequence using an initial seed of all ones. Each symbol should be a new PN23 sequence, 33
that is PRB 0 should contain the data from a new PN23 sequence for each symbol. Symbols number 5 and 6 34
should be stock data sections type “E” as shown above.  This stock data section consists of two adjacent 35
symbols each containing two sections.  The corresponding C-Plane message will contain 4 section IDs in a 36
single C-Plane message describing symbols #5 and #6.  The startSymbolId in the application header will be 37
symbol #5. The second section ID for symbol #5 will have the SymInc bit set informing the O-RU that the 38
next section will begin describing symbol #6. The corresponding U-Plane messages will be a new PN23 39
Sequence for each symbol (5 and 6). Additional sections should be included to describe the DCI symbols as 40
well as Reference Signals described in 38.141-1.  41
 42
For the uplink sections and symbols: Load uplink test waveform (G-FR1-A1-5 : SCS30k_51RB, 100 43
MHz) on the RF Signal Source.  Note this signal has a PN23 sequence as user data.  Configure the source to 44
generate a new PN23 sequence in symbols #5 and #6.  Configure the Signal Source to play test waveforms 45
on 10ms frame boundaries starting when it receives a trigger signal from the O-DU emulator that all C-46
Plane messages have been sent.  Ensure the O-RU and source are synchronized so downlink slots do not 47
conflict with uplink slots.  Load C-Plane message sequence on Test Equipment O-RU (TER) – Only 48
symbols #5 and #6 in each slot will be used in this test. All other symbols will contain either reference 49
signals or data but will not be considered part of the test.  These two symbols will be used to determine 50
whether the radio properly increments the current symbol ID when the symInc bit is set. The C-Plane 51
message for symbol #5 should have the symInc bit set.  This message should have a second section 52
describing symbol #6 (using the symInc mechanism).  All PRBs in each symbol will be requested (In the 53
example waveform 51 PRBs). 54
 55
Steps: 56
 Arm Test Equipment O-RU (TER) to capture DUT fronthaul Messages  57
 Launch test to play the C-Plane messages and the downlink U-Plane messages and trigger the 58
source to play the RF signal on a frame boundary.  59

Steps: 9
 Arm Test Equipment O-RU (TER) to capture DUT fronthaul Messages  10
 Launch test to play the C-Plane messages and the downlink U-Plane messages and trigger the 11
source to play the RF signal on a frame boundary.  12
 Play messages to the O-RU respecting the timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.1.  Repeat 13
the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to 14
demodulate and decode the frame. 15
 Record U-Plane messages from DUT for a complete frame and the eAxC corresponding to the 16
Antenna port  17
 Extract IQ information from the captured U-Plane messages 18
 Extract IQ information from the signal analyzer for downlink slots 19
 Extract Payload for both signals 20
 Compare payload binary sequences  21
 22
 23
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  24
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance requirement for 25
this radio category (i.e., EVM). 26
2. The signal extracted by the U-Plane messages (uplink) should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance 27
requirement for this radio category (i.e., EVM). 28
3. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should be the same as the signal described above.  If it contains 29
all the same PRB assignments and the correct PN23PN23 sequence as data, the downlink test passes. 30
4. The test frame extracted from the uplink U-Plane messages should be the same as the uplink signal described 31
above.  If it contains all the same PRB assignments and the correct PN23PN23 sequence as data, the uplink test 32
passes. 33
 34
 35
3.2.5.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming (BFM)  36
This section describes the beamforming conformance testing for ORAN fronthaul interface. The tests do not aim to test 37
the O-RU beamforming performance or capabilities but to test that the O-RU under test focuses the RF energy or 38
sensitivity into a specific direction and with a specific granularity following the O-DU emulator (i.e., O-RAN interface 39
of the TER described in section 2.1) C-Plane messages.  40
Unless stated otherwise in a test case, the following statements apply to all the test cases defined in this section: 41
 It is based on conducted testing with a setup such as described in Section 2.1 and it only applies to O-RU DUTs 42
that have conducted antenna ports or TAB connectors. 43
 44
 It applies to Type A and Type B O-RU DUTs. 45
 46
 It applies to LTE and/or 5G New Radio O-RU DUTs.  In both cases, precoding is not required in any test case.   47
 48
 If O-RU DUT supports Analog Beamforming (i.e. time domain beamforming), all the U-Plane test frames are 49
defined by segmenting the Stock Test A: 1 section per symbol.  The definition of this Stock Test A can be 50
found in Figure 3.2.1.1-2 and the description accompanying this Figure.  Each slot shall include multiple 51
sections (one per symbol within the slot) and only one beam at a time (i.e. one beamId at a time) and therefore 52
only one beam can be tested per slot. 53
 54
 If O-RU DUT supports Digital Beamforming (i.e. frequency domain beamforming), all the U-Plane test frames 55
are defined by segmenting the Stock Test B: 2 sections per symbol definition as shown in Figure 3.2.1.1-2.  56

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       159
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
Each slot shall include multiple sections (two per symbol within the slot) and only one beam per section at a 1
time (i.e. one beamId at a time) and therefore up to two different beams can be tested per slot. 2
 3
 If O-RU DUT supports multiple polarizations, it is up to the TER to determine if the testing is carried out for 4
each polarization separately or multiple polarizations at the same time. In any case, it is important to guarantee 5
that the correct eAxC_ID for the correct polarization (or polarizations) is exercised.  6
 7
 For O-RU DUT that support LTE:  8
o The tests will use a combination of Downlink and Uplink standard 3GPP LTE test frames. 9
o The Downlink part of the radio frame will follow E-TM1.1 test frame for LTE TDD (Section 6.1.1.1 10
TS136.141-1) with 20MHz bandwidth (100 RB). 11
o The Uplink part of the radio frame will use a standard 3GPP LTE UL FRC Configuration definition for 12
FDD (TS36.141-1) and power levels at least 30dB above Reference Sensitivity power level with 20MHz 13
bandwidth (100 RB). 14
o The Downlink symbols are allocated at slots 0 to 3, 8 to 13 and 18 to 19. Note that slots 3 and 13 have 15
symbols assigned as Guard Periods, symbols 4, 5 and 6, where no signal is transmitted or expected to be 16
received. 17
o The Uplink symbols are allocated at slots 4 to 7 and 14 to 17. 18
o The full test radio frame is shown in Figure : 19
 20 Figure 3.2.5.2-1 Combined DL and UL TDD 20 MHz 100 RB 21
If 20MHz is not supported by the O-RU DUT, then it will use the highest bandwidth supported by the O-22
RU DUT. 23
 24
 For O-RU DUT that support 5G NR:  25
o The tests will use a combination of Downlink and Uplink standard 3GPP 5G NR test frames. See 26
figure X. 27
o The Downlink part of the radio frame will use a standard 3GPP NR-FR1-TM1.1 test frame for TDD in 28
[19] (Section 4.9.2 TS138.141-1) of the Conducted Transmitter Characteristic Test section (Section 6 29
TS138.141-1) as described in section 3.2.1.1. The test numerology will be preferably 30KHz subcarrier 30
spacing and 100 MHz Bandwidth. If not supported, then it will use any other supported subcarrier 31
spacing and the highest bandwidth of the O-RU DUT. 32
o The Uplink part of the radio frame will use a standard 3GPP Reference Sensitivity level definition 33
(Section 7.2 and Annex A TS138.141-1) of the Conducted Receiver Characteristic Test section 34
(Section 7 TS 138.141) and power levels at least 30dB above Reference Sensitivity power level as 35
described in section 3.2.1.1.  The test numerology will be preferably 30kHz subcarrier spacing and 100 36
MHz Bandwidth, if supported. Otherwise, it will use any available subcarrier space and the highest 37
bandwidth supported by the O-RU DUT. 38
o The Downlink symbols are allocated at slots 0 to 7 and 10 to 17.  39
o The Uplink symbols are allocated at slots 7 to 9 and 17 to 19. 40
o Note that slots 7 and 17 have symbols allocated for Downlink, symbols 0 to 5, some other symbols 41
assigned as Guard Period where no signal is transmitted or expected to be received, symbols 6 to 9, 42
and finally some other symbols allocated for Uplink, symbols 10 to 13. 43
 44
 The O-RU DUT must: 45
o support the default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.1 of this document. 46
o have installed current release of shipping software.  47
o have at least two conducted antenna ports (or TAB connectors) to be connected to a signal analyzer. 48
Likewise, it must have at least two conducted antenna ports or TAB connectors to be connected to a signal 49
generator. 50
o be fully calibrated up to the antenna ports or (TAB connectors) (if needed). It is expected to be calibrated 51
by O-RU vendor prior to testing.  52
 53

 1
 The TER must: 2
o be capable of carrying out any signal processing required to generate and demodulate 3GPP compliant 3
waveforms. 4
o be able to calculate or extract beamweights (or magnitude and phase relations) between antenna ports or 5
TAB connectors. Alternatively, and if the O-RU DUT manufacturer provides the list of beam directions 6
supported by the O-RU DUT, TER might calculate or extract the beam direction instead of the 7
beamweights. 8
o be able to generate and deliver signals with the required beamweights (or magnitude and phase relations) at 9
the antenna ports or TAB connectors.  10
o be fully calibrated up to the interfaces where is connected to the O-RU DUT antenna ports (or TAB 11
connectors). For that, a known test signal might be either injected by the TER into the O-RU DUT, or 12
internally generated by the O-RU DUT, and the O-RU DUT must not apply any digital or analog 13

and U-Plane signals from TER into the O-RU and using C-Plane messages with beamID=0.   15

corresponding Stock sectioning defined above, as well as be capable of capturing U-Plane messages and 20
extracting 3GPP test frames (i.e. IQ data) from the captured U-Plane messages. 21
o be capable of generating the C-Plane messages for, receiving, extracting and demodulating the 3GPP test 22
frames following the corresponding Stock sectioning defined above. 23
 24
 The TER might have less testing ports than the O-RU DUT conducted antenna ports (or TAB connectors) if 25
testing is carried out sequentially; or as many antenna ports as the number of conducted antenna ports (or TAB 26
connectors) under test if testing is carried out simultaneously. 27
 28
 It is up to the TER on how to extract the beamweights (or magnitude and phase relation) between the antenna 29
ports or TAB connectors, or the beam direction / properties, in order to match it with the manufacturer’s 30
declaration. 31
 32
 The user payload will be generated as PN23 with a seed of all ones. 33

 It applies to the following CUS fronthaul specification sections: 35

 Section 6.3.3 for coding of applicable Information Elements 38
 Section 10 for beamforming guidelines. 39

3.2.5.2.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – No Beamforming 42
A. Test Description and Applicability 43
This test is MANDATORY. 44
 45
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with no beamforming 46
(beamId=0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 47
 48
B. Test Entrance Criteria 49
 Manufacturers’ declaration that defines list of magnitude and phase relation (or beamweights) between 50
antenna ports or TAB connectors and/or beam directions with antenna array characteristics when O-RU DUT 51
is operating with no beamforming.  52
 53
C. Test Methodology 54
 55
a. Initial Conditions 56
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 57
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  58

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       161
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
 Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase coherence between the antenna 1
ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.  2
 Connect the signal analyzer to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the beam under 3
test and configure the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the 4
transmitted signal.   5
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.  6
 7
b. Procedure 8
a. Build an appropriate IQ signal described above in the O-DU emulator.   9
b. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the 10
signal and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two sections (DL-SCH 11
and DCI) using section type 1 messages.  Section type zero messages will be used to signal Guard Period 12
resources in the test waveform. 13
c. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing 14
windows described in section3.2.1.1.1.   15
d. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to 16
demodulate and decode the test frame. 17
e. Extract either the beamweights, or magnitude and phase relation, or beam direction from the measured 18
signal. 19
 20
 21
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  22
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance requirement for 23
this radio category (i.e., EVM). 24
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should be the same as the signal described above and should 25
contain all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data. 26
3. The signal relation (i.e. beamweights, or magnitude and phase relation) between antenna ports or TAB 27
connectors, or the extracted beam direction, should match the expected relation, or beam direction, for the 28
expected no beamforming within a tolerance defined by the manufacturer.  29
 30
 31
3.2.5.2.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP UL – No Beamforming 32
A. Test Description and Applicability 33
This test is MANDATORY. 34
 35
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can receive a basic 3GPP test frame with no beamforming 36
(beamId=0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 37
 38
B. Test Entrance Criteria 39
 Manufacturers’ declaration that defines list of magnitude and phase relation (or beamweights) between antenna 40
ports or TAB connectors and/or beam directions with antenna array characteristics when O-RU DUT is 41
operating with no beamforming.  42
 43
C. Test Methodology 44
 45
a. Initial Conditions 46
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 47
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1. 48
 Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase coherence between the antenna 49
ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.  50
 Connect the signal source to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the beam under test 51
and configure the source with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and generate the test 52
signal.  53
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.   54
 55
b. Procedure 56
a. Build an appropriate test signal described above in the signal source of the TER.  57
b. Inject the test signal into the O-RU with the application of an initial set of beamweights, or equivalently 58
magnitude and phase relation, between all the TER ports connected to the antenna ports (or TAB 59

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       162
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
connectors) to emulate the phase and magnitude difference “seen” by the antenna elements under test. For 1
example, initial beamweights could be set to be “all equal” (i.e. no beamforming). 2
c. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the 3
signal and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (UL-4
SCH) using section type 1 messages.. Section type zero messages will be used to signal Guard Periods in 5
the test waveform. 6
d. Play the C plane messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.1. while 7
also triggering the signal source.   8
e. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the DUT, allow it to create and send the U 9
plane messages to the O-DU and for the O-DU to demodulate, decode and extract the payload. 10
f. Repeat the previous steps but now in step b apply a different set of beamweights or phase relation between 11
all the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) when injecting the test signal into the O-RU. For example, 12
repeating the process for a number of different beamweights will simulate the reception of the test signal 13
from different beam directions. This allows to determine if the O-RU is really focusing the sensitivity to 14
the correct beam direction. 15
 16
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  17
1. The test frame received by the TER/O-DU should be the same as the signal described above and should 18
contain all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data. 19
2. The beamweights or magnitude and phase relation at the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) of the test signal 20
that achieves the highest performance (i.e. best EVM, power, SNR, etc.) should match with the manufacturer’s 21
declaration of the phase relation expected for no beamforming. 22
 23
3.2.5.2.3 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Predefined-beam 24
Beamforming 25
A. Test Description and Applicability 26
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 27
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with predefined-beams 28
beamforming (beamId≠0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 29
The transmitted beam direction is measured for each indexed beam required in this measurement, see below. The 30
measured transmitted direction is compared to manufacturer-designated direction. Transmitted direction could be 31
defined by the phase relation between the antenna ports or TAB connectors under test, or directly by extracting the 32
beam direction. 33
Depending on the O-RU beamforming capabilities regarding the ability to generate “coarse”, “fine” and/or “beam 34
groups”, as defined in [2] Section 10.4.1.1. 35
 36
The elevation θ and azimuth Φ angles are defined as in [2] Section 10.4.1.1: 37
 38
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Predefined-beam Beamforming conformance test 39
might include multiple test that the O-RU must comply: 40
 41
a. “Coarse” beamIds test:  42
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that are defined as coarse granularity (coarse beamIds) to the O-DU 43
emulator, the test should include the following beams: 44
1. A coarse beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles. 45
2. A coarse beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 46
3. A coarse beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 47
4. A coarse beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 48
5. A coarse beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 49
 50
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth (Φ) or elevation angle (θ), fewer than 5 beam angles will be measured. 51
 52
b.  “Fine” beamIds test:  53
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that are defined as fine granularity (fine beamIds) to the O-DU 54
emulator, the test should include the following beams: 55

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       163
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
1. A fine beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles. 1
2. A fine beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 2
3. A fine beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 3
4. A fine beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 4
5. A fine beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 5
 6
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth or elevation angle, fewer than 5 beam angles will be measured. 7
 8
c.  “beam-group” beamIds test:  9
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that belong to same and different beam-groups to the O-DU emulator, 10
the test should include the following beams: 11
1. All beams that belong to a beam-group with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) or elevation (θ) angles. 12
2. All beams that belong to a beam-group with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ). 13
3. All beams that belong to a beam-group with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ). 14
4. All beams that belong to a beam-group with maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 15
5. All beams that belong to a beam-group with minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 16
 17
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth or elevation angle, fewer than 5 beam-groups will be measured. 18
 19
 20
B. Test Entrance Criteria 21
 Manufacturers’ defined list of beam indices and their associated magnitude and phase relation between antenna 22
ports or TAB connectors and/or beam directions with antenna array characteristics. 23
 24
C. Test Methodology 25
 26
a. Initial Conditions 27
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 28
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  29
 Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase coherence between the antenna 30
ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.   31
 Connect the signal analyzer to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the beam under 32
test and configure the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the 33
transmitted signal.  34
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range. 35
   36

c. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows 43

d. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to demodulate 45
and decode the test frame. 46
e. Extract either the beamweights, or magnitude and phase relation, or beam direction from the measured 47
signal. 48
 49

3.2.5.2.5 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Weight-based Dynamic 1
Beamforming 2
A. Test Description and Applicability 3
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 4
 5
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with weight-based dynamic 6
beamforming with one spatial stream (single eAxC).  7
 8
The transmitted beam direction is measured for each weighted beam required in this measurement, see below. The 9
measured transmitted direction is compared to manufacturer-designated direction. Transmitted direction could be 10
defined by the phase relation between the antenna ports or TAB connectors under test, or by directly extracting the 11
beam direction. 12
The elevation θ and azimuth Φ angles are defined as in [2] Section 10.4.1.1: 13
 14
 15
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Weight-based Dynamic Beamforming conformance 16
test should evaluate the following beams for the O-RU to comply: 17
 18
a. A weight-based beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles. 19
b. A weight-based beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation 20
angle (θ). 21
c. A weight-based beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle 22
(θ). 23
d. A weight-based beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle 24
(θ). 25
e. A weight-based beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle 26
(θ). 27
 28
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth (Φ) or elevation angle (θ), fewer than 5 beam angles will be measured. 29
 30
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Weight—based Dynamic Beamforming 31
conformance test should also evaluate the following compression methods for each of the supported beams 32
described above (a. to e.) for the O-RU to comply: 33
a. No compression method applied to the beamforming weights.  34
b. Block floating point compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit mantissa. 35
c. Block scaling compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit scaler. 36
d. μ-law compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit fixed width. 37
e. Beamspace compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit scaler.  38
 39
If the O-RU does not support all the compression methods described above, fewer than 5 compression methods will 40
be measured. 41
 42
 43
B. Test Entrance Criteria 44
 Manufacturers’ defined list of frequency domain (ϕ) and or time domain (θ) weights for each supported beam, 45
or alternatively, list of gain and phase relation, or complex beam weights, between antenna ports or TAB 46
connectors for each supported beam . Also, the O-RU needs to report to the O-DU the antenna array 47
characteristics. 48

 Connect the signal analyzer to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the beam under 1

 5
b. Procedure 6
a. Build an appropriate IQ signal described above in the O-DU emulator.   7
b. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal 8
and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by one or two sections (DL-SCH and DCI) 9
using section type 1 messages, the sections in the first symbol of the slot will contain section extension 10
extType=0x01 to convey the beam weights, it is not required that the next sections contain extension type 1 11
since the same beam IDs will not change along the slot. If O-RU does not support a field, then its value 12
should be 0x0. Section type zero messages will be used to signal Guard Period resources in the test 13
waveform. 14
c. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows 15
described in section 3.2.1.1.1.   16
d. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to 17

e. Extract either the beamweights, or magnitude and phase relation, or beam direction from the measured 19
signal. 20

 47
C. Test Methodology 48
 49
a. Initial Conditions 50
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 51
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  52
 Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase coherence between the antenna 53

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       167
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
 Connect the signal source to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the beam under test 1
and configure the source with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and generate the test 2
signal.  3
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.   4
 5
b. Procedure 6
 7
a. Build an appropriate test signal described above in the signal source of the TER.  8
b. Inject the test signal into the O-RU with the application of an initial set of beamweights, or equivalently 9
magnitude and phase relation, between all the TER ports connected to the antenna ports (or TAB 10
connectors) to emulate the phase and magnitude difference “seen” by the antenna elements under test. For 11
example, initial beamweights could be set to be “all equal” (i.e. no beamforming).   12
c. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal 13
and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by one or two sections (UL-SCH) using section 14
type 1 messages, the sections in the first symbol of the slot will contain section extension extType=0x01 to 15
convey the beam weights, it is not required that the next sections contain extension type 1 since the same 16
beam IDs will not change along the slot. If O-RU does not support a field, then its value should be 0x0. 17
Section type zero messages will be used to signal Guard Period resources in the test waveform. 18
d. Play the C plane messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.1. while 19
also triggering the signal source.   20
e. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the DUT, allow it to create and send the U 21
plane messages to the O-DU and for the O-DU to demodulate, decode and extract the payload. 22
f. Repeat the previous steps but now in step b apply a different set of beamweights or phase relation between 23
all the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) when injecting the test signal into the O-RU. For example, 24
repeating the process for a number of different beamweights will simulate the reception of the test signal 25
from different beam directions. This allows to determine if the O-RU is really focusing the sensitivity to the 26
correct beam direction. 27
 28
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  29
1. The test frame received by the TER/O-DU should be the same as the signal described above and should contain 30
all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data. 31
2. The beamweights or magnitude and phase relation at the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) of the test signal 32
that achieves the highest performance (i.e. best EVM, power, SNR, etc.) should match with the manufacturer’s 33
declaration of the beam under test. 34

Test Description and Applicability 7 This Test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 8  9 The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with channel-information-based 10 beamforming with multiple spatial streams from multiple users (i.e. MU-MIMO). 11  12 For Category A radios, the test is for each polarization separately and consequently either different or same channel 13 models can be defined for each of the polarization. For Category B, same channel might be used for both 14 polarizations and the test might measure each polarization separately. 15 The transmitted beam direction is measured for each scenario required in this measurement.  The measured 16 transmitted direction is extracted from the decoded received signal in the TER. Transmitted direction is defined by 17 properly receiving a data transmission between the O-RU and the target User Equipment while destroying or 18 heavily attenuating the data transmission between the O-RU and the other User Equipment. 19 The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Channel-Information-based Beamforming 20 conformance test should evaluate the following scenarios for the O-RU to comply and will rely on TER Channel 21 Emulation capabilities as shown in Figure 3.2.3.2-3.  22  23  24 Figure 3.2.5.2-2 TER with Channel Emulation Capability 25  26 A scenario where two spatial streams, or eAxC flows, are generated for two users (one layer each) with M antenna 27 ports or TAB connectors. The O-DU will report to the O-RU via C plane messages an emulated channel estimate 28 𝐻 ≜  [ℎଵଵ, . . . , ℎଵெ, ℎଶଵ, . . . , ℎଶெ]∈ ℂଶ௫ெ. The emulated channel  𝐻  shall model a static channel, with rank not lower 29 than the number of spatial streams, and it shall not be a block-diagonal channel. As an example, a Butler channel 30 model could be implemented as emulated channel. The O-RU will calculate and apply the beamweight matrix 𝐺 ≜31  [𝑔ଵଵ, . . . , 𝑔ଵெ, 𝑔ଶଵ, . . . , 𝑔ଶெ] ∈ ℂெ௫ in such that the received signal at the users is the same as the generated in the O-32 DU. It is up to the O-RU on how to calculate the beamforming weights, for example Zero-forcing, regularized zero-33 forcing / MMSE, etc.   34

3.2.5.3 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Compression (CMP) 40
Validate the correct implementation and interpretation of mandatory and optional IQ data compression formats 41
described in [2]. Also, evaluate the consistency in U-Plane signaling. 42
It applies to the following CUS fronthaul specification sections in [2]: 43
 Section 5.4.2 for layout of C-Plane message, in particular Section Type 1 44
 Section 5.4.4.10 for applicability of "udCompHdr" and "reserved" fields 45
 Section 6.3.3.15/16/17 for applicability of udCompParam 46
 Section 6.3.2 for U-Plane message layout 47
 Section 6.3.3 for coding of applicable Information Elements 48
 Table 8-2 for mandatory/optional capabilities. 49
 Annex A  50
 51
The objective is primarily to test the protocol, prior to the compression algorithms performance. 52
Signalling: IQ Compression related fields in UC-Plane messages include:  53
 U-Plane IQ data field  54
 C-Plane udCompHdr (per section 5.4.4.10 of [2]) 55

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       173
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
 U-Plane udComphdr (per section 6.3.3.13 of [2]) 1
 U-Plane udCompParam (per section 6.3.3.15 of [2]) 2
 Modulation compression parameters used in the Section Extension Type =4 3
 csf (constellation shift flag)  4
 modCompScaler (modulation compression scaler value) 5
 6
Compression: Current specification includes 5 compression modes, including uncompressed mode (fixed point).  Tests 7
should cover each one of these modes   8
 fixed-point 9
 block floating-point 10
 block scaling 11
 mu-law 12
 modulation compression  13
 14
IQ Bit Width: For fixed-point, block floating point, block scaling and mu-law compression, IQ information can be 15
represented using different bit width (1-16 bits). To optimize test time, tests should be performed on a subset of bit 16
widths  17
 9 bits 18
 14 bits  19
3.2.5.3.1 Overview of Compression Test Methodology 20
A common test methodology and structure will be used across all compression test cases. Each one of the test cases will 21
be defined with specific input parameters and expected output values.  22
To minimize influence of the Radio’s RF performance to the test results, the test methodology will be based on a 23
relative comparison between modulated signal measurements performed on a TDD test frame with uncompressed IQ 24
(fixed 16 bits) and measurements on the same test frame using compressed IQ. The test will verify that the difference 25
between measurements fits within an acceptable range for the test to pass. 26
For downlink test, the modulated signal measurement is performed by a signal analyser on the antenna port of the O-27
RU.  28
For uplink measurement, the modulated signal measurement is performed with the IQ extracted from the Uplink U-29
Plane data sent by the O-RU on the O-RAN interface.  30
The following paragraphs in this overview section outline the details of these common test methodologies.  31
3.2.5.3.1.1 Test Frame 32
TDD test methodology for compression will combine similar downlink and uplink test patterns used for FDD test. The 33
main difference is that uplink and downlink tests are performed simultaneously for TDD.  34
The test frames used for compression conformance test will be referred in this document as “NR-FR1-TDD-CMP-35
TST-DL” TDD Downlink Standard Compression Test frame and “NR-FR1-TDD-CMP-TST-UL” TDD Uplink 36
Standard Compression Test frame. They are 5G NR frames based on the description in section 3.2.1.1.3 For scenario #3 37
(Conducted TDD Tests for FR1 Radios) with specific attributes described below. 38
The Downlink UC-Plane test stimulus file includes the C-Plane and U-Plane messages that require the O-RU to transmit 39
on the downlink the NR-FR1-TDD-CMP-TST-DL test frame.  40
The Uplink C-Plane test stimulus file includes the C-Plane messages that require the O-RU to provide the uplink U-41
Plane messages according to the NR-FR1-TDD-CMP-TST-UL test frame received by the O-RU on its antenna port. 42
Signalling and IQ information will be based on various compression schemes 43

3.2.5.3.1.2 Test Frame Power  3
To ensure that the compressed IQ exponent value is properly tested, each symbol of the test frame will include 3 4
sections with different power levels.  The Power levels are relative powers to the first group of PRBs transmitted.  Any 5
valid 3GPP power level may be used for the first set of PRBs as long as the power levels of the remaining PRBs are 6
also valid.  Figure 3.2.3.3-1 below shows PRB power relative to the first set of PRBs. 7
    0 dB for the bottom third of total PRBs in the symbol (referred as PDSCH0) 8
 -10 dB for the middle third of total PRBs in the symbol (referred as PDSCH1) 9
 -20 dB for the upper third of total PRBs in the symbol (referred as PDSCH2) 10
 11
The spectrum representation of the frame shown in Figure 3.2.3.3-1 below highlights the various power levels for each 12
group of PRBS within a symbol.  13

________________________________________________________________________________________________ Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       176
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00  1 Figure 3.2.5.3-1 PRB Spectrum Power Visualization 2  3 3.2.5.3.1.3 Test Frame User data  4 To validate that user data has not been impacted by compression, the test payload for the 3 sections is based on a 5 PN23PN23 sequence that will be measured and compared by the test apparatus.   6 3.2.5.3.1.4 Test Frame Modulation Scheme 7 To maximise coverage on the compressed IQ mantissa value, the test frame will use the highest possible modulation 8 (256 QAM modulation for downlink).  An example measurement is show in Figure 3.2.3.3-2. 9  10 Table 3.2.5.3-3 Example User Data Modulation Validation 11  12 3.2.5.3.1.5 Summary of Required Measurements for Compression Tests 13 3 measurements types will be required for downlink tests and 4 measurements will be required for uplink tests.  14  Power level:  Using the test frames (NR-FR1-CMP-TST-FRAME-DL and NR-FR1-CMP-TST-FRAME-UL) 15 sent twice with both compressed and uncompressed IQ data, power level measurements are performed to 16 validate compression algorithms influence on Exponent (udCompParam).  17 The Power level measurements are called: 18 For downlink 19  20 o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH0 in dBm 21 o CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH0 in dBm 22 o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH1 in dBm 23 o CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH1 in dBm 24 o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH2 in dBm 25 o CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH2 in dBm 26  27 For Uplink 28 o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-UL-PDSCH0 in dBm 29 o CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-UL-PDSCH0 in dBm 30 o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-UL-PDSCH1 in dBm 31 o CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-UL-PDSCH1 in dBm 32 o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-UL-PDSCH2 in dBm 33 o CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-UL-PDSCH2 in dBm 34  35 For the test to pass, the difference between compressed and uncompressed measurements should be within an 36 acceptable range, called 37 o ACC_PWR_PDSCH0 = ± 1dB 38 o ACC_PWR_PDSCH1 = ± 1dB 39 o ACC_PWR_PDSCH2 = ± 1dB 40

________________________________________________________________________________________________ Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       177
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00 o  1  EVM:  Using a common test frame sent twice with both compressed and uncompressed IQ data, EVM 2 measurements comparisons between uncompressed IQ and compressed IQ will help validate acceptable 3 compression influence on signal quality.  4  5 For downlink These 6 EVM measurements required: 6 o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH0 in % 7 o CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH0  in % 8 o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH1  in % 9 o CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH1  in % 10 o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH2  in % 11 o CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH2  in % 12  13 For uplink These 6 EVM measurements required: 14 o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-UL-PDSCH0 in % 15 o CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-UL-PDSCH0  in % 16 o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-UL-PDSCH1  in % 17 o CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-UL-PDSCH1  in % 18 o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-UL-PDSCH2  in % 19 o CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-UL-PDSCH2  in % 20  21 For the test to pass, the difference between the compressed and uncompressed measurements for the same 22 PDSCH signal must be within the following range: 23 o ACC_EVM_PDSCH0 ≤ 4 percentage points 24 o ACC_EVM_PDSCH1 ≤ 4 percentage points 25 o ACC_EVM_PDSCH2 ≤ 4 percentage points 26  27 An example measurement showing both power and EVM is shown below in Figure 3.2.5.3-2 28 Example Compression EVM Measurement. 29  30   Figure 3.2.5.3-2 Example Compression EVM Measurement 31  32  Payload Data Integrity:  comparing user data between the O-RAN test frame and the RF measurement to 33 validate that compression does not influence user data.  The User data measurements are called: 34 For Downlink 35  36 o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-DL-PDSCH0  37 o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-DL-PDSCH1  38 o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-DL-PDSCH2  39 o CMP-Compressed-BER-DL-PDSCH0  40 o CMP-Compressed-BER-DL-PDSCH1  41 o CMP-Compressed-BER-DL-PDSCH2  42  43 For Uplink 44  45 o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-UL-PDSCH0  46 o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-UL-PDSCH1  47 o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-UL-PDSCH2  48

3.2.5.3.1.7 Results Analysis 2
In general, for each specific Compression Test in this conformance test document, the test will pass if the following 3
conditions are met: 4
 Power measurement differences between Uncompressed and Compressed are within acceptable range  5
 EVM measurement difference between Uncompressed and Compressed are within acceptable range  6
 Data integrity measurements show no data corruption 7
 Uplink U-Plane Header measurements exclude fields for static compression 8
 9

Threshold Criteria. 11

3.2.5.3.2 TDD UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Compression Static Format (SFM) Fixed-Point 3
(FP)  4
A. Test Description and Applicability 5
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY and should be performed if the O-RU supports this compression 6
format. 7
 8
The purpose of this test is to: 9
 Validate correct encoding of IQ data under the following conditions.  10
o RU Static compression configurations 11

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       181
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
o Fixed point IQ data format 1
o Selection of 2 supported bit width: 9 bits, 14 bits  2
o Uplink / downlink 3
 Validate that in the U-Plane PRB header, the udCompHeader, “reserved” and udCompParam fields are 4
not present  5
 6
B. Test Entrance Criteria 7
The test uses the setup and methodology described in section 3.2.1.1. 8
 9
 10
C. Test Methodology 11
a.  Initial Conditions 12
 The O-RU is started 13
 Fronthaul Ethernet interface configured for communication between TER and the DUT. 14
 O-RU synchronized with TER using S-Plane 15
 Communication established between TER and the DUT such that it is possible to exchange U-Plane and 16
C-Plane messages  17
 Signal Analyzer connected to DUT’s antenna port and setup according to DUT RF output configuration 18
 Signal Source connected to DUT’s antenna port and setup according to DUT RF input configuration 19
 20
b.  Procedure 21
For each supported bit width (9 bits, 14 bits), the following tests need to be performed: 22
  23
1. Launch Uncompressed Test  24
 Via the M-Plane or another suitable mechanism, put the O-RU into a static configuration with the downlink 25
and uplink configured as follows: no compression, (16 bits) 26
 Arm Signal Analyzers and Signal Source 27
o Arm Signal analyzer to capture the next Frame  28
o Arm Signal Source to generate the Frame NR-FR1-CMP-TST-FRAME-UL 29
 Arm the CUSM emulator to send the TDD O-RAN test frame, including 30
o Downlink: CU-plane of “uncompressed” NR-FR1-TDD-CMP-TST-ST-DL-UNC-16B test stimulus 31
file to the DUT 32
o Uplink: C-plane of “uncompressed” NR-FR1-TDD-CMP-TST-ST-UL-UNC-16B test stimulus file 33
to the DUT 34
 ARM CUSM-E to capture the Uplink U-Plane Data from the DUT 35
 Launch the test until: 36
o RF Signal Analyzer has captured the downlink frame 37
o CUSM-E has captured the uplink U-plane data  38
2. Uncompressed Downlink Measurements  39
 With the RF Signal Analyzer, perform the 3 power measurements  40
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH0 in dBm 41
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH1 in dBm 42
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-DL PDSCH2 in dBm 43
 With the RF Signal Analyzer, perform the 3 EVM measurements  44
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH0 in % 45
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH1 in % 46
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH2 in % 47
 With the RF Signal Analyzer, check Data integrity measurements  48
o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-DL-PDSCH0  49
o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-DL-PDSCH1  50
o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-DL-PDSCH2 51
3. Uncompressed Uplink Measurements  52
 Extract IQ information from Capture U-Plane trace of the CUSM-E 53
 Using the Signal Analyzer software, perform the 3 power measurements  54
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-UL-PDSCH0 in dBm 55
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-UL-PDSCH1 in dBm 56
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-UL-PDSCH2 in dBm 57
 58
 Using the Signal Analyzer software, perform the 3 EVM measurements  59
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-UL-PDSCH0 in % 60

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       182
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-UL-PDSCH1 in % 1
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-UL-PDSCH2 in % 2
 3
 Using the Signal Analyzer software, perform Data integrity measurements  4
o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-UL-PDSCH0  5
o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-UL-PDSCH1  6
o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-UL-PDSCH2 7
4. Launch “compressed” Test  8
 Via the M-Plane or another suitable mechanism, put the O-RU into a static configuration with the downlink 9
and uplink configured as follows: Fixed point, 9-bit (then 14 bits) 10
 Arm Signal Analyzers and Signal Sources 11
o Arm Signal analyzer to capture the next Frame  12
o Arm Signal Source to generate the Frame NR-FR1-CMP-TST-FRAME-UL 13
 Arm the CUSM emulator to send the TDD O-RAN test frame, including 14
o Downlink: CU-plane of the “Compressed” NR-FR1-TDD-CMP-TST-ST-DL-FPF-9B (then 14B) 15
test stimulus file to the DUT 16
o Uplink: CU-plane of the “Compressed” NR-FR1-TDD-CMP-TST-ST-UL-FPF-9B (then 14B) test 17
stimulus file to the DUT 18
 ARM CUSM-E to capture the Uplink U-Plane Data from the DUT 19
 Launch the test until: 20
o RF Signal Analyzer has captured the downlink frame 21
o CUSM-E has captured the uplink U-plane data 22
5. Compressed Downlink Measurements  23
 With the Signal Analyzer, perform the 3 power measurements  24
o CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH0 in dBm 25
o CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH1 in dBm 26
o CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH2 in dBm 27
 With the Signal Analyzer, perform the 3 EVM measurements  28
o CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH0 in % 29
o CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH1 in % 30
o CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH2 in % 31
 With the Signal Analyzer, check Data integrity measurements  32
o CMP-Compressed-BER-DL-PDSCH0  33
o CMP-Compressed-BER-DL-PDSCH1  34
o CMP-Compressed-BER-DL-PDSCH2 35
6. Validate Downlink conformance conditions  36
 Power measurements within acceptable range  37
o Difference between CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH0 and CMP-Compressed-38
Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH0 is within ACC_PWR_PDSCH0 range 39
o Difference between CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH1 and CMP-Compressed-40
Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH1 is within ACC_PWR_PDSCH1 range 41
o Difference between CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH2 and CMP-Compressed-42
Measured-Power-DL-PDSCH2 is within ACC_PWR_PDSCH2 range 43
 EVM measurements within acceptable range  44
o Difference between CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH0 and CMP-Compressed-45
Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH0 is less than ACC_EVM_PDSCH0 46
o Difference between CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH1 and CMP-Compressed-47
Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH1 is less than ACC_EVM_PDSCH1 48
o Difference between CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH2 and CMP-Compressed-49
Measured-EVM-DL-PDSCH2 is less than ACC_EVM_PDSCH2 50
 BER Measurements show no errors  51
o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-DL-PDSCH0 =0 52
o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-DL-PDSCH1 =0 53
o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-DL-PDSCH2 =0 54
o CMP-Compressed-BER-DL-PDSCH0 =0 55
o CMP-Compressed-BER-DL-PDSCH1 =0 56
o CMP-Compressed-BER-DL-PDSCH2 =0 57

3.2.6 FR1 and FR2 TDD Non-conducted OTA Signal Tests 1
 2
3.2.6.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class NR testing Generic (NRG)  3
All TDD tests described in this section will be combined UL and DL tests (i.e., a single test frame describing both up 4
link and down link). The default test frame used in this section is described in section 3.2.1.1.3 of this document for 5
FR1 radios and Section 3.2.1.1.4 for FR2 radios.  6
There are several variations on this test signal depending on the capabilities of the radio.  If the radio does not support 7
the numerology used in the example tests as reported in the M-plane it will be up to the test developer to modify their 8
tests to adapt to the radio.  This can usually be accomplished by using stock test patterns described above.  The test is 9
expected to follow the same spirit as the tests in this document but things like symbol numbers, number of PRBs, etc. 10
may have to be changed. 11
3.2.6.1.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Base 3GPP DL/UL 12
A. Test Description and Applicability 13
This test is MANDATORY. 14
 15
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can meet the most basic uplink and downlink requirements for O-16
RAN fronthaul using a TDD signal.  Subsequent tests will build on this to exercise additional capabilities of the 17
Fronthaul. 18
 19
Using the standard TDD test frame described in section 3.2.1.1.3 for FR1 or 3.2.1.1.4 for FR2, the O-DU emulator 20
(i.e., O-RAN interface of the TER described in section 2.1) will generate C-Plane and U-Plane messages that 21
require the O-RU to transmit on the down link and uplink the default signal.   22
 23
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit and receive  a basic 3GPP, TDD test frame using the 24
default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.5 of this document (or a similar 3GPP waveform) except only one spatial 25
stream on one antenna will be used.  This test is applicable for Category A and Category B radios (No precoding is 26
required).  As per section 3.2.1.1.5 all downlink user data in this test will be zeros and all uplink user data will be a 27
PN23 sequence. 28
 29
B. Test Entrance Criteria 30
The O-RU must support the default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.3 for FR1 or 3.2.1.1.4 for FR2 of this document.  31
The test numerology will be 30 KHz subcarrier spacing and 100 MHz Bandwidth as described by TM-FR1-TM1.1 32
for FR1, 120 kHz subcarrier spacing and 100 MHz bandwidth as described by TM FR2-TM1.1 for FR2.  It will be 33
for 5G New Radio only.  34
 35
 36
C. Test Methodology 37
a. Initial Conditions 38
Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 39
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  Connect the signal analyser and 40
signal source to the O-RU antenna ports and configure the analyser with any set-up information needed to 41
allow it to synch and demodulate the transmitted signal.   42
b. Procedure 43
Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the signal described above in section 3.2.1.1.3 for FR1 or 44
3.2.1.1.4  for FR2 in the CUSM emulator.  Built the appropriate test frame (uplink slots) for the signal 45
source. Use the CUSM emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe 46
the signal. Every symbol used in the test should be described by a single section (DL-SCH that are used for 47
the test, DMRS and DCI) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for 48
this test.  Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages for downlink slots only. Play those messages to the 49
O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.3 for FR1 or 3.2.1.1.4  for FR2.  Repeat the 50
entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyser and allow it to demodulate and 51
decode the test frame.  It will be the responsibility of the TER’s signal analyser and source to coordinate 52
downlink and uplink TDD transmissions.  The CUSM Emulator of the TER is responsible for receiving 53

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       191
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
uplink U-Plane messages, extracting IQ and decoding it to bits which can be compared to those sent by the 1
signal source. 2
 3
 4
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  5
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance requirement for 6
this radio category (i.e., EVM). 7
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should be the same as the signal described above.  If it contains 8
all the same PRB assignments and all zero data, the test passes. 9
 10
3.2.6.1.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Extended 3GPP DL/UL – Resource Allocation 11
A. Test Description and Applicability 12
This test is MANDATORY. 13
 14
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can meet the extended uplink and downlink requirements for O-RAN 15
fronthaul using a TDD signal.  This test modifies the previous test by using a PN23 sequence in all test PDSCH 16
sections. 17
 18
Using the standard TDD test frame described in section 3.2.1.1.3 for FR1 or 3.2.1.1.4  for FR2 the O-DU emulator 19
(i.e., O-RAN interface of the TER described in section 2.1) will generate C-Plane and U-Plane messages that 20
require the O-RU to transmit on the down link and uplink the default signal.   21
 22
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit and receive  an extended 3GPP TDD test frame using 23
the default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.3 for FR1 or 3.2.1.1.4  for FR2 of this document (or a similar 3GPP 24
waveform) except only one spatial stream on one antenna will be used.  This test is applicable for Category A and 25
Category B radios (No precoding is required).  All downlink user data in this test will be a PN23 sequence and all 26
uplink user data will also be a PN23 sequence. 27
 28
B. Test Entrance Criteria 29
The O-RU must support the default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.3 for FR1 or 3.2.1.1.4  for FR2 of this document.  30
