C. Test Methodology 36
a. Initial Conditions 37
Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 38
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  Connect the signal analyser to the 39
O-RU antenna port and configure the analyser with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and 40
demodulate the transmitted signal.   41
b. Procedure 42
Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the signal described above in section 3.2.1.1.3 for FR1 or 43
3.2.1.1.4  for FR2 in the CUSM emulator. In this case use a PN23 sequence for the downlink shared 44
channel.  Build the appropriate test frame (uplink slots) for the signal source. Use the CUSM emulator 45
control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the uplink and downlink signals. 46
Every symbol used in the test should be described by a single section (DL-SCH that are used for the test, 47
DMRS and DCI) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test.  48
Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages for downlink slots only. Play those messages to the O-RU 49
respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.3 for FR1 or 3.2.1.1.4  for FR2.  Repeat the entire 50
frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyser and allow it to demodulate and decode the 51
test frame.  It will be the responsibility of the TER’s signal analyser and source to coordinate downlink and 52
uplink TDD transmissions.  The CUSM Emulator of the TER is responsible for receiving uplink U-Plane 53
messages, extracting IQ and decoding it to bits which can be compared to those sent by the signal source. 54

 12

(i.e., O-RAN interface of the TER described in section 2.1) will generate C-Plane and U-Plane messages that 19
require the O-RU to transmit on the down link and uplink the specified signal using the SymInc bit in both uplink 20
and downlink.   21

will also be a PN23 sequence. 25

For the downlink slots and symbols: Every symbol should be described by a single type 1 section (DL-2
SCH and DCI) except symbols #5 and #6 which will be used for the SymInc test. The data in these sections 3
must be a PN23 sequence using an initial seed of all ones. Each symbol should be a new PN23 sequence, 4
that is PRB 0 should contain the data from a new PN23 sequence for each symbol. Symbols number 5 and 6 5
should be stock data sections type “E” as shown above.  This stock data section consists of two adjacent 6
symbols each containing two sections.  The corresponding C-Plane message will contain 4 section IDs in a 7
single C-Plane message describing symbols #5 and #6.  The startSymbolId in the application header will be 8
symbol #5. The second section ID for symbol #5 will have the SymInc bit set informing the O-RU that the 9
next section will begin describing symbol #6. The corresponding U-Plane messages will be a new PN23 10
sequence for each symbol (5 and 6). Additional sections should be included to describe the DCI symbols as 11
well as Reference Signals described in 38.141-1.  12
 13
For the uplink sections and symbols: Load uplink test waveform  on the RF Signal Source.  Note this 14
signal has a PN23 sequence as user data.  Configure the source to generate a new PN23 sequence in 15
symbols #5 and #6.  Configure the Signal Source to play test waveforms on 10ms frame boundaries starting 16
when it receives a trigger signal from the O-DU emulator that all C-Plane messages have been sent.  Ensure 17
the O-RU and source are synchronized so downlink slots do not conflict with uplink slots.  Load C-Plane 18
message sequence on Test Equipment O-RU (TER) – Only symbols #5 and #6 in each slot will be used in 19
this test. All other symbols will contain either reference signals or data but will not be considered part of 20
the test.  These two symbols will be used to determine whether the radio properly increments the current 21
symbol ID when the symInc bit is set. The C-Plane message for symbol #5 should have the symInc bit set.  22
This message should have a second section describing symbol #6 (using the symInc mechanism).  All PRBs 23
in each symbol will be requested (In the example waveform 51 PRBs). 24
 25
Steps: 26
 Arm Test Equipment O-RU (TER) to capture DUT fronthaul Messages  27
 Launch test to play the C-Plane messages and the downlink U-Plane messages and trigger the 28
source to play the RF signal on a frame boundary.  29
 Play messages to the O-RU respecting the timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.3 for FR1 or 30
3.2.1.1.4  for FR2.  Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal 31
analyzer and allow it to demodulate and decode the frame. 32
 Record U-Plane messages from DUT for a complete frame and the eAxC corresponding to the 33
Antenna port  34
 Extract IQ information from the captured U-Plane messages 35
 Extract IQ information from the signal analyzer for downlink slots 36
 Extract Payload for both signals 37
 Compare payload binary sequences  38

                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00 3.2.6.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming (BFM)  1 This section describes the beamforming conformance testing for ORAN fronthaul interface. The tests do not aim to test 2 the O-RU beamforming performance or capabilities but to test that the O-RU under test focuses the RF energy or 3 sensitivity into a specific direction and with a specific granularity following the O-DU emulator (i.e., O-RAN interface 4 of the TER described in section 2.1) C-Plane messages.  5 Unless stated otherwise in a test case, the following statements apply to all the test cases defined in this section: 6  It is based on Over-the-Air (OTA) testing with a setup such as described in Section 2.1 and it may be applied to 7 any O-RU DUTs, whether the O-RU DUTs have conducted antenna ports or TAB connectors or not.  8  Section 3.2.1.1.2 for scenario #2 non-conducted OTA FDD FR1 radios contains a description of test setups, as 9 mentioned by 3GPP TS 37.843 defines various radiated test systems. If not explicitly mentioned, scenario #4 10 non-conducted OTA TDD tests for FR1 and FR2 radios will inherit those descriptions.  11  12  It applies to Type A and Type B O-RU DUTs. 13  14  It applies to LTE and/or 5G New Radio O-RU DUTs.  In both cases, precoding is not required in any test case.   15  16  If O-RU DUT supports Analog Beamforming (i.e. time domain beamforming), all the U-Plane test frames are 17 defined by segmenting the Stock Test A: 1 section per symbol.  The definition of this Stock Test A can be 18 found in Figure 3.2.1.1-2 and the description accompanying this Figure.  Each slot shall include multiple 19 sections (one per symbol within the slot) and only one beam at a time (i.e. one beamId at a time) and therefore 20 only one beam can be tested per slot. 21  22  If O-RU DUT supports Digital Beamforming (i.e. frequency domain beamforming), all the U-Plane test frames 23 are defined by segmenting the Stock Test B: 2 sections per symbol definition as shown in Figure 3.2.1.1-2.  24 Each slot shall include multiple sections (two per symbol within the slot) and only one beam per section at a 25 time (i.e. one beamId at a time) and therefore up to two different beams can be tested per slot. 26  27  If O-RU DUT supports multiple polarizations, it is up to the TER to determine if the testing is carried out for 28 each polarization separately or multiple polarizations at the same time. In any case, it is important to guarantee 29 that the correct eAxC_ID for the correct polarization (or polarizations) is exercised.  30  31  For O-RU DUT that support LTE:  32 o Downlink tests will use a standard 3GPP E-TM1.1 test frame for TDD, based on uplink/downlink 33 configuration 3 and special subframe configuration 8  (Section 6.1.1.1 TS 36.141) with 20MHz bandwidth 34 (100 RB) as shown in Figure 3.2.3.2-1. 35  36

3.2.6.2.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – No Beamforming 43
A. Test Description and Applicability 44
This test is MANDATORY. 45
 46
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with no beamforming 47
(beamId=0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 48
 49
B. Test Entrance Criteria 50
 Manufacturers’ declaration that defines list of beam directions when O-RU DUT is operating with no 51
beamforming. This list serves as indication of the expected transmitted beam direction in below evaluation.   52
 53
C. Test Methodology 54
 55
a. Initial Conditions 56
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 57
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  58

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       203
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
 Ensure that the test antenna/s and TER equipment is calibrated within acceptable tolerance.  1
 Place the test antenna/s to a defined position within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4 and 2
configure the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the 3
transmitted signal. 4
 Place the O-RU into a test calibrated point within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4. 5
 Align the O-RU to a default initial position, i.e. align the O-RU to the origin of coordinates of the declared 6
coordinate reference point and orientation in the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4.  7
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.  8
 9
b. Procedure 10
k. Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 or NR-FR2-TM1.1 signal described above 11
in the O-DU emulator.   12
l. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the 13
signal and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (DL-SCH 14
and DCI) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 15
m. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing 16
windows described in section 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4.   17
n. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to 18
demodulate and decode the test frame. 19
o. Measure any metric/s that allows for extracting the transmitted beam direction from a single measurement, 20
i.e. transform-based techniques, or take as many measurements of any metric/s from multiple angles, by 21
for example rotating the O-RU, that allows for extracting beam direction from multiple measurement, i.e. 22
beam scanning. 23
 24
 25
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  26
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer at the contemplated transmitted beam direction should satisfy a 27
basic 3GPP signal performance requirement for this radio category (i.e., EVM). 28
2. The test frame received at the contemplated transmitted beam direction by the signal analyzer should be the 29
same as the signal described above and should contain all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 30
data. 31
3. The extracted or measured beam direction is defined as the direction where the best metric/s were measured (i.e. 32
best EVM, power, SNR, etc.) and should match the expected transmitted beam direction for the expected no 33
beamforming within a tolerance defined by the manufacturer.  34
 35
 36
3.2.6.2.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP UL – No Beamforming 37
A. Test Description and Applicability 38
This test is MANDATORY. 39
 40
 41
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can receive a basic 3GPP test frame with no beamforming 42
(beamId=0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 43
 44
 45
B. Test Entrance Criteria 46
 Manufacturers’ declaration that defines list of beam directions when O-RU DUT is operating with no 47
beamforming. This list serves as indication of the expected receive beam direction in below evaluation.   48
  49
 50
C. Test Methodology 51
 52
a. Initial Conditions 53
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 54
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  55
 Ensure that the test antenna/s and TER equipment is calibrated within acceptable tolerance.  56
 Place the test antenna/s to a defined position within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4 and 57
configure the signal source with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and generate the test 58
signal. 59

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       204
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
 Place the O-RU into a test calibrated point within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4. 1
 Align the O-RU to a default initial position, i.e. align the O-RU to the origin of coordinates of the declared 2
coordinate reference point and orientation in the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4.  3
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.  4
 5
b. Procedure 6
a. Build an appropriate test signal described above in the signal source of the TER.  7
b. Inject the test signal into the O-RU with the application of an initial beam direction. This initial beam 8
direction could be the boresight direction of the receiver antenna array, corresponding to the 9
manufacturers declaration of the expected receive direction. 10
c. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the 11
signal and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (UL-12
SCH) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 13
d. Play the C plane messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4 14
while also triggering the signal source.   15
e. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the DUT, allow it to create and send the U 16
plane messages to the O-DU. 17
f. Allow the O-DU to demodulate, decode and extract the payload and to measure and extract any required 18
metric/s from the received signal that will be used later to determine what is the best received direction. 19
g. Repeat the previous steps but now in step b apply a different beam direction when injecting the test signal 20
into the O-RU. Repeating the process for a number of different beam directions will exercise the reception 21
of the test signal from different receive beam directions. This allows to determine if the O-RU is really 22
focusing the sensitivity to the correct expected receive beam direction. 23
 24
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  25
1. The test frame received at the contemplated receive beam direction by the TER/O-DU should be the same as the 26
signal described above and should contain all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data. 27
2. The extracted or measured receive beam direction is defined as the direction where the best metric/s were 28
measured (i.e. best EVM, power, SNR, etc.) and should match the expected receive beam direction for the 29
expected no beamforming within a tolerance defined by the manufacturer.  30
 31
3.2.6.2.3 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Predefined-beam 32
Beamforming 33
A. Test Description and Applicability 34
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 35
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with predefined-beams 36
beamforming (beamId≠0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 37
The transmitted beam direction is measured for each indexed beam required in this measurement, see below. The 38
measured transmitted direction is compared to manufacturer-designated direction. Transmitted beam direction is 39
defined by extracting the beam direction from directional measurement samples. , e.g. spherical scan. 40
Depending on the O-RU beamforming capabilities regarding the ability to generate “coarse”, “fine” and/or “beam 41
groups”, as defined in [2] Section 10.4.1.1. 42
 43
The elevation θ and azimuth Φ angles are defined as in [2] Section 10.4.1.1: 44
 45
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Predefined-beam Beamforming conformance test 46
might include multiple test that the O-RU must comply: 47
a. “Coarse” beamIds test:  48
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that are defined as coarse granularity (coarse beamIds) to the O-DU 49
emulator, the test should include the following beams: 50
1. A coarse beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles. 51
2. A coarse beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 52
3. A coarse beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 53
4. A coarse beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 54
5. A coarse beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 55
 56

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       205
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth (Φ) or elevation angle (θ), fewer than 5 beam angles will be measured. 1
 2
b.  “Fine” beamIds test:  3
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that are defined as fine granularity (fine beamIds) to the O-DU 4
emulator, the test should include the following beams: 5
1. A fine beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles. 6
2. A fine beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 7
3. A fine beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 8
4. A fine beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 9
5. A fine beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 10
 11
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth or elevation angle, fewer than 5 beam angles will be measured. 12
 13
c.  “beam-group” beamIds test:  14
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that belong to same and different beam-groups to the O-DU emulator, 15
the test should include the following beams: 16
1. All beams that belong to a beam-group with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) or elevation (θ) angles. 17
2. All beams that belong to a beam-group with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ). 18
3. All beams that belong to a beam-group with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ). 19
4. All beams that belong to a beam-group with maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 20
5. All beams that belong to a beam-group with minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 21
 22
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth or elevation angle, fewer than 5 beam-groups will be measured. 23
 24
 25
B. Test Entrance Criteria 26
 Manufacturers’ defined list of beam indices and their associated beam directions with antenna array 27
characteristics. This list serves as indication of the expected transmitted beam direction in below evaluation.   28
 29
C. Test Methodology 30
 31
a. Initial Conditions 32
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 33

 Ensure that the test antenna/s and TER equipment is calibrated within acceptable tolerance.  35

 Place the O-RU into a test calibrated point within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4. 39

 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.  42
   43
b. Procedure 44
a. Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal described above in the O-DU 45
emulator.   46
b. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the 47
signal and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (DL-SCH 48
and DCI) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 49
c. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing 50
windows described in section 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4.   51
d. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to 52
demodulate and decode the test frame. 53
e. Measure any metric/s that allows for extracting the transmitted beam direction from a single measurement, 54
i.e. transform-based techniques, or take as many measurements of any metric/s from multiple angles, by 55
for example rotating the O-RU, that allows for extracting beam direction from multiple measurement, i.e. 56
beam scanning. 57

 19

 24
 Manufacturers’ defined list of beam indices and their associated beam directions with antenna array 25
characteristics. This list serves as indication of the expected receive beam direction in below evaluation.   26

C. Test Methodology 28
 29
a. Initial Conditions 30
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 31
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  32
 Ensure that the test antenna/s and TER equipment is calibrated within acceptable tolerance.  33
 Place the test antenna/s to a defined position within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4 and 34
configure the signal source with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and generate the test 35
signal. 36
 Place the O-RU into a test calibrated point within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4. 37
 Align the O-RU to a default initial position, i.e. align the O-RU to the origin of coordinates of the declared 38
coordinate reference point and orientation in the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4.  39
Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range 40
b. Procedure 41
a. Build an appropriate test signal described above in the signal source of the TER.  42
b. Inject the test signal into the O-RU with the application of an initial beam direction. This initial beam 43
direction could be the boresight direction of the receiver antenna array, corresponding to the 44
manufacturers declaration of the expected receive direction. 45
c. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the 46
signal and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (UL-47
SCH) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 48
d. Play the C plane messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.3.2.1.1.4 49
while also triggering the signal source.   50
e. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the DUT, allow it to create and send the U 51
plane messages to the O-DU. 52
f. Allow the O-DU to demodulate, decode and extract the payload and to measure and extract any required 53
metric/s from the received signal that will be used later to determine what is the best received direction. 54
g. Repeat the previous steps but now in step b apply a different beam direction when injecting the test signal 55
into the O-RU. Repeating the process for a number of different beam directions will exercise the reception 56

of the test signal from different beam directions. This allows to determine if the O-RU is really focusing 1

3.2.6.2.5 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Weight-based Dynamic 11
Beamforming 12
A. Test Description and Applicability 13
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 14
 15
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with weight-based dynamic 16
beamforming with one spatial stream (single eAxC).  17
 18
The transmitted beam direction is measured for each weighted beam required in this measurement, see below. The 19
measured transmitted direction is compared to manufacturer-designated direction. Transmitted beam direction is 20
obtained by directly extracting the beam direction from the directional samples. 21
The elevation θ and azimuth Φ angles are defined as in [2] Section 10.4.1.1: 22
 23
 24
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Weight-based Dynamic Beamforming conformance 25
test should evaluate the following beams for the O-RU to comply: 26
a. A weight-based beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles. 27
b. A weight-based beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle 28
(θ). 29
c. A weight-based beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle 30
(θ). 31
d. A weight-based beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle 32
(θ). 33
e. A weight-based beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle 34
(θ). 35
 36
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth (Φ) or elevation angle (θ), fewer than 5 beam angles will be measured. 37
 38
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Weight—based Dynamic Beamforming 39
conformance test should also evaluate the following compression methods for each of the supported beams 40
described above (a. to e.) for the O-RU to comply: 41
a. No compression method applied to the beamforming weights.  42
b. Block floating point compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit mantissa. 43
c. Block scaling compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit scaler. 44
d. μ-law compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit fixed width. 45
e. Beamspace compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit scaler.  46
 47
If the O-RU does not support all the compression methods described above, fewer than 5 compression methods will 48
be measured. 49

Test Description and Applicability 14 This Test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 15  16 The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with channel-information-based 17 beamforming with multiple spatial streams from multiple users (i.e. MU-MIMO). 18  19 For Category A radios, the test is for each polarization separately and consequently either different or same channel 20 models can be defined for each of the polarization. For Category B, same channel might be used for both 21 polarizations and the test might measure each polarization separately. 22 The transmitted beam direction is measured for each scenario required in this measurement.  The measured 23 transmitted direction is extracted from the decoded received signal in the TER. Transmitted direction is defined by 24 properly receiving a data transmission between the O-RU and the target User Equipment while destroying or 25 heavily attenuating the data transmission between the O-RU and the other User Equipment. 26 The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Channel-Information-based Beamforming 27 conformance test should evaluate the following scenarios for the O-RU to comply.  28  29  30 Figure 3.2.6.2-3 TER with antennas representing multiple UEs 31  32 b. A scenario where two spatial streams, or eAxC flows, are generated for two users (one layer each) with M 33 antennas ports or TAB connectors. The O-DU will report to the O-RU via C plane messages the channel 34 estimate 𝐻 ≜  [ℎଵଵ, . . . , ℎଵெ, ℎଶଵ, . . . , ℎଶெ]∈ ℂଶ௫, which is the effective channel as seen by the antennas 35

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       213
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
representing the multiple UEs, which are spaced sufficiently such that the O-RU can effectively equalize out 1
the interference between the users. The O-RU will calculate and apply the beamweight matrix 𝐺 ≜2
 [𝑔ଵଵ, . . . ,𝑔ଵெ,𝑔ଶଵ, . . . ,𝑔ଶெ] ∈ ℂெ௫  in such that the received signal at the users is the same as the generated in the 3
O-DU. It is up to the O-RU on how to calculate the beamforming weights, for example Zero-forcing, 4
regularized zero-forcing / MMSE, etc.   5
 6
If O-RU supports Analog Beamforming (Time Domain Beamforming), the test should not apply any analog 7
beamforming or time domain beamforming. In this case, M is not the number of antennas ports or TAB connectors 8
but the number of TRX channels supported by the O-RU. 9
 10

 12
 The O-RU must have at least two TRX chains with radiating antennas  13
 The TER equipment must include 2 antennas with sufficient separation to emulate the 2 users such that the O-14
RU can equalize out the mutual interference of the users due to the effective MU-MIMO channel. 15
 Manufacturers’ defined list of number of TRX chains and what antennas are connected to each TRX chain 16

 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 21
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  22
 Ensure that the test antennas and TER equipment are calibrated within acceptable tolerance.  23
 Place the test antennas within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.4  with sufficient separation for 24
effective MU-MIMO beamforming and configure the analyzer ports with any setup information needed to 25
synch and demodulate the MU-MIMO transmitted signal 26
 Place the O-RU into a test calibrated point within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.4. 27
 Align the O-RU to a default initial position, i.e. align the O-RU to the origin of coordinates of the declared 28
coordinate reference point and orientation in the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.4.  29
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.   30
 31
b. Procedure 32
a. Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal described above in the O-DU 33
emulator, with the data symbols for user 1 and user 2 fully overlapping in time and frequency, but with user 34
data initialized using different seeds for the PN23 sequence.   35
b. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal 36
and the scenario under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (DL-SCH and 37
DCI) using section type 5 and 6 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 38
c. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows 39
described in section 3.2.1.1.1. 40
d. Capture the test signals and pass them through a channel emulator or apply the signal processing required to 41
emulate the channel under test using the 2 test antennas.   42
e. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to 43
demodulate and decode the test frames for the 2 users. 44
 45
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  46
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance requirement for this 47
radio category (i.e., EVM). 48
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer for the 2 users should be the same as the signal described above 49
and should contain all the same PRB assignments and all the respective  PN23 data. 50
 51
 52
3.2.6.2.10 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP UL – Channel-Information-based 53
Beamforming 54
A. Test Description and Applicability 55
This Test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 56
 57

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       214
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can receive a basic 3GPP test frame with channel-information-based 1
beamforming with multiple spatial streams from multiple users (i.e. MU-MIMO).  2
 3
Same description and criteria for selecting the beams to be tested applies as in section 3.2.3.2.103.2.6.2.9 but 4
considering the uplink direction.  5
B. Test Entrance Criteria 6
 7
 The O-RU must have at least two TRX chains with radiating sensing antennas  8
 The TER equipment must include 2 antennas with sufficient separation to emulate the 2 users such that the O-9
RU can equalize out the mutual interference of the users due to the effective MU-MIMO channel. 10
 The O-RU must have at least two TRX chains with conducted antenna ports (or TAB connectors) to be 11
connected to a signal generator. 12
 The TER equipment must include 2 antennas with sufficient separation to emulate the 2 users the O-RU need 13
to be able to equalize out the mutual interference of the users due to the effective MU-MIMO channel. 14
Manufacturers’ defined list of number of TRX chains and what antennas are connected to each TRX chain. 15
 16
C. Test Methodology 17
 18
a. Initial Conditions 19
 Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 20
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  21
 Ensure that the test antennas and TER equipment are calibrated within acceptable tolerance.  22
 Place the test antennas within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.4 with sufficient separation for 23
effective MU-MIMO beamforming and configure the generator ports with any setup information needed to 24
transmit the signals from the 2 UEs 25
 Place the O-RU into a test calibrated point within the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.4. 26
 Align the O-RU to a default initial position, i.e. align the O-RU to the origin of coordinates of the declared 27
coordinate reference point and orientation in the OTA chamber as defined in 3.2.1.1.4.  28
 Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.  29
  30
b. Procedure 31
a. Build the appropriate test signals for each of the 2 users as described above in the signal source of the TER 32
using a different seed to initialize the PN23 data for each user. 33
b. Transmit the test signals over the air with sufficient transmit power according to  3.2.1.1.4 34
c. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal 35
and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (UL-SCH) using 36
section type 5 and 6. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 37
d. Play the C plane messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 2.4. while also 38
triggering the signal source.   39
e. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the DUT, allow it to create and send the U-40
plane messages to the O-DU and for the O-DU to demodulate, decode and extract the payload for each of 41
the users. 42
 43
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  44
The test frames received by the TER/O-DU should be the same as the signals described above and should contain all the 45
same PRB assignments and all the original PN23 data of the 2 users. 46

3.3 S-Plane Conformance Tests 20
This section describes tests that are used to validate S-Plane functional and performance conformance of network 21
elements using the O-RAN WG4 fronthaul interface defined in [2] and the O-RAN WG4 M-Plane interface defined in 22
[3].  This version of the conformance specification defines both O-DU and O-RU conformance tests.  Future versions of 23
this specification will describe additional S-Plane functional and performance conformance tests of other clocks used in 24
the front haul, e.g. PRTC/T-GM, etc.  25
S-Plane functionality of the O-RU is determined based on status retrieved from the O-RU using the M-Plane or SMO as 26
appropriate, whereas, S-Plane performance is determined by over-the-air (OTA) or conductive (i.e. a cabled electrical 27
connection to the DUT’s radio interface) measurements of O-RU synchronization signal.  28
S-Plane functionality of the O-DU is determined based on status retrieved from the O-DU using the SMO. As M-plane 29
specification in WG5 become available, retrieval of O-DU status based on M-plane will be considered for functional 30
tests, as well.  31
The performance of O-DU is determined by time/frequency error measurements on output signals (such as 1PPS, or 32
fronthaul SyncE+PTP master ports in LLS-C1 and LLS-C2).  When applicable, O-DU tests are based on ITU-T 33
G.8275.1 profile. ITU-T G.8275.2 is not specifically supported in this document version because this standard does not 34
specify performance criteria and is left for further study.   35
O-DU tests consider both local and remote PRTC connections, as shown in Figure 3.3.1-1. The connection type is 36
relevant for performance tests because the input conditions applied to DUT depends on connection types supported: 37
  An embedded PRTC (e.g. using embedded GNSS receiver, Figure 3.3.1-1a) has no exposed direct O-DU 38
interface, so test stimulus is applied to the Time Reference input (e.g. GNSS RF). 39
  A local PRTC is collocated with the O-DU and may communicate to O-DU via either a 1PPS and serial link 40
(e.g. ITU-T G.8271 or similar interface), Figure 3.3.1-1b, or an Ethernet interface (PTP and PLSF, Figure 41
3.3.1-1c).  42

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       216
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
 A remote PRTC is located anywhere in the network (backhaul or fronthaul) and communicates to O-DU via an 1
Ethernet interface (PTP and PLSF, Figure 3.3.1-1d). 2
 3
 4
Figure 3.3.1-1 Methods to connect PRTC to O-DU  5
 6
Both functional and performance tests require the provision of a test equipment i.e. provision of a test setup that 7
includes a CUSM-E which delivers the necessary stimuli as described in section 3.31. 8
The S-Plane conformance test suite assumes that the vendor’s equipment is conformant and has been tested to meet the 9
requirements of G.8275.1 and IEEE1588v2 and other relevant S-Plane standards. Therefore, this document does not 10
attempt to duplicate tests for these standards.    11
The below sections of bullets summarize the test scope in order to validate conformance to the synchronization plane 12
specification referenced by [2] section 9.  13
 General points which apply to testing of both functional and performance aspects of the O-DU and O-RU: 14
 The tests apply to both 4G (LTE/E-UTRA) and 5G (NR) and are applicable to all O-RAN IOT profiles listed 15
in Annex A 16
 A CUSM-E is needed to generate the necessary M-plane or SMO and S-Plane traffic that includes PTP and 17
possibly SyncE SSM over ESMC. It is synchronized to a time reference. For the O-RU testing a CUSM-E 18
must also generate CU-Plane background traffic. 19
 Shall be done in the lab at constant temperature  20
 The CUS specification [2] may in the future support different kinds of Physical Layer Frequency Support 21
(PLSF), however the only fully specified PLFS by the current edition of [2] is SyncE. Thus, these S-Plane tests 22
are defined to include SyncE when required. 23
 Testing of SyncE is optional and is only valid when the SyncE device which can be driven by a master (e.g. O-24
RU) makes use of it. Therefore, the related SyncE test cases are optional. 25
 26
 The following bulleted points apply specifically to functional tests of the O-RU in addition to the general points 27
above, 28
 For validation of S-Plane, the following are used: 29
o A CUSM-E sends and receives synchronization information over the fronthaul interface.  30
o A Measurement Equipment to perform frequency/phase/time measurements from any available 31
synchronization interface.  32
o DUT’s S-Plane reports its state over M-Plane. 33
 The acceptance criterion for these tests is to comply with specification [2]. 34
 35

 The following bullets points apply specifically to functional test of the O-DU in addition to the general points 1
above: 2
 On its input ports, O-DU end application like O-RU may optionally use SyncE along with PTP. However, in 3
the case of an LLS-C1/C2 O-DU acting as G.8275.1 SyncE+PTP master, SyncE emission is mandatory on the 4
fronthaul for validation of S-plane: 5
o DUT reports its S-Plane state over SMO (and in future WG5 M-plane). 6
 The acceptance criterion for these tests is to comply with specification [2]. 7
 The CUSM-E also provides local time source input signals to the O-DU: 8
o GNSS RF signals, delivered by a GNSS generator referenced to the local time reference 9
o PRTC output signals (1PPS + serial link)  10
 The following bulleted points apply specifically to performance tests for O-RU and O-DU in addition to the general 11
points above. 12
 These tests are not defined to fully stress the DUT. Rather they are intended to stress the DUT enough to 13
determine that it can properly operate via the defined front haul protocol.    14
o The thermal profile is not defined. The tests are defined to be run at a constant temperature, but the 15
thermal profile choice and range is left as a decision for the vendor.  16
o The variable C/U-Plane profile (for example similar to test case 13 shown in figure VI.11 of ITU-T 17
G.8261 [10]) will be defined as part of the work on the future performance tests.  18
o All performance tests described in this section assume the following two components in the procedure (test 19
methodology sections): 20
o Establishing the necessary M-plane session to bring up the O-RU or O-DU and make it ready for 21
transmission of a measurement signal. For the O-DU, the establishment of an M-plane session can be done 22
when the WG5 M-plane is available. In the interim, the O-DU shall be configured using SMO.  23
o For the O-RU in addition to the M-plane session, the transmission of a test signal necessitates the 24
provision of a CU plane test vector. The test vector needs to have enough information to set up a 25
synchronization channel within the radio frame transmitted over the air.  26
o For O-DU performance tests the test cannot be executed unless the O-DU provides an Ethernet port with 27
sync master function and/or a 1PPS output signal.  28
 The acceptance criterion for the performance tests is to satisfy the 3GPP OTA TAE limits specified in 3GPP 29
TS 36.141 [18] for 4G (LTE) and 38.141-2 [20] for 5G (NR), and summarized in eCPRI [11] and ITU-T 30
G.8271 [7]. The conditions applicable to each test will be set out in the relevant sections below (future work 31
item). OTA TAE limits for MIMO/Tx Diversity is outside the scope of this document because they apply 32
between endpoints belonging to the same O-RU. 33
 The CUS Specification [2] which follows eCPRI and IEEE802.1 CM recommendation, defines two examples 34
of O-RU types, but these are not strict classes like the T-BC classes specified in ITU-T G.8273.2. 35
3.3.1 Test Environment 36
The following describes the necessary functions and capabilities of the test equipment in order to perform O-RU or O-37
DU conformance tests. A diagram of the O-RU test set up shown in Figure 3.3.1-2, and a similar diagram of the O-DU 38
test set up is shown in Figure 3.3.1-3.  39
Referring to Figure 3.3.1-2, the stimulus is applied to the O-RU via an Ethernet interface which simulates an ORAN 40
CUS-Plane protocols by using equipment to generate an O-DU and/or front haul time reference. This interface carries 41
the PTP and SyncE stimulus to test the O-RU and carries M-Plane information to configure DUT and as needed C-42
Plane and U-Plane information to generate a test signal to measure time accuracy.  Performance measurements are made 43
at the radio output.  These measurements can be made either over the air (called a non-conductive measurement), or via 44
a cable connection from the radio interface (called conductive measurement).  If the O-RU has a 1PPS (One Pulse Per 45
Second) output, which has been correlated to the radio output, the measurements can be made using the 1PPS output.  46
Figure 3.3.1-2 applies to LLS-C1/C2/C3 topologies.  LLS-C4 topology is for further study. 47

optionally SyncE, or 1PPS output (if available). If no master ethernet port or 1PPS output are available, then 11
performance test cannot be executed. 12

 Typically, in LLS-C3/C4, using a 1PPS measurement interface may avoid having to configure an Ethernet port 14
as PTP master for measurement purpose. 15

 4
CUSM-Plane Emulator: This function implements various planes (C, U, S, M) to simulate a front haul/transport 5
network connecting to DUT (i.e. O-RU, O-DU). It should be capable of testing S-Plane performance under stress with 6
various noise profiles. S-Plane signals sent to DUT and measurement equipment are traceable to reference signals 7
received from the master time reference. Emulator should generate noise free reference signal for Measurement 8
Equipment and (when required) a noise profile for the DUT. The CUSM-Plane emulator may be composed of multiple 9
components or could be a single component containing all the capabilities listed below. When O-RU is the DUT UC-10
Plane is needed for O-RU to generate a radio information required to measure timing.  For O-DU, CU-Plane 11
functionality is not used since timing is measured directly from an Ethernet or 1PPS test port.  12
 Time Reference/S-Plane: This equipment is the frequency and time reference. It delivers frequency (e.g. 13
SyncE, 10MHz, 1PPS), phase (e.g.1PPS, 10ms frame boundary) and time (e.g. ToD, PTP) signals to the Sync 14
Tester equipment and to the various simulators/generators listed below. PRTC specified by ITU-T G.8272 is 15
one example in terms of performance. The level of performance for these reference signals should be 16
significantly (by an order of magnitude) better than the 3GPP synchronization requirements, when absolute 17
limits are measured against the reference clock. The time reference function with the CUSM-Plane emulator is 18
traceable to UTC. The time output is used to synchronize the Signal Analyzer or Test Equipment performing 19
time error measurements. The phase output is used to synchronize the Signal Analyzer or Test Equipment 20
performing time error measurements. 21

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       220
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
 PRTC/T-GM: for testing an O-DU from either local or remote PRTC over Ethernet. It includes a PTP master 1
clock and, when applicable, a SyncE master function that propagate the Time reference and allow adding 2
configured noise patterns. 3
 GNSS Emulator: for testing an O-DU with integrated local PRTC. The GNSS emulator will provide an RF 4
signal to the O-DU. The RF signal emulates a signal received by a GNSS antenna and allows adding 5
configured noise patterns. As an alternative to a GNSS emulator following case is acceptable: the test 6
environment provides the capability to access a GNSS antenna mounted at a suitable location inside the 7
building with line of sight to sufficient number of GNSS satellites (>4).  8
 PRTC Emulator: for testing an O-DU with integrated T-GM, but without an integrated local PRTC: in this 9
case, the test setup needs to provide the following signals to the O-DU: 1PPS (according to ITU G.703), 10
10MHz, and serial link carrying ToD and PRTC status. There are different ToD formats such as ITU-T G.8271 11
Annex A and NMEA. The ToD format of the test setup needs to deliver the ToD format supported by the O-12
DU. This interface allows adding configured noise patterns. 13
 SMO: Responsible for configuring CUSM Plane emulator to send configuration to DUT for the defined 14
conformance tests. 15
 M-Plane: Translate the SMO configuration into the proper M-Plane messages to correctly configure and report 16
status from the DUT.  For O-RU testing this is implemented using WG4 M-Plane protocol.  For O-DU this is 17
implemented by either using a Network Management System (SMO) which is compatible with the DUT or 18
using a WG5 M-Plane emulator. 19
 UC-Plane: S-Plane tests require the transmission of UC-Plane traffic over the fronthaul, the emulator shall 20
implement the O-RAN UC-Plane protocol and shall send a stock data frame defined in Section 2.3.5 and 21
shown in Figure 2-3 as UC-Plane messages to DUT O-RU. 22
The emulator shall merge all traffic types for transmission over the fronthaul without degrading performance of S-23
Plane. 24

Measurement Equipment: This equipment is responsible for extracting the desired synchronization information from 26
the test signal transmitted by the DUT, and then measuring this information to determine if the performance is within 27
limits. This could be a single piece of test equipment containing all the capabilities listed below, or it may be created by 28
interconnecting a separate signal analyzer and performance measurement system.  29
For O-RU testing the following measurement equipment is needed. 30
 Signal Extractor/Analyzer: This equipment demodulates the time reference signal from the O-RU’s downlink 31
radio interface. It receives RF signals from the DUT’s air or preferably coaxial interface. This equipment 32
should be connected to Synchronization/Reference Clock to be able to lock on the correct synchronization 33
channel of the O-RU RF output signal. 34
 Performance Measurement Equipment: This equipment performs error measurements of the 1pps and 35
10MHz signals from DUT or from Signal Extractor.  It uses standard metrics to validate if measured signal 36
meets the defined limits. It is recommended to use a ≥2 GHz sampling on 1pps signals (for 1 ns sampling 37
accuracy)  38
For O-DU testing the following measurement equipment is used. 39
 PTP/SyncE/1pps Measurement Equipment: This equipment is responsible for extracting the desired 40
synchronization information from the master Ethernet port (e.g. decoding the PTP and/or SyncE sent from 41

3.3.2 Functional test of O-RU using ITU-T G.8275.1 profile (LLS-C1/C2/C3) 3
A. Test Description and Applicability 4
This test is MANDATORY. 5
The purpose of this test is to validate that an O-RU is correctly synchronizing to a CUSM Emulator delivering both 6
PTP and (optionally) SyncE using ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] profile and that the O-RU correctly reports its status to the 7
CUSM Emulator based on the nominal or degraded synchronization conditions generated by CUSM Emulator.  8
B. Test Entrance Criteria 9
O-RU is connected to CUSM Emulator directly.  10
O-RU must be operating with the respective SMO or M-Plane properly. (as defined in 3.2.1.1.53.2.1.1.5). 11
C. Test Methodology 12
a. Initial Conditions 13
This test uses the O-RU (DUT), a CUSM-Plane emulator with SMO features to generate stimulus for the O-14
RU (DUT) and signal analyzer to measure the radio interface timing. 15
b. Procedure 16
Three conditions must be tested: 17
Startup: CUSM-Plane Emulator is configured to act as a clock, with PTP and SyncE ports in passive state (no 18
messages sent) 19
Nominal: CUSM-E is configured to start acting as a PTP master compliant with the ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] 20
profile advertising LOCKED status with nominal clockClass and clockAccuracy. If SyncE is to be tested 21
CUSM-Plane Emulator is configured to act as a clock, with SyncE ports in master state, compliant to ITU-T 22
G.8264 profile advertising nominal SSM value as specified by ITU-T G.8275.1 [5]. 23
Degraded: There are two levels of degraded conditions for both PTP and SyncE that can be configured to the 24
CUSM-Emulator. 25
 The first degradation level is where the CUSM-E is configured to act as a clock, with PTP and SyncE 26
ports in master state, compliant to ITU-T G.8275.1 profile, and sending configured clockClass and/or 27
SSM values within the O-RU’s configured accepted limits via the M-plane.  28
 The second degradation level is where the same clockClass and/or SSM values are sent by CUSM-E 29
outside the O-RU’s configured accepted limits via the M-plane. 30
To cover the all the relevant scenarios the test sequence listed in Table 3.3.2-3.2.6.8-1 steps through the 31
Startup/Nominal/Degraded states in a sequence. The steps in this table and Table 3.3.2-2 are intended to be 32
exercised in sequential order.  Since SyncE is optional, there are two columns, one for PTP status and a second 33
for SyncE.  Each of the status items corresponds the conditions defined above. 34
 35

3.3.3 Performance test of O-RU using ITU-T G.8275.1 Profile (LLS-C1/C2/C3) 11
A. Test Description and Applicability 12
This test is MANDATORY.   13
This test validates that an O-RU is synchronizing from a CUSM-plane Emulator delivering configured (ideal and 14
normal operating conditions) PTP and (optionally) SyncE. Frequency and time error generated by the O-RU must 15
be within specified limits.  16
This test focuses on LLS-C1.  In this edition of the document this test can provisionally apply to LLS-C2, but some 17
details related to frequency error require further study.  LLS-C3 will be addressed in a future version. 18
CUS -plane spec lists two classes of O-DU (class A has ±15 ppb frequency error limit; class B has ±5 ppb limit). 19
This test applies to the strictest one from O-RU prospective and therefore considers class A O-DU. 20

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       224
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
B. Test Entrance Criteria 1
O-RU is connected to CUSM-Plane Emulator via direct fiber link(s).  2
Conformance Functional test 2.5.2 is successfully passed. 3
It is the vendor’s responsibility to make sure that limits defined in the test are also met in worse-case field 4
conditions.  Thermal testing, PTP PDV tolerance and SyncE jitter/wander tolerance are beyond the scope of this 5
test. 6
O-RU must be operating with the respective SMO or M-Plane properly. (as defined in 3.2.1.1.5) 7
C. Test Methodology 8
a. Initial Conditions 9
These tests use the O-RU DUT and a CUSM-Plane emulator with SMO features.   10
Frequency and time error are measured on the Air interface at the O-RU output. 11
CUSM-Plane Emulator is configured to act as a clock, with PTP ports in master state, compliant to ITU-T 12
G.8275.1 profile advertising LOCKED status with nominal clockClass and clockAccuracy. 13
CUSM-Plane Emulator is configured to act as a clock, with SyncE ports in master state, compliant to ITU-T 14
G.8264 profile advertising nominal SSM value.  15
The DUT shall have achieved frequency and phase lock prior to starting the test. 16
b. Procedure:  17
Unlike the functional test defined in section 3.3.2, where start-up / nominal / degraded scenarios are tested, 18
only nominal scenarios with ideal and normal operation input noise are tested in this section. 19
1. Ideal: PTP and SyncE (if used) provide “ideal” O-RU input synchronization with no added noise. 20
2. Normal Operation: PTP and SyncE (if used) provide “Within normal operating limits” O-RU inputs as 21
specified in CUS-Plane Specification [1], simultaneously meeting two limits:  22
a. Maximum time error: ± 1400 ns,  23
b. Maximum frequency error (0.1Hz low pass filtered): ±15 ppb  24
Notes applicable to this Normal Operation condition test: 25
 The CUSM-Plane Emulator may be configured to generate the time and frequency error of PTP and SyncE, 26
either simultaneously or sequence.  27
 CU and M plane messages do not need to be modified. It has no impact if they are delayed by the time and 28
frequency error applied in this test. 29
 The time error added to the input signal shall follow a sinusoidal waveform with amplitude (A) and frequency 30
(f). Three such signal frequencies are specified for the test, but intermediate ones can be used for testing, as 31
long as the following relationship between amplitude and frequency: A[ns] = 15[ppb]/(2*pi*f[Hz]) is 32
maintained and simultaneously meets the 2a and 2b conditions above. An additional constant time error may 33
be added to the sinusoidal waveform for each frequency, so that the maximum time error reaches the maximum 34
value of 1420 ns: cTE[ns] = 1420[ns] - A[ns]. 35
 Based on ITU-T analysis it is considered that the time error budget comprises both constant and dynamic 36
errors. Because of this the time error budget is proposed to be split so that the constant time error represents at 37
least half of the total budget. This is approximately consistent with ITU-T 8271.1. 38
 Testing any higher frequency input noise than the ITU cut-off frequency (0.1Hz) would require using limits 39
that are defined by vendor-specific parameters (CUS spec provides an example for a 75 MHz low pass filtering 40
and 18ppb frequency noise generation O-RU). It is therefore outside the scope of this document and such 41
performance must be validated by vendors and documented in test reports. 42
 The following table and graph show the three sinusoidal time error waveforms to be used for testing: 43
 44

D. Pass/Fail Criteria (expected results)  6
The results as measured for conducted or non-conducted (OTA) on the Air interface from the two conditions 7
specified above shall be less than or equal to these values:  8
1. Ideal Case:  9
a. ±35 ppb maximum frequency error  10
(3GPP limit 50 ppb - 15ppb = 35 ppb, where 15ppb is the error of a class A O-DU (worst-case)) 11
b. +/-80ns maximum time error 12
(3GPP limit 1500 ns – CUS spec 1420ns = 80 ns, where 1420ns is the error allocated to the O-DU for 13
LLS-C1).   14
c. As multiple O-RUs are not tested, there is no distinction between relative and absolute time error 15
measurement. 16
2. Normal Operation Case:  17
a. ±50 ppb maximum frequency error  18
(3GPP limit) 19
b. ±1500ns maximum time error 20
(3GPP limit).  21
As multiple O-RUs are not tested, there is no distinction between relative and absolute time error measurement. 22
Note: This test as currently defined does not provide any allowances for measurement error. It is left to the tester to 23
factor in any errors based on the test equipment used. Defining the allowed measurement error is for future study. 24

3.3.5 Functional test of O-DU Synchronized from ITU-T G.8275.1 profile PRTC/T-1
GM (LLS-C1/C2/C3/C4) 2
A. Test Description and Applicability 3
This test is MANDATORY. 4
The purpose of this test is to validate that an O-DU is correctly synchronizing to a timing reference delivering by 5
PTP (and optionally SyncE) when using ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] profile and that the O-DU correctly reports its status 6
to the SMO or WG5 M-Plane controller based on the nominal or degraded synchronization conditions generated by 7
CUSM Emulator.  8
This test covers all cases where O-DU is synchronized using the Ethernet interface, whether the PRTC/T-GM is: 9
 Local (direct link from a co-located equipment): case c in figure 3.3.1-1 10
 Remote (network connection from a distant equipment): case d in figure 3.3.1-1 11
These O-DU functional tests do not consider configurations which have multiple sources. It is assumed the O-DU 12
has only a single synchronization source. Multiple sources such as a Multiport PTP/SyncE are for further study. 13
B. Test Entrance Criteria 14
O-DU is connected to the sync stimuli directly as shown in Figure 3.3.1-3 via the Ethernet Test Port.  15
O-DU must be properly operating with the respective SMO or M-Plane (when WG5 M-Plane specification is 16
available and implemented). (as described in 3.3.1). 17
C. Test Methodology 18
a. Initial Conditions 19
This test uses the O-DU (DUT), a sync tester setup and SMO features to generate stimulus for the O-DU 20
(DUT) and retrieve its sync status. For LLS-C1/C2 the fronthaul ports must be enabled as ITU-T G.8275.1 21
synchronization master.  22
b. Procedure 23
Three conditions must be tested: 24
Startup: The CUSM-E is configured to act as a clock, with PTP and SyncE ports in passive state (no messages 25
sent). 26
Nominal: The CUSM-E is configured to start acting as either a PTP master compliant with the ITU-T 27
G.8275.1 [5] profile advertising LOCKED status with nominal clockClass and clockAccuracy. If SyncE 28
is to be tested CUSM-E is configured to act as a clock, with SyncE ports in master state, compliant to 29
ITU-T G.8264 profile advertising nominal SSM value as specified by ITU-T G.8275.1 [5]. 30
Degraded: There are two levels of degraded conditions for both PTP and SyncE that the CUSM-E can be 31
configured to. 32
 The first degradation level is where the CUSM-E is configured to act as a clock, with PTP and SyncE 33
ports in master state, compliant to ITU-T G.8275.1 profile, and sending configured clockClass and/or 34
SSM values within the O-DU’s configured accepted limits via the M-plane.  35
 The second degradation level is where the same clockClass and/or SSM values are sent by CUSM-E 36
outside the O-DU’s configured accepted limits via the SMO (or M-plane). 37
To cover the all the relevant PTP functional scenarios the test sequence listed in Table 3.3.5-1 steps through 38
the Startup/Nominal/Degraded states in a sequence.  Since SyncE is optional, there are two columns, one for 39
PTP status and a second for SyncE.   In this table each of the status items (Startup, Nominal, Degraded) 40
correspond to the conditions defined above. 41
 42

D. Pass Fail Criteria (expected results) 4
The acceptance criterion is that the status reported by the O-DU for the steps defined in above procedure 5
matches the results described in the 2 tables which follow, Table 3.3.5-2 and Table 3.3.5-3. The tables cover 2 6
different use cases.  1) PTP without SyncE, and 2) PTP with SyncE. The test engineer should choose the 7
appropriate table(s) based on the equipment’s intended application(s).    8
Each of the tables are formatted similarly.  The left two columns indicate the procedural steps as defined in 9
Table 3.3.2-3.2.6.8-1. The right columns list the O-DU status parameters that are defined in the M-Plane 10
specification [3] (chapter 10) and relevant YANG models. These parameters are queried from the test O-DU 11
and their values should match those listed in the tables.  12
When an O-DU’s selected time source is PTP and optional SyncE, the parameters to be checked are: Sync-13
state, PTP sync-source-status, PTP clock-class, SyncE sync-source-status, SyncE quality-level. 14
In LLS-C1 and LLS-C2 and regardless of the selected time source, the PTP Master sync-source-status, PTP 15
Master clock class, SyncE Master sync-source-status, and SyncE Master Quality Level shall also be monitored. 16
Specifically, for LLS-C1 configuration the emission of SyncE by O-DU is only mandatory if the O-RU 17
requires it. 18
For PTP master clock-class, optional SyncE quality-level and master quality-level, the “Rcvd Value” table 19
entry indicates that the value read should be the same as the one received by the O-DU (except in Startup and 20
Disconnected modes when there is no such received value and the default one is reported).  21
In case of local failure in the O-DU then O-DU should use FREERUN mode. 22
These tests do not consider configurations which have multiple sources. This is for further study.  23

prior to O-DU acquiring LOCK, and it also occurs when O-DU is in HOLDOVER and the reference 4
is no longer within specification.  5
Note 3: in case of local failure inside the O-DU. 6
Note 4: As per ITU-T G.8275.1, degraded clockclass values in holdover may be either, (a) 7, then 140 or150 or 7
160, for an O-DU acting as a Grandmaster clock, or (b) 135, then 165 for an O-DU behaving as a 8
Boundary clock. 9
Note 5: Depending on O-DU implementation the Sync-state may be LOCKED or “HOLDOVER (Note 2) then 10
FREERUN.”  11

3.3.6 Functional test of O-DU Synchronized from Embedded or Local non-PTP 1
PRTC (LLS-C1/C2/C3/C4) 2
A. Test Description and Applicability 3
This test is CONDITIONAL-MANDATORY. This test is mandatory if the DUT contains: 4
 Either an O-DU with an embedded local PRTC using a GNSS receiver (see case a in figure 3.3.1-1) 5
 Or an O-DU connected by a 1PPS + serial interface (e.g. ITU-T G.8271, see case b in figure 3.3.1-1) to a co-6
located PRTC provided by the test setup. 7
The purpose of this test is to validate that an O-DU is correctly synchronizing to a non-PTP local time source and 8
that the O-DU correctly reports its status to the SMO or WG5 M-Plane controller based on the nominal or degraded 9
synchronization conditions generated by CUSM Emulator.  10
This O-DU functional test does not consider configurations which have multiple time sources.  11
B. Test Entrance Criteria 12
O-DU is connected to the time sync stimuli directly as shown in Figure 3.3.1-3 via the GNSS RF signal or local 13
PRTC output signals.  14
O-DU must be properly operating with the respective SMO or M-Plane (when WG5 M-Plane specification is 15
available and implemented) emulator components. (as described in 3.3.1). 16
C. Test Methodology 17
a. Initial Conditions 18
This test uses a time reference, synchronization tester setup and SMO/M-Plane functions to generate stimulus 19
for the O-DU (DUT) and then retrieves the O-DU’s sync status. For LLS-C1/C2 the fronthaul ports must be 20
enabled as an ITU-T G.8275.1 synchronization master.  21
b. Procedure 22
Three conditions must be tested: 23
Startup: The CUSM-E is configured to act as a clock, with its output signals (either GNSS RF or PRTC ones) 24
not started sending time information to DUT. 25
Nominal: The CUSM-E is configured to start delivering output signals (either GNSS RF or PRTC ones) in 26
LOCKED status with optimal time and state information.  27
Degraded: The degraded conditions for GNSS receiver’s or PRTC output are not well defined.  There are no 28
defined “slightly degraded” or “severely degraded” signal indications. Thus, the indication of a 29
degraded state may be implementation specific.  Further, a degraded GNSS scenario is the only 30
condition which causes the O-DU to lose its locked status.  31
For GNSS RF signals, one proposal is to simulate the reception of a single satellite with a low signal level. 32
However, all GNSS receivers may not offer the same sensitivity and robustness to this scenario. 33
For GNSS-based PRTC output signals, one proposal is to advertise an alarm on poor signal status, but every 34
protocol may have its own alarm mapping 35
To cover the all the relevant functional scenarios the test sequence listed in Table 3.3.6-1 steps through the 36
Startup/Nominal/Degraded states in order.  In this table each of the status items corresponds to the conditions 37
defined above. 38
 39

                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00

SyncE assistance for GNSS is not considered in this test case and is left for future study. 16

3.3.7 Performance test of O-DU Synchronized from either Local or Remote PRTC 2
using ITU-T G.8275.1 PTP Profile (LLS-C1/C2/C3/C4) 3
A. Test Description and Applicability 4
This test scope is relevant to LLS-C1 to LLS-C4. 5
This test is CONDITIONAL-MANDATORY for O-DUs which support LLS-C1, LLS-C2 and do not only derive 6
their timing information from an embedded PRTC.   7
This test is OPTIONAL for O-DUs that only support LLS-C3 or LLS-C4 topology and is dependent on the 8
availability of a measurement point.  For equipment that only supports LLS-C3 or LLS-C4, if the measurement 9
point is not available, then the O-DU shall document that this conformance test cannot be performed. 10
This test validates that an O-DU correctly synchronizes to incoming S-Plane timing information, from a CUSM-11
plane Emulator which is emulating: 12
 Either a local PRTC (using 1PPS+ serial link interface, e.g. ITU-T G.8271, see case b in figure 3.3.1-1) or 13
local PRTC/T-GM (PTP and optionally SyncE, see case c in figure 3.3.1-1) and meeting ITU-T G.8271.1 14
reference point B network limits. 15
 Or a remote PRTC/T-GM (PTP and optionally SyncE, see case d in figure 3.3.1-1) meeting ITU-T G.8271.1 16
reference point C network limits. The CUSM-E may be configured to inject either ideal or normal operating 17
condition noise into the S-Plane timing information. Frequency and time error measured at the output of the O-18
DU must be within specified limits, which may differ between LLS-C1-C4 configurations.  19
As an example, the local reference link may use ITU-T G.8271 Annex A “1PPS+ToD” protocol. 20
This test covers the two classes defined by CUS -plane spec for LLS -C1 and LLS -C2 (class A has ±15 ppb 21
frequency error limit; class B has ±5 ppb limit).  22
This test is defined assuming a Full Timing Support (FTS) profile used on all PTP ports of the O-DU.  Partial 23
timing support is left for further study. 24
The test intent is to exercise S-Plane performance under ideal and a typical/normal operating condition.  The test is 25
not intended to exercise worst case conditions. It is the vendor’s responsibility to make sure that limits defined in 26
the test are also met in worse-case field conditions.  Variable temperature, PTP PDV tolerance and SyncE 27
jitter/wander tolerance, holdover and transients are beyond the scope of the CUS-Plane specification. 28
 29
B. Test Entrance Criteria 30
Conformance Functional test 3.3.5 has successfully passed. 31
O-DU is connected to CUSM-Plane Emulator’s time reference output interface.  32
O-DU is connected to CUSM-E’s SMO or M-Plane function. (as defined in 3.3.1) 33
C. Test Methodology 34
a. Initial Conditions 35
These tests configure the DUT (O-DU) using the CUSM-Plane emulator’s SMO or M-Plane features.  The O-36
DU configuration depends on which LLS-C1-C4 topologies are to be tested and also it depends on whether the 37
PRTC is local or remote.   38
For LLS-C1 and LLS-C2 configuration, the test is set up to measure frequency and time error on one of the 39
Ethernet master fronthaul ports of the DUT. 40
For LLS-C3 and LLS-C4 configuration, the test is configured to measure time error on a measurement port of 41
the O-DU, typically a 1PPS signal if available or an unused Ethernet port. 42

________________________________________________________________________________________________
Copyright © 2021 by the O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V.
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in the Annex ZZZ.       233
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v02.00
CUSM-Plane Emulator is configured to act as a clock, with PTP ports in master state, compliant to ITU-T 1
G.8275.1 profile advertising LOCKED status with nominal clockClass and clockAccuracy. 2
CUSM-Plane Emulator is configured to act as a clock, with SyncE ports in master state, compliant to ITU-T 3
G.8264 profile advertising nominal SSM value.  4
CUSM-Plane Emulator is configured to deliver 1PPS and act as a PRTC advertising LOCKED status over its 5
serial link with nominal quality level (whatever protocol is used, ITU-T G.8271 or proprietary).  6
Once the DUT has been configured, the DUT shall have achieved frequency and phase lock prior to starting 7
the test. 8
b. Procedure:  9
Unlike the functional test defined in section 3.3.5 3.3.2, where start-up / nominal / degraded scenarios are 10
tested, only nominal scenarios with ideal and normal operation input noise are tested in this section. 11
1. Ideal Operation: The time source provides “ideal” O-DU synchronization input with no implicitly 12
added dynamic or constant time error. This applies when testing with either a local or remote time 13
source. 14
2. Normal Operation: The time source provides an input stimulus with some added noise that is “within 15
normal operating limits.” O-DU inputs as specified in CUS-Plane Specification [1]. The TEL stimulus is 16
split between dynamic (|dTEL|) and constant (|cTE|) and is shown in Table 3.3.3-11The maximum time 17
error (|TEL|) is  18
 1100ns at ITU-T G.8271.1 section 7.3 reference point C (for remote PRTC/T-GM over PTP) . 19
 100ns at ITU-T G.8271.1 section 7.2 reference point B (for both local PRTC/T-GM over PTP, and PRTC 20
over 1PPS+ serial link interface) 21
The TEL stimulus is split between dynamic (|dTEL|) and constant (|cTE|) and is shown in Table 3.3.7-1.  The 22
time error added to the input signal shall follow a sinusoidal waveform with amplitude (A) and frequency (f) as 23
specified in Table 3.3.7-1. Three such signal frequencies are specified for this test, but intermediate ones can 24
be used for testing as well. 25
